1 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Hernandez v. State


No. 40, September Term, 1999


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


357 Md. 204; 742 A.2d 952; 1999 Md. LEXIS 814



December 21, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Montgomery County). Case Criminal No. 80696. D. Warren Donohue, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO REVERSE THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR MONTGOMERY COUNTY AND TO REMAND THIS CAUSE TO THAT COURT FOR A NEW TRIAL. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY MONTGOMERY COUNTY, MARYLAND.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed from Court of Special Appeals' (Maryland) decision upholding petitioner's convictions for child abuse and second degree rape.


OVERVIEW: At trial, Spanish speaking defendant requested a voir dire question regarding race-based bias. The court refused to propound the question. Following affirmance of his child abuse and second degree rape convictions, defendant appealed; the court reversed and ordered a new trial. The court held that defendant had options concerning voir dire questions directed to race, ethnicity, and cultural heritage. Regarding race, defendant could request racial bias questions not identifying his race or those which identified his race. Regarding ethnicity or cultural heritage, defendant must identify and include himself in a particular cognizable group to pose questions relating to such. The trial court was not obliged to assign defendant's race, ethnicity, or cultural heritage. When defendant self-identified a race, ethnicity, or cultural heritage, the trial court should make this fact clear to the venire, and, if requested, voir dire questions directed to such bias was required to be propound.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the convictions and ordered a new trial because petitioner, who through an interpreter testified in Spanish, was prejudiced because the trial court refused to propound his requested voir dire question regarding race-based bias.

 

2 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kanaras


No. 58, September Term, 1998


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


357 Md. 170; 742 A.2d 508; 1999 Md. LEXIS 812



December 20, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Kent County). J. Frederick Price, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED, AND CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO AFFIRM THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR KENT COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court issued writ of certiorari to Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) to resolve, among other issues, question of whether Post Conviction Procedure Act, Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 645A, precluded appeal from final circuit court order ruling upon a motion to correct allegedly illegal sentence.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner had been sentenced to life imprisonment, although there had been the possibility of parole due to petitioner's cooperation in the trial of an accomplice. Subsequently, the Governor issued guidelines which, in effect, denied petitioner parole. Petitioner sought relief under the Maryland Post Conviction Procedure Act, Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 645-A (1957, 1996 Repl. Vol.), and under Md. R. Crim. Causes 4-345(a). The circuit court denied his petitions. The Court of Special Appeals held that the Circuit Court's ruling under Rule 4-345(a) was appealable and that petitioner's sentence had become illegal. The court affirmed the ruling as to petitioner's right to appeal, but still reversed the judgment, holding that petitioner's sentence was not illegal; as the sentence was legal when imposed and continually remained legal, a motion under Rule 4-345(a) to correct an illegal sentence was not an appropriate action.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and case remanded with directions to affirm the judgment of the circuit court. Although intermediate court was correct in holding that circuit court's order upon a motion to correct allegedly illegal sentence was appealable, intermediate court was incorrect in holding that petitioner's sentence was illegal.

 

3 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Comptroller of the Treasury v. Gannett Co.


No. 49, September Term, 1999


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


356 Md. 699; 741 A.2d 1130; 1999 Md. LEXIS 803



December 9, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. DeLawrence Beard, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR MONTGOMERY COUNTY AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant comptroller of the treasury appealed the ruling of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland) that appellant lacked the authority to assess additional income tax against appellee corporation, by imputing interest income from certain intercompany debt not reported on appellee's federal income tax returns.


OVERVIEW: Appellee corporation was the parent company to many wholly-owned subsidiary companies. Appellee maintained four centralized, intercompany accounts with its subsidiaries. The subsidiaries deposited their proceeds in the appropriate account and then drew on that account to pay their related individual expenses. If a subsidiary deposited more proceeds than it withdrew, appellee maintained an interest-free debit with the subsidiary. If the subsidiary spent more money than it deposited, appellee maintained an interest-free credit with the subsidiary. For the tax years 1990-92, appellee maintained with its subsidiaries a credit in three of the four intercompany accounts. Appellant claimed that, under I.R.C. §§ 482, 7872 (1999), it could assess income tax against these credits by imputing interest income from them. The court held that because income-determining statutes must be construed against the government, the appellant did not have the power to allocate income under I.R.C. § 482 as the IRS does.


OUTCOME: Decision affirmed; appellee's modified federal taxable income as reported on its consolidated tax returns did not reflect any income derived from I.R.C. §§ 482 and 7872. Appellant could only allocate appellee's portion of that consolidated income based on the remaining applicable state code provisions pertaining to apportionment and modification.

 

4 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


McNeil v. State


No. 131, September Term, 1998


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


356 Md. 396; 739 A.2d 80; 1999 Md. LEXIS 649



October 19, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County), Case No. K-97-56. Eugene M. Lerner, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; APPELLANT TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed conviction of various sexual offenses and denial of his motion to suppress evidence in the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland) arguing that solicitation of a prostitute by a potential customer was not a crime under Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 15(e).


OVERVIEW: The evidence at trial indicated that defendant forced the victim into his car at the point of a knife, drove her into the woods against her will, and raped her. Defendant subsequently attempted to engage an undercover police officer, posing as a prostitute in a sting operation, in certain sexual activity. Evidence obtained as a result of his arrest for that endeavor incriminated him in the rape prosecution. Defendant moved to suppress the evidence obtained after his arrest, arguing that being a prospective customer of a prostitute did not constitute a crime under Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 15(e). The motion was denied and defendant appealed rape conviction. The court held that the crime of soliciting for prostitution stated in Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 15(e) covered the conduct both of the prostitute in soliciting potential customers and of the potential customer in soliciting the prostitute.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; court held that the crime of soliciting for prostitution covered the conduct of defendant potential customer in soliciting the prostitute, who was actually an undercover police officer. Defendant's arrest was thus based upon probable cause.

Mike Smith Pontiac, Inc. v. Mercedes-Benz, Inc.


No. 156, September Term, 1998


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


356 Md. 542; 741 A.2d 462; 1999 Md. LEXIS 593



October 15, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Harford County). Case # CJ 7975-12-438. William O. Carr, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY THE PETITIONER, MIKE SMITH PONTIAC, GMC, INC.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed petition for writ of certiorari to Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which held that satisfaction of Florida judgment also satisfied judgment in Maryland under Uniform Enforcement of Foreign Judgments Act, Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. §§ 11-801 to -807 (1998 Repl. Vol.).


OVERVIEW: A federal court in Florida entered a judgment in favor of petitioner, auto dealer and judgment creditor, against respondent, auto dealer and judgment debtor. Petitioner filed the federal judgment in a Maryland court, pursuant to the Uniform Enforcement of Foreign Judgments Act, Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. §§ 11-801 to -807 (1998 Repl. Vol.). The Florida judgment was satisfied by payment, including post-judgment interest at the nationwide federal rate, and the satisfaction was filed in Florida. Petitioner sought payment of the interest at Maryland's higher statutory post-judgment interest rate. The court held that the Maryland domesticated judgment was subject to the post-judgment defense of satisfaction and therefore was satisfied and discharged by payment in full of the Florida judgment, without regard to Maryland's higher post-judgment interest rate.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed, because the Maryland domesticated judgment was subject to the post-judgment defense of satisfaction and therefore was satisfied and discharged by payment in full of the Florida judgment, notwithstanding Maryland's higher post-judgment interest rate.

 

6 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Motor Vehicle Admn. v. Richards


No. 2, September Term, 1999


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


356 Md. 356; 739 A.2d 58; 1999 Md. LEXIS 595



October 14, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Circuit Court for Carroll County. Case No. C-98-26541. Francis M. Arnold, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR CARROLL COUNTY REVERSED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO AFFIRM THE RULING OF THE ADMINISTRATIVE LAW JUDGE PRESIDING OVER RESPONDENT'S LICENSE SUSPENSION HEARING. COSTS TO BE PAID BY RESPONDENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Carroll County (Maryland) reversing the decision of an Administrative Law Judge suspending respondent's driver's license for refusing to take a chemical breath test.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner motor vehicle administration petitioned for review of the lower court's decision overturning an administrative law judge's (ALJ) suspension of respondent's driver's license for failure to take a chemical breath test, pursuant to Md. Code Ann., Transp. § 16-205.1. Respondent's position was that the statute violated U.S. Const. amend. IV and the evidence of respondent's refusal to take the breath test should have been excluded from the proceeding. The court held that an administrative proceeding to revoke a driver's license was a civil proceeding, not a criminal proceeding. Therefore, the exclusionary rule did not apply because the exclusionary rule was a deterrent rule and its deterrent value would be minimal in proceedings with an administrative agency unrelated to the police department.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court and reinstated the decision of the administrative law judge because the Fourth Amendment exclusionary rule did not apply in non-criminal administrative proceedings.

State v. Bolden


No. 151, September Term, 1998


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


356 Md. 160; 737 A.2d 1086; 1999 Md. LEXIS 577



September 23, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Caroline County). J. Owen Wise, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED; CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT FOR CONSIDERATION OF THE OTHER QUESTIONS PRESENTED BY BOLDEN WHICH WERE NOT ANSWERED. COSTS TO ABIDE THE FINAL RESULT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Prosecution appealed the judgment of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which held that defendant's drug sales sentences constituted cruel and unusual punishment in violation of U.S. Const. amend. VIII, and Md. Declaration of Rights art. 25. Defendant filed a cross-petition for a writ of certiorari.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to 25 years' imprisonment for one sale of cocaine, 32 years' imprisonment for two sales of cocaine which took place on the same day, and 40 years' imprisonment for another offense. The Court of Special Appeals vacated his 40-year sentence and held that the consecutive sentences constituted cruel and unusual punishment in violation of U.S. Const. amend. VIII, and Md. Declaration of Rights art. 25. The prosecution did not challenge the ruling vacating the 40-year sentence but appealed the court's decision as to the constitutional issue. Defendant filed a cross-petition for a writ of certiorari. The court found the consecutive sentences were not grossly disproportionate in length to the crimes being punished, based on the seriousness of the conduct involved, the seriousness of relevant past conduct, articulated purposes supporting the sentence, and the importance of deferring to the legislature and to the sentencing court.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed because defendant's sentences were not grossly disproportionate in length to the crimes being punished; case remanded for consideration other questions presented by defendant which were not answered.

White v. North


No. 85, September Term, 1998


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


356 Md. 31; 736 A.2d 1072; 1999 Md. LEXIS 507



September 14, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County). Case # C-9633900 AA. Robert H. Heller, Jr., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS VACATED; CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO VACATE THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY AND REMAND THE CASE TO THE CIRCUIT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO VACATE THE DECISION OF THE BOARD OF APPEALS OF ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY AND REMAND THE CASE TO THE BOARD OF APPEALS FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION AND BELVOIR FARMS HOMEOWNER'S ASS'N, INC. V. NORTH, 355 MD. 259, 734 A.2D 227 (1999); COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY RESPONDENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On writ of certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), petitioners sought review of decision which affirmed reversal of a decision granting their request for a zoning variance to construct an in-ground concrete swimming pool in the sloped back yard of their home.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners sought review of decision which reversed the zoning board's grant of petitioners' request for a zoning variance to construct an in-ground concrete swimming pool in the sloped backyard of their home which was located within the county's critical area. The lower court affirmed the reversal on the ground that "unwarranted hardship," as used in Anne Arundel County Code, art. 3, § 2-107(b) (1996), required a property owner to be deprived of all reasonable use of their property before a variance could be granted. The court held that the correct standard to use in evaluating the requirement of unwarranted hardship was whether the denial of the petitioners' request to build a swimming pool was a denial of a reasonable and significant use. The court remanded the case to the zoning board for reconsideration of their application.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirming reversal of grant of zoning variance vacated; the correct standard to use in evaluating the requirement of unwarranted hardship was whether the denial of the petitioners' request to build a swimming pool was a denial of a reasonable and significant use.

 

9 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Winkler Constr. Co. v. Jerome


No. 157, September Term, 1998


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


355 Md. 231; 734 A.2d 212; 1999 Md. LEXIS 466



August 2, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Carroll County). Case No. C-97-25067. Raymond E. Beck, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED; CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO AFFIRM JUDGMENT OF CIRCUIT COURT FOR CARROLL COUNTY; COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY RESPONDENTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff subcontractor sought review of a decision by the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) invalidating plaintiff's mechanic's lien on residential property for failure to plead facts showing that the owner had not made full payment to the prime contractor at the time the notice of lien was given as well as the amount of the owner's indebtedness, as set forth in Md. Code Ann., Real Prop. § 104(a)(2) and (f)(3).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff subcontractor challenged the court of appeals' decision that plaintiff's mechanic's lien on defendant's residential home was invalid for failing to meet the procedural prerequisites of Md. Code Ann., Real Prop. § 104(a)(2) and (f)(3). Upon further appeal, the court held that the appellate court erred in finding the complaint was deficient for failing to plead facts demonstrating that defendant owner had not made full payment to the prime contractor at the time plaintiff gave its notice of lien or that the lien did not exceed the amount of defendant's indebtedness. Neither of those facts could reasonably be expected to be within plaintiff's knowledge; therefore, plaintiff, as claimant, was not required to aver either in the complaint. A statutory presumption existed that the materials supplied by plaintiff were received by defendant and that the lien was valid, unless defendant presented rebuttal evidence, which did not occur in this case. The court reversed, reinstating the circuit court's decision that plaintiff's mechanics' lien was valid.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision holding that plaintiff's mechanic's lien complaint was deficient because it failed to plead statutory prerequisites relating to defendant property owner's indebtedness to the prime contractor at the time plaintiff gave its notice of lien. Because the complaint adequately pleaded that plaintiff delivered the materials to defendant, a rebuttable statutory presumption as to the validity of the lien arose.

Belvoir Farms Homeowners Ass'n v. North


No. 159, September Term, 1998


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


355 Md. 259; 734 A.2d 227; 1999 Md. LEXIS 467



August 2, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Case # C-1997-42848 AA. Joseph P. Manck, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY VACATED; CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO VACATE THE DECISION OF THE ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY BOARD OF APPEALS AND TO REMAND THE CASE TO THE BOARD OF APPEALS FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION; COSTS TO BE PAID BY RESPONDENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland) denying defendants a use variance to build additional boat slips on a protected creek under zoning regulations promulgated in the Anne Arundel County, Md., Zoning Code art. 3, § 2-107 (b), governing development in the Chesapeake Bay Critical Area.


OVERVIEW: Defendants challenged the trial court's decision denying them a variance to build additional boats slips in a residential development in the Chesapeake Bay Critical Area pursuant to restrictions imposed by the Anne Arundel County, Md., Zoning Code art. 3, § 2-107 (b). On appeal, the court held that the Anne Arundel County Board of Zoning Appeals (BZA), which had granted the variance, had erroneously applied the wrong standard in reaching its decision. Under the Anne Arundel County, Md., Zoning Code art. 3, § 2-107 (b), the "unwarranted hardship" standard rather than the "practical difficulties" standard should have been applied. Because the court lacked the authority to grant or deny a variance or substitute its judgment for that of the administrative body, the court remanded the case to the BZA for reconsideration and for application of the correct standard.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the decision of the circuit court denying defendants a use variance and remanded the issue of whether to grant the variance, which would permit additional boat slips on a protected creek, to the county board of zoning appeals, because the board had erred in applying the "practical difficulties" rather than the "unwarranted hardship" standard when it granted the variance upon initial review.

 

11 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Chevy Chase Land Co. v. United States


Misc. No. 24, September Term, 1998


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


355 Md. 110; 733 A.2d 1055; 1999 Md. LEXIS 462



July 29, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the U.S. Court of Federal Claims in 92-CV-248 (United States Court of Appeals for the Federal Circuit). James F. Merow, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CERTIFIED QUESTIONS ANSWERED AS HEREIN SET FORTH. COSTS IN THIS COURT TO BE EVENLY DIVIDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The United States Court of Appeals for the Federal Circuit certified three state law questions in a suit alleging an illegal taking of land under the Rails-to-Trails Act, 16 U.S.C.S. § 1247(d) (1983), asking (1) whether a deed conveying a railroad right-of-way conveyed an easement or fee simple; (2) if an easement, whether it was subject to any state law limitations; and (3) whether the easement was abandoned as a matter of law, and if so, when.


OVERVIEW: Three questions were certified for decision under Maryland law by the United States Court of Appeals for the Federal Circuit in a suit brought under the takings clause of U.S. Const. amend. V: (1) whether a deed conveying a railroad right-of-way conveyed an easement or a fee simple; (2) if an easement, whether the conveyance was subject to any state law limitations on the use of the right-of-way; and (3) whether, as a matter of law, the railroad abandoned its easement prior to conveying it to defendants Montgomery County, Maryland, and the United States for interim use as a public recreational path under the Rails-to-Trails Act (the Act), 16 U.S.C.S. § 1247(d) (1983). The state court of appeals answered all three questions in favor of defendants. By use of the language "right of way," the deed conveyed a perpetual easement to the railroad. Use of the railway for recreational trails fell within the easement's intended purpose of transportation. The railroad did not abandon its easement by complying with the procedural requirements of the Act, because the Act expressly preserved a reversionary interest in favor of the railroad for future transportation purposes.


OUTCOME: The state court answered all three questions certified by the federal court of appeals in favor of the county and federal government defendants, holding that (1) a deed conveying a right-of-way to a railroad conveyed a perpetual easement; (2) the easement was not subject to any state law limitations as long as it was used for transportation purposes; and (3) the railroad did not abandon the easement by complying with the Rails-to-Trails Act.

 

12 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Spring v. Bradley


No. 121, September Term, 1998


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


355 Md. 79; 733 A.2d 1038; 1999 Md. LEXIS 458



July 28, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Talbot County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Case No. 20-C-97-003183 OC. William S. Horne, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED, WITH COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant land owner sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Talbot County (Maryland) that denied appellant's request for mandamus, injunctive, and declaratory relief in an action to compel municipal water and sewer service.


OVERVIEW: Appellant owned a 13.26 acre undeveloped tract of land directly bordering appellee town. Appellee provided water sewer service to another property, before it was ultimately annexed to appellee, near appellant's property. Appellant and appellee could not reach an agreement about annexation. Appellant sought mandamus, injunctive, and declaratory relief in the lower court seeking to compel appellee to provide water and sewer service to his property. Appellant contended that appellee had provided service to at least three other properties lying outside the town limits. The lower court denied appellant's requests. The court affirmed on appeal, holding that appellee did not conduct itself as a public service company through its limited and special extensions of service. The court held that a municipality could not be compelled to supply water to anyone outside its limits absent a special contract or a position as a public utility.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of appellant's request for injunctive and declaratory relief because a municipality could not be compelled to supply water to anyone outside its limits absent a special contract or a position as a public utility. The court found that appellee town did not conduct itself as a public service company.

 

13 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Conyers v. State


No. 27, September Term, 1998


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


354 Md. 132; 729 A.2d 910; 1999 Md. LEXIS 253



May 17, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied October 4, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 6379.



DISPOSITION: Review of Death Penalty (Circuit Court for Wicomico County). D. William Simpson, JUDGE. JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Circuit Court for Wicomico County (Maryland), entering his convictions for premeditated murder, felony murder, first-degree burglary, robbery, and use of a handgun in the commission of a crime of violence. Defendant claimed the trial court committed reversible error in restricting direct exam of defense witnesses, giving improper jury instructions, and in admitting or failing to admit evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's convictions for premeditated murder and robbery, among others, were affirmed where defendant's appellate claims were not preserved for review, and the trial court properly denied defendant's motion in limine and admitted photographs of the victim and the crime scene. The court denied defendant's motion in limine to allow the testimony of a law professor regarding mitigating circumstances for sentencing. Defendant was convicted and appealed. Defendant claimed the testimony should have been admitted where it may have given a juror a reason to impose a sentence less than death and that crime scene photographs were improperly admitted where they were irrelevant and prejudicial. The reviewing court affirmed the lower court's decision, finding the majority of defendant's claims were unpreserved for appellate review. The trial court properly refused admission of the professor's testimony where the testimony was of no aid to a jury because it was irrelevant to defendant's character and background or the circumstances of the crime. Photographs of the crime scene and the victim were properly admitted to assist the jury in visualizing the atrociousness of the crime.


OUTCOME: The reviewing court affirmed defendant's convictions for premeditated murder and robbery, among others, where defendant failed to preserve the majority of his appellate issues for appellate review. The trial court properly denied admission of a law professor's testimony regarding mitigation was irrelevant and of no aid to a jury. Crime scene and victim photographs showed the atrociousness of the crime and were properly admitted.

 

14 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Read v. Supervisor of Assessments


No. 148, September Term, 1998


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


354 Md. 383; 731 A.2d 868; 1999 Md. LEXIS 248



May 13, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Michael E. Loney, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The matter came before the court on appeal from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland), pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Appellant had unsuccessfully contested the imposition of rollback taxes with respect to appellant's withdrawal and conveyance of property subject to a Forest Conservation and Management Agreement.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed a judgment upholding the imposition of rollback taxes with respect to appellant's withdrawal and conveyance of property subject to a Forest Conservation and Management Agreement (FCMA). After contracts for the sale of two FCMA lots were finalized but before the lots were conveyed to the new owners without the FCMA obligations, appellant requested the Maryland Department of Natural Resources to withdraw the lots from the FCMA in order to avoid the imposition of a rollback tax. The court held that the intent of the original Conservation of Woodland Areas Act, in effect when appellant entered into his initial FCMA and during subsequent renewals, was to impose a rollback tax for property withdrawn for the purpose of conveyance, even if that conveyance was effected after the property technically was withdrawn. Under the interdependence and end result tests used in applying the step transaction doctrine, the transactions conducted by appellant were required to be stepped together and substantively considered one transaction: a withdrawal for the purposes of sale and conveyance. Accordingly, the rollback taxes were properly imposed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment upholding the imposition of rollback taxes with respect to appellant's withdrawal and conveyance of property subject to a Forest Conservation and Management Agreement because, under the step transaction doctrine, the transactions conducted by appellant were required to be stepped together and substantively considered one transaction: a withdrawal for the purposes of sale and conveyance.

 

15 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Robinson v. State


No. 74, September Term, 1998


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


353 Md. 683; 728 A.2d 698; 1999 Md. LEXIS 183



April 28, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Prince George's County), Richard J. Sothoron, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO REVERSE THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR PRINCE GEORGE'S COUNTY AND TO REMAND THE CASE FOR NEW TRIAL. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY PRINCE GEORGE'S COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Certiorari was granted to the Court of Special Appeals, the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), which affirmed petitioner's conviction for common law assault and battery after the effective date of the statutory assault provisions of 1996 Md. Laws 632.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted of common law assault and battery after the passage of 1996 Md. Laws 632. Petitioner, on certiorari review, argued that the statutory enactment abolished the common law crimes of assault and battery. While statutes were not presumed to repeal the common law further than required, where a statute dealt with an entire subject matter, the statute was generally construed as abrogating the common law as to that subject. 1996 Md. Laws 632 created degrees of assault unknown to the common law and repealed aggravated assaults. Under the previous statutory scheme, those assaults that fell outside the statute could still be prosecuted under the common law. Since enactment, all assaults fit within the statute, and the common law offenses were thus abrogated. Because the time frame during which the crime for which petitioner was convicted had commenced prior to enactment, the subject matter jurisdiction of the court was not defeated. Rather, the conviction was reversed based on the trial court's error in allowing the jury to speculate as to whether or not petitioner's conduct occurred prior to the date of enactment.


OUTCOME: Petitioner's conviction was reversed because, although the common law offenses of assault and battery existed during part of the time frame when the conduct for which petitioner was convicted occurred, allowing the jury to speculate as to whether petitioner's conduct actually occurred in that period was error.

 

16 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Luskin's, Inc. v. Consumer Protection Div.


No. 64, September Term, 1998


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


353 Md. 335; 726 A.2d 702; 1999 Md. LEXIS 112



March 22, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected May 13, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Circuit Court for Harford County. Case # 12-C-93-003080 AA. Cypert O. Whitfill, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART. CASE REMANDED TO THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS FOR THE ENTRY OF A JUDGMENT VACATING THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR HARFORD COUNTY AND REMANDING THIS ACTION TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR HARFORD COUNTY WITH DIRECTIONS TO VACATE THE ORDER OF THE CONSUMER PROTECTION DIVISION AND TO REMAND THIS ACTION TO THE CONSUMER PROTECTION DIVISION FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID ONE-HALF BY LUSKIN'S, INC. AND ONE-HALF BY THE CONSUMER PROTECTION DIVISION.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner retailer petitioned for a writ of certiorari in an enforcement action brought by respondent agency under the Maryland Consumer Protection Act, Md. Code Ann. Com. Law Art. §§ 13-101 through 13-501, after the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) reversed the decision of the lower court, raising multiple issues, principally, what was the standard for determining deceptive advertising, particularly advertising that something was "free."


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was a retailer of electronic and household goods and services. Respondent agency was the consumer protection division. Respondent brought an enforcement action under the Maryland Consumer Protection Act (the Act), Md. Code Ann. Com. Law Art. §§ 13-101 through 13-501. Petitioner advertised and conducted a conditional gift promotional program that respondent found deceptive. The circuit court reversed that decision, which the court of special appeals then reversed. Petitioner filed a petition for a writ of certiorari, which was granted. Principal among the multiple issues raised was the standard for determining deceptive advertising, particularly advertising that something was "free." The parties argued over whether an ad was adjudged deceptive by a reasonable person standard or by an "unsophisticated" person standard. Semantics accounted for a large part of the gulf between the parties' positions. Upon review of the evolving approach by the Federal Trade Commission (FTC) to determinations of what was deceptive, the appellate court found that the standard in Cliffdale Associates and others was the standard for determining deception. Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


OUTCOME: The appellate court granted petitioner retailer's petition for a writ of certiorari. The appellate court affirmed in part and reversed in part the judgment that reversed the decision of the lower court that was in favor of petitioner. The matter was remanded with instructions. Petitioner and respondent agency were each to pay one-half of the costs. The standard applied in Cliffdale Associates was the standard for determining deception.

One 1995 Corvette v. Mayor & City Council of Baltimore


No. 63, September Term, 1998


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


353 Md. 114; 724 A.2d 680; 1999 Md. LEXIS 58



February 23, 1999, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED AND CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO AFFIRM THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY; COSTS IN THIS COURT AND THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY RESPONDENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of a decision of the Court of Special Appeals of Maryland that reversed a trial court decision suppressing evidence in a civil forfeiture case brought by respondent city pursuant to Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 297(b)(2) and (4). Petitioner alleged violations of the exclusionary rule under U.S. Const. amend. IV.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was stopped due to suspected drug activity observed by police during routine surveillance. After drugs were found in petitioner's automobile, the police seized the car. Although the drug charges were dropped, respondent city filed a forfeiture action pursuant to Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 297(b)(2) and (4). On petitioner's motion, the trial court dismissed the case, ruling that the evidence of drugs necessary to prove respondent's case had been obtained in violation of U.S. Const. amend. IV and was suppressed from the forfeiture proceeding under the exclusionary rule. On appeal, respondent argued that the exclusionary rule did not apply to forfeiture proceedings under Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 297. The intermediate court reversed the trial court ruling. On petitioner's appeal, the appellate court reversed held that the intermediate court erred in reversing the trial court decision. The court held that the exclusionary rule applied to civil in rem forfeiture actions in Maryland for alleged drug activity under § 297 because such proceedings were quasi-criminal in nature.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the intermediate court and held that the intermediate court erred in reversing the trial court decision that suppressed evidence in a civil forfeiture case. The court held that the exclusionary rule applied to civil in rem forfeiture actions for alleged drug activity.

In re Adoption No. 12612


No. 83, September Term, 1998


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


353 Md. 209; 725 A.2d 1037; 1999 Md. LEXIS 51



February 17, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended February 26, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Montgomery County). Michael D. Mason, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED; CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO REVERSE JUDGMENT OF CIRCUIT COURT FOR MONTGOMERY COUNTY AND REMAND TO THAT COURT FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS IN CONFORMANCE WITH THIS OPINION; COSTS IN THIS COURT AND COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY RESPONDENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In her attempt to adopt a minor child, petitioner appealed a decision of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland) that granted custody of the child to his mother. Petitioner claimed that the court erred because it did not, as required, determine whether there was a likelihood that mother would abuse child, and the court's determination that mother posed no threat of death or fatal abuse to child did not meet the requirement.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner, who took care of a minor child while his mother was incarcerated for committing credit card fraud while on probation for murdering one of her other children, filed to adopt the child and terminate mother's parental rights. The circuit court awarded custody to mother, holding that petitioner failed to meet her burden of proving that it was in the child's best interests to terminate mother's parental rights. Petitioner appealed, claiming that the circuit court was required to determine whether there was a likelihood that mother would abuse child. Petitioner claimed that the circuit court's determination that mother posed no threat of death or fatal abuse to the child did not meet that requirement. The appellate court reversed. It explained that under Md. Code Ann., Fam. Law § 9-101, in custody disputes the circuit court was required to determine whether there was a likelihood that the person whose custody was challenged would abuse the child. The circuit court made no such determination regarding mother. The circuit court did not comply with § 9-101, so the appellate court remanded the case for further proceedings to determine whether mother was likely to abuse child.


OUTCOME: In petitioner's attempt to adopt a minor child and terminate his mother's parental rights, the appellate court reversed the circuit court's decision to grant custody to mother. The appellate court remanded the case for further proceedings, explaining that the circuit court did not comply with the statutory requirement that it determine whether there was a likelihood that mother would abuse child.

Owens v. State


No. 129, September Term, 1997


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


352 Md. 663; 724 A.2d 43; 1999 Md. LEXIS 38



February 12, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Case # 97 CR 2003. Robert E. Cadigan, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: IN THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE COUNTY AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision of the Circuit Court for Baltimore County that convicted him of statutory rape in violation of Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 463(a)(3) (1957 & 1996 Repl. Vol.) after he had sexual relations with a girl under age 14. Appellant claimed that his right to due process was violated because the trial court prevented him from presenting his defense that he reasonably believed the victim was above 13 years of age.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of statutory rape under Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 463(a)(3) (1957 & 1996 Repl. Vol.) after he had sexual relations with a girl under age 14. Appellant challenged his conviction, claiming that his right to due process was violated because the trial court prevented him from presenting his defense that he reasonably believed the victim was above 13 years of age. The appellate court affirmed appellant's conviction, holding that appellant's due process rights were not violated. Due process required that persons of ordinary intelligence and experience have a reasonable opportunity to know what actions were prohibited so that they could conform their conduct according to the law. Section 463(a)(3) clearly prohibited sexual intercourse with a child under age 14, informing appellant of the prohibited conduct and putting him on notice of the potential risks of miscalculating the victim's age. Additionally, § 463(a)(3) made no provision for a mistake-of-age defense. The legislature's decision not to allow a mistake-of-age defense furthered the state's interest in protecting children from sexual abuse, so appellant's rights were not violated.


OUTCOME: Appellate court affirmed trial court's decision to convict appellant of statutory rape without letting him present a defense that he believed the victim was of age. Appellate court explained that appellant's due process rights were not violated because the rape statute clearly described the prohibited behavior, and the legislature's refusal to allow a mistake-of-age defense furthered the state's interest in protecting children from sexual abuse.

Wiggins v. State


No. 121, September Term, 1997


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


352 Md. 580; 724 A.2d 1; 1999 Md. LEXIS 36



February 10, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied October 4, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 5220.


PRIOR HISTORY: Review of Death Penalty - Circuit Court for Baltimore County. No. 88CR5464. John F. Fader, II, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: ORDER DENYING PETITION FOR POST CONVICTION RELIEF AFFIRMED, WITH COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the denial of post conviction relief under Md. Code Ann. art. 27, § 645A, for a death sentence imposed pursuant to a first degree murder conviction in the Circuit Court of Baltimore County (Maryland).


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of denial of post conviction relief under Md. Code Ann. art. 27, § 645A, in connection with an imposed death sentence for murder. Appellant claimed he was denied effective assistance of counsel through his attorney's failure to elicit evidence from a coroner about time of death and failure to present mitigating evidence of a dysfunctional childhood. The court noted evidence of appellant's guilt was almost entirely circumstantial, without an eyewitness or physical evidence to directly connect him to the murder itself. The court rejected appellant's argument that counsel's failure to impeach the coroner about a prior inconsistent statement fell below objectively reasonable representation. The court found no constitutional deficiency when the testimony estimating time of death at least two hours after appellant had possession of the victim's car was more exculpatory than inculpatory. The court noted that at that time state law allowed prior inconsistent statements only to impeach credibility not as substantive evidence. Court found counsel's presentation of mitigating evidence was based upon a presumed sound tactical decision to concentrate efforts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of appellant's motion for post conviction relief for a murder conviction, in appellee prosecution's favor, because appellant failed to establish he was denied effective assistance of counsel when attorney's failure to elicit testimony about coroner's alleged prior inconsistent statement about time of death was based on a then in place evidence rule and such trial testimony was more exculpatory than inculpatory.

State v. Evans


No. 28, September Term, 1997, No. 32, September Term, 1997


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


352 Md. 496; 723 A.2d 423; 1999 Md. LEXIS 32



January 26, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied October 4, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 5232 and 1999 U.S. LEXIS 5231.
Writ of certiorari denied Evans v. Maryland, 528 U.S. 833, 145 L. Ed. 2d 77, 120 S. Ct. 310, 1999 U.S. LEXIS 5232 (1999)
Writ of certiorari denied Sykes-Bey v. Maryland, 528 U.S. 833, 145 L. Ed. 2d 77, 120 S. Ct. 91, 1999 U.S. LEXIS 5231 (1999)
Post-conviction proceeding at Evans v. State, 2003 Md. App. LEXIS 73 (Md. Ct. Spec. App., June 25, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Baltimore City). Case Nos. 194186071 and 194073090. John Prevas, JUDGE.
Evans v. State, 113 Md. App. 347, 688 A.2d 28, 1997 Md. App. LEXIS 4 (1997)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED. CASE OF RESPONDENT EVANS REMANDED TO THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS WITH DIRECTIONS TO AFFIRM THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY; COSTS IN THIS COURT AND THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY RESPONDENT EVANS. CASE OF RESPONDENT SYKES-BEY REMANDED TO THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS FOR CONSIDERATION OF THE ISSUE OF PROBABLE CAUSE; COSTS IN THIS COURT TO BE PAID BY RESPONDENT SYKES-BEY AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO ABIDE BY THAT RESULT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, the state of Maryland, sought review of the judgment of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which reversed two respondents' convictions for violating Maryland's controlled dangerous substance laws, because it found that the evidence against them, discovered during searches of their persons, should have been suppressed because their initial detentions did not constitute valid arrests.


OVERVIEW: In two consolidated cases, respondents were physically detained by the police on the basis of probable cause to believe that each had participated in an illegal drug transaction. In both instances, the police searched respondents while they were detained and released them with the intention of later charging them with violation of the controlled dangerous substance laws of Maryland. The court below, in each of the respondent's respective cases, reversed respondents' convictions after it found that the initial detentions of respondents were not arrests, that the full search conducted by the police incident to those detentions were therefore unconstitutional, and, consequently, that the trial court had erred in denying appellants' motions to suppress. The judgments of the court below were reversed on appeal. The initial detentions of respondents were found to have been valid arrests. The court held that the failure of the police to subject appellants to the formal criminal charging process at the time of their valid arrests under Maryland law did not offend the U.S. Constitution. Consequently, the searches, as incident to lawful arrests, were proper.


OUTCOME: The reversal of respondents' convictions for violations of Maryland's controlled dangerous substance laws, which was based on the lower court's determinations that the evidence against them should have been suppressed, was reversed. The court found that the failure of police to subject respondents to the formal criminal charging process at the time of their valid arrests did not negate the validity of the arrests or the incident searches.

Degren v. State


No. 54, September Term, 1998


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


352 Md. 400; 722 A.2d 887; 1999 Md. LEXIS 3



January 14, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Charles County). Case # CR97-80. Robert C. Nalley, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of the judgment of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which affirmed her conviction for child abuse in violation of Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 35C. Petitioner, who had been convicted for failing to prevent the rape of a 12 year-old girl, that took place in her presence, argued that her omission or failure to prevent another person's act was not punishable under the language of the statute.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was found guilty of child abuse in violation of Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 35C for her failure to prevent the sexual molestation or exploitation of a 12 year-old girl. The facts adduced at trial showed that petitioner had sat on the edge of a bed and watched the 12 year-old victim being raped by petitioner's husband and a family friend. The evidence further showed that petitioner failed to intervene. Petitioner's conviction was affirmed by the court below. The judgment of the court below was affirmed on appeal because the court found that the definition of sexual abuse in Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 35C contemplated not just an affirmative act in directly molesting or exploiting a child, but also one's omission or failure to act to prevent molestation or exploitation when it is reasonably possible to act. In addition, the trial judge was not found to have erred in allowing the prosecutor to tell the jury in closing argument that nobody had more of a reason to lie than petitioner because the comment was made in response to an attack on the credibility of witnesses first raised by the defense counsel in his closing argument. Moreover, the comment did not prejudice petitioner.


OUTCOME: The affirmance of petitioner's conviction for child abuse by the court below was affirmed on appeal. The court's judgment was based on its finding that Maryland's child abuse statute's definition of sexual abuse contemplated one's omission or failure to act to prevent another's affirmative act in directly molesting or exploiting a child when it was reasonably possible to do so.

Anne Arundel County v. City of Annapolis


No. 47, September Term, 1998


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


352 Md. 117; 721 A.2d 217; 1998 Md. LEXIS 945



December 10, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected December 30, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Case # C-9736303 OC. Eugene M. Lerner, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county and others sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland), which granted appellee city and other appellees' motion for summary judgment on the grounds that appellee city's annexation of certain lands did not create a prohibited enclave in violation of Md. Code Ann. art. 23A, § 19(a)(2) (1957).


OVERVIEW: The issue presented upon review was whether an annexation by appellee city, which left an area of appellant county separated from the rest of the county by waterways on three sides and appellee on the other, violated Md. Code. Ann. art. 23A, § 19(a)(2) (1957), because it created the type of enclave prohibited by that statute. The court held that the plain language of § 19(a)(2), and the legislature's intent in enacting the statute, prevented only an annexation by a municipality that would create an enclave of unincorporated land entirely surrounded by that municipality's borders. The statute did not prohibit annexation when areas left unincorporated would be separated from other unincorporated areas by natural features, i.e. physical geography alone. The court found that the separation of fast land areas by a body of water did not alter appellant's jurisdiction over all the lands, including the waterways, in question. Those segments of fast land and navigable water remain contiguous. Therefore, the court concluded that the annexation by appellee did not violate § 19(a)(2). Accordingly, the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment, which granted appellee city and other appellees' motion for summary judgment, was affirmed. Under the plain meaning of the statute in question, the annexation by appellee city did not create a prohibited enclave because it did not create an unincorporated area completely surrounded by appellee city.

Kirwan v. The Diamondback


No. 57, September Term, 1997


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


352 Md. 74; 721 A.2d 196; 1998 Md. LEXIS 943; 27 Media L. Rep. 1399



December 8, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected December 10, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. E. Allen Shepherd, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED, APPELLANTS TO PAY COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant University of Maryland appealed a decision from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), pursuant to a writ of certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals, which granted plaintiff newspaper's request for information pursuant to the Maryland Public Information Act, Md. Code Ann., State Gov't § 10-611 through § 10-628. Plaintiff filed a cross-appeal, challenging the denial of its request for attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: The lower court granted the request of plaintiff newspaper for information including records of campus parking violations committed by the men's basketball team and its head coach, pursuant to Md. Code Ann., State Gov't § 10-611 through § 10-628. Defendant University of Maryland appealed, contending that either the before-mentioned statute or 20 U.S.C.S. § 1232(g), authorized the nondisclosure of the information. Defendant claimed that any records concerning parking tickets received by the coach were exempt from disclosure under § 10-616(i) because they constituted personnel records. The court held that a parking ticket merely charged a very minor misdemeanor and was not a personnel record. Defendant further argued that the records regarding the students contained financial information and thus were exempt from disclosure under § 10-617(f). The court held that records of parking tickets were not records of indebtedness, and thus were not financial information. "Education records" within the meaning of 20 U.S.C.S. § 1232(g), did not include records of parking tickets or correspondence regarding a student-athlete accepting a loan to pay parking tickets. The court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision below granting plaintiff newspaper's request for information, on the grounds that none of the statutes asserted by defendant University of Maryland authorized the non-disclosure of the information. The court denied plaintiff's cross-appeal for attorney fees on the ground that while plaintiff substantially prevailed, defendant's position was not wholly unwarranted, thus the trial court did not abuse its discretion.

Secretary, Dep't of Pub. Safety & Correctional Servs. v. Henderson


No. 39, September Term, 1998


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


351 Md. 438; 718 A.2d 1150; 1998 Md. LEXIS 810



October 8, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore City pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED; APPELLANTS TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff prisoner filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus. The Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland) found that the prisoner was entitled to a writ of habeas corpus and ordered defendant state correctional officials to release the prisoner and to reinstate his mandatory supervision release. The state correctional officials appealed.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner was convicted of the offense of robbery with a deadly weapon. He was paroled and then convicted of the offense of possession with intent to distribute cocaine. His sentences were aggregated in accordance with Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 700 (1992). The prisoner's good conduct rates were based on that single term of confinement, and he was released under mandatory supervision on July 7, 1997. Based on case law, filed 20 months later, the correctional officials determined that the prisoner's sentences should not have been aggregated, and they recalculated his good time credits accordingly. The officials issued a retake warrant for the arrest of the prisoner as an escapee. The trial court granted the prisoner's petition for habeas corpus and ordered that the prisoner's mandatory supervision release be reinstated. The correctional officials appealed. The court held that (1) the correctional officials erred when they recalculated the prisoner's credits so as to deprive him of the liberty to which he was statutorily entitled, and (2) the prisoner's re-incarceration was unlawful because it was not authorized by statute, so he was entitled to release for that reason.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which granted the prisoner's petition for a writ of habeas corpus and which ordered the correctional officials to release the prisoner and reinstate his mandatory supervision release.

Giffin v. Crane


NO. 30, SEPTEMBER TERM, 1997


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


351 Md. 133; 716 A.2d 1029; 1998 Md. LEXIS 643

PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Montgomery County). L. Leonard Ruben, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS VACATED; CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO REVERSE THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR MONTGOMERY COUNTY. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY THE RESPONDENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent mother filed a petition for modification of custody and for child support. The trial court granted the petition and the Maryland Court of Special Appeals affirmed. Petitioner father sought review.


OVERVIEW: The father and the mother both filed complaints to obtain a divorce and both sought custody of their two minor children. The parties resolved the custody issue, agreeing that the father would have sole physical custody of both children. Following a review of the custody arrangement, as agreed upon by the parties, a doctor recommended that physical custody of the children be transferred to the mother. The father refused to accept the recommendation or relinquish the children. The mother thus filed a petition for modification. The court held (1) the trial court erred as a matter of law in ordering that custody of the children be transferred from the father to the mother because the trial court impermissibly relied on the mother's gender as the basis for its decision, (2) the trial court's reliance on the mother's gender as the basis for its decision violated the Maryland Equal Rights Amendment, Article 46 of the Maryland Declaration of Rights, and (3) the trial court's reliance on the mother's gender did not constitute harmless error.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the special appeals court and remanded the matter to the trial court for further proceedings.

State v. Wiegmann


No. 13, September Term, 1998


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


350 Md. 585; 714 A.2d 841; 1998 Md. LEXIS 581



August 4, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 13. SEPT. TERM, 1998 FILED August 4 1998 Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Howard County) Donna Hill Staton JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED; CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS THAT IT REMAND TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR HOWARD COUNTY FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION; PETITIONER TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: State of Maryland sought review of the judgment of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) which vacated defendant's conviction for battery, holding that his arrest was illegal because the master had no authority to order him to be taken into custody, after defendant resisted arrest during contempt proceedings for his failure to pay court-ordered child support.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appeared in court in contempt proceedings for failure to pay court-ordered child support before a master. The master found defendant in contempt and ordered him to be held in custody. Defendant physically resisted the attempt to take him into custody. He was convicted of battery by the trial court. An appellate court vacated his conviction, on the ground that the arrest was illegal because masters had no authority to order arrests. On review, the court affirmed, holding that masters had no express authority under Md. R. Fam. L. Actions 9-207 or Md. R. Civ. P., Cir. Ct. 2-541(c) or implicit authority to order arrests pending an entry of judicial order in accordance with their recommendation of contempt. The court further declined to abolish the common law rule that there was a right to resist an unlawful arrest, holding that such an action would be best left to the legislature and its primary power to declare the public policy of the state.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment against State of Maryland, vacating defendant's battery conviction, holding that masters had no authority to order an arrest pending an entry of judicial order in accordance with the master's recommendation of contempt, and declining to abolish the common law rule of the right to resist an unlawful arrest because such an action would be more properly left to the legislature.

Pinkney v. State


No. 88, September Term, 1997


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


350 Md. 201; 711 A.2d 205; 1998 Md. LEXIS 419



June 15, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore City pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Kathleen O'Ferrall Friedman, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED; CASE REMANDED TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY FOR A NEW TRIAL. COSTS TO BE PAID BY THE MAYOR AND CITY COUNCIL OF BALTIMORE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland), which convicted him, in absentia, of theft under Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 342 (1957, 1996 Repl. Vol., 1997 Supp.).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with theft. On the day of his trial, the trial court granted him a continuance to obtain counsel. On the continued trial date, defendant had again failed to retain counsel, so the trial court again continued the trial. At the third trial date, neither defendant nor an attorney appeared. The trial court tried and convicted defendant in absentia and, at sentencing, disregarded his explanation for failing to appear at trial, which was that he had a seizure. Defendant appealed. The court held that 1) a criminal defendant could be tried in absentia after waiving his right to be present at trial, 2) before trying a defendant in absentia, a trial court was required to find a knowing and voluntary waiver of the right to be present and to exercise sound discretion in determining whether to proceed with trial, 3) voluntary absence could not be presumed, and a waiver was required to be clearly established in the record, and 4) the trial court's inadequate inquiry into defendant's whereabouts on the morning of trial did not give it a sufficient basis to conclude that his absence was the product of voluntary choice.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for theft and remanded the case for a new trial.

Catonsville Nursing Home v. Loveman


No. 100, September Term, 1997


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


349 Md. 560; 709 A.2d 749; 1998 Md. LEXIS 314



May 15, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected June 6, 1998. As Corrected June 5, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Alfred L. Brennan, Sr., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE COUNTY REVERSED; CASE REMANDED TO THE CIRCUIT COURT WITH DIRECTION THAT IT AFFIRM THE DECISION OF THE COMMISSION; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLEE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant health resources planning commission (commission) held that appellant nursing home facility had the right to seek a certificate of need (CON) on behalf of the facility, instead of appellee landlord of the facility. The Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland) reversed the finding by the commission. The commission and the nursing home facility appealed from the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The commission and nursing home argued that the nursing home, as the lessee and operator of the nursing home facility, had the right to seek a (CON) for the facility. The commission and nursing home argued that the landlord of the nursing home had waived his exemption to apply for the CON and furthermore, did not have the right to apply for the facility's CON. The court held that the landlord had abandoned his right to an exemption for the CON requirement and reversed the finding of the trial court. The court held that the landlord's exemption as to the CON requirement for the existing nursing home facility was an incorporeal hereditament, which was personal, did not run with the land, and was subject to abandonment. When the landlord became unqualified to hold an operator's license by reason of criminal conviction for Medicaid fraud and acquiesced in the obtainment of a CON by subsequent operators, the landlord waived his right to an exemption.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the matter.

Roberts v. Total Health Care


No. 76, September Term, 1996


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


349 Md. 499; 709 A.2d 142; 1998 Md. LEXIS 313



May 14, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Baltimore City). Thomas Ward, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED. PETITIONERS TO PAY COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, Medicaid recipient, challenged the decision of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which held that plaintiff, health maintenance organization, who was a Medicaid contractor, was entitled to payment of subrogation funds from a tort settlement for the lead poisoning of recipient's children. The court of special appeals held that the state's Medicaid subrogation right under Md. Code Ann. Health-Gen. I § 15-120 was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: Recipient contended that § 15-120 violated principles of due process. The court disagreed and affirmed the award of subrogation funds to health maintenance organization. The court held that: 1) § 15-120's requirement that money be held from settlement proceeds did not deprive recipient or her attorney of a significant property interest because when recipient asserted a right to recover for medical expenses, she was asserting a right which belonged to the state to the extent of any payments under the Medicaid program; 2) the obligation to hold sufficient funds from the settlement proceeds to satisfy the state's subrogation claim did not violate due process principles because nothing was filed with a court and no lien attached; and, 3) health maintenance organization had a subrogation right under § 15-120, as validly assigned by the state, because it was acting as an agent or administrator for the state in providing medical care to indigent persons and in collecting back any payments received for medical treatment from responsible third parties.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the court of special appeals.

Miles v. State


No. 14, September Term, 1996


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


349 Md. 215; 707 A.2d 841; 1998 Md. LEXIS 234



April 6, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Baltimore City). Thomas Ward, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED IN PART AND VACATED IN PART, AND CASE REMANDED TO THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS WITH DIRECTIONS TO AFFIRM THE JUDGMENT ON THE CHARGE OF BATTERY AND TO VACATE THE CONVICTION ON THE CHARGE OF AGGRESSIVE PANHANDLING. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE DIVIDED EQUALLY BETWEEN THE PETITIONER AND THE MAYOR AND CITY COUNCIL OF BALTIMORE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Court of Special Appeals, Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland), which affirmed defendant's sentences following his conviction on charges of battery and aggressive panhandling.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of common law battery for punching a man who had denied his request for money. Based on the same act, defendant was also convicted of aggressive panhandling, in violation of former Baltimore City Code art. 19, § 249. The trial court sentenced defendant to 10 years imprisonment for the battery conviction and a consecutive 90-day term of imprisonment for the panhandling conviction. Defendant appealed, arguing that his sentence on the battery conviction should have merged with his sentence on the panhandling conviction because common law battery was a lesser-included offense. The appellate court disagreed and affirmed defendant's sentences. The court vacated defendant's aggressive panhandling conviction, holding that (1) the "required evidence test" was inapplicable to a merger question involving a state common law or statutory offense and an offense created by a local ordinance; (2) under the rule of lenity, defendant could not have been sentenced for both offenses because the convictions were based on the same act; and (3) defendant's aggressive panhandling conviction could not have stood because art. 19, § 249 was repealed and it had no savings clause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, in part, and reversed, in part, the decision of the appellate court and remanded the matter to the appellate court with instructions to affirm the judgment on the battery charge and to vacate the judgment on the aggressive panhandling charge.

Holiday Point Marina Partners v. Anne Arundel County


No. 4, September Term, 1996


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


349 Md. 190; 707 A.2d 829; 1998 Md. LEXIS 237



April 3, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 4. Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County). Robert H. Heller, Jr. JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS VACATED, AND CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO VACATE THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY AND TO REMAND THE CASE TO THE CIRCUIT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO DISMISS THE DECLARATORY JUDGMENT ACTION. PETITIONER TO PAY THE COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff marina appealed a decision of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of defendant county on the marina's complaint for a declaratory judgment that Anne Arundel County, Md., County Code § 5-108(e) was invalid, holding that the county was empowered to enact zoning laws for the purpose of protecting the environment, and the ordinance was not preempted by federal or state law.


OVERVIEW: A marina received approvals and permits from state and federal officials to construct an expansion. The county denied a building permit, stating that the expansion violated Anne Arundel County, Md., County Code § 5-108(e), in that the expansion was closer than one-half mile to an oyster bed. The marina appealed the denial of a variance by filing an action seeking a declaratory judgment that the ordinance was invalid. The Court of Special Appeals affirmed the grant of summary judgment and, on petition for certiorari, the court vacated with instructions to dismiss. The court held that a declaratory judgment action would not lie, as the administrative and judicial review procedures were exclusive pursuant to Md. Ann. Code art. 25A, § 5(U) (1957). Even if the marina had followed proper procedure, it would not be entitled to relief, as the county's zoning power extended to regulation of the situs of piers and the number of boat slips, and the local ordinance was not preempted by state law.


OUTCOME: The judgment affirming the grant of summary judgment in favor of the county was vacated and remanded with directions to vacate the judgment of the trial court and to remand to the trial court with directions to dismiss the marina's declaratory judgment action.

Gresser v. Anne Arundel County


Nos. 20, September Term, 1997, 21, September Term, 1997, 22, September Term, 1997


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


349 Md. 542; 709 A.2d 740; 1998 Md. LEXIS 13



January 28, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County. H. Chester Goudy, JUDGE. Case # C-93-6223OL.

Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County). H. Chester Goudy, JUDGE. Case # C-93-04789.

Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County. H. Chester Goudy, JUDGE. Case # C-92-12564OC.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO VACATE THE INJUNCTION AND DECLARATORY JUDGMENT AND REMAND THIS CASE TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, adult business owners, appealed from the decision of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which in three now-consolidated cases upheld the trial court's grant of summary judgment to respondent county and held that an ordinance regulating the location and operation of adult businesses was "legal" and ordered petitioners to cease use and operation of an adult film arcade.


OVERVIEW: The court granted certiorari in three consolidated cases in which the appellate court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to respondent county and determined that an ordinance regulating the location and operation of adult bookstores, film arcades, and motion picture theaters was "legal" and ordered that petitioner adult business owners cease use and operation of an adult film arcade. The court reversed and found that respondent had conceded that the only two violations alleged against petitioners were unenforceable and that this should have resulted in the vacating of the trial court's injunction. The court held that because the appellate court affirmed the granting of an injunction for reasons not decided by the trial court and not raised below, it had to vacate the decision and remand the matter to the trial court for a full hearing on the constitutionality of the ordinances and whether an injunction should be issued.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's affirmation of the trial court's grant of summary judgment to respondent county because the only grounds against petitioner adult business owners were conceded and found to be erroneous. The court remanded for a full hearing on the constitutionality of the ordinances regulating adult businesses and whether an injunction should be issued.

Clermont v. State
