Harford County v. Town of Bel Air


No. 114, September Term, 1995


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


348 Md. 363; 704 A.2d 421; 1998 Md. LEXIS 5



January 14, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Harford County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Maurice W. Baldwin, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR HARFORD COUNTY MODIFIED IN ACCORDANCE WITH PART II OF THIS OPINION, AND, AS SO MODIFIED, AFFIRMED. HARFORD COUNTY TO PAY COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, county government, sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Hartford County (Maryland), which held that respondent township was exempt from the dumping fee imposed on respondent on the ground that it was bound by a 1982 declaratory judgment under principles of res judicata, in a breach of contract action.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner, county government, challenged the trial court's judgment, which held that respondent township was exempt from the disposal fee imposed on respondent on the ground that it was bound by the declaratory judgment under the principle of res judicata. The trial court's judgment was affirmed. The court held that petitioner had no governmental immunity in contract actions or in declaratory judgment actions relating to contractual rights and liabilities, regardless of whether the contract was made in the performance of a governmental or a proprietary function. The court found governments in Maryland did not enjoy immunity from suits in contract seeking damages. Thus, the contract was declared valid and respondent was exempt from municipal waste and recyclable fees. Finally, the court held that petitioner had no right to rescind or modify a contract merely because it found that it had made a bad deal. The court held that petitioner was able to meet the state's mandatory recycling requirement without charging respondent the disposal fee.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that held the agreement was valid and respondent township was exempt from the disposal fees because local governments in Maryland did not enjoy immunity from suits in damages in contract actions involving governmental or proprietary functions.

Mt. Olive African Methodist Episcopal Church v. Board of Incorporators of the African Methodist Episcopal Church


No. 26, September Term, 1996


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


348 Md. 299; 703 A.2d 194; 1997 Md. LEXIS 629



December 19, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. (Circuit Court for Wicomico County). D. William Simpson, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED; CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO AFFIRM THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR WICOMICO COUNTY. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY THE RESPONDENTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner local church appealed by writ of certiorari the judgment of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) in favor of respondents, national church, church members and officials, in the action to determine ownership of title to the local church property. The case was brought in reliance upon the Religious Corporations Law, Md. Code Ann. §§ 3-301 to 3-336 (1975 & 1993 Repl.), specifically Md. Code §§ 3-301 to 3-313.


OVERVIEW: The national church, church members, and officials brought the declaratory judgment action to obtain title to the local church's real property after the local church withdrew from the national church. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the local church, and the appeals court reversed that decision. On review, the court noted that the national church was a hierarchical, connectional denomination, and that the local church bought the property. The court ruled that the appeals court erroneously concluded that the local church's charter caused the property to be held in trust for the national church. The charter did not contain an explicit reverter provision, and its meaning was doubtful. Under Md. Code Ann. §§ 3-301 to 3-313, the trustees of the local church were entitled to own, use, and control the property upon withdrawal from the denomination absent express or implied contracts with the national church to the contrary. None of the three common law grounds for transfer of local church property to the denomination upon withdrawal was established. The court reversed the judgment and remanded for affirmance of the trial court decision.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of respondents and remanded with instructions to affirm the judgment of the trial court. Costs were awarded to the local church.

Bowman v. Goad


No. 51, September Term, 1997


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


348 Md. 199; 703 A.2d 144; 1997 Md. LEXIS 622



December 9, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Eugene Lerner, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY VACATED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO DISMISS THE COMPLAINT. COSTS TO BE PAID BY THE APPELLANT RUDOLPH ALBERT BOWMAN.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizen, as representative of a class of persons who allegedly paid wrongly charged fees to defendant sheriffs, appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland), which granted the sheriffs' motion for summary judgment dismissing the citizen's claim for damages for fees wrongfully collected by the sheriffs, plus attorney's fees.


OVERVIEW: The citizen filed the action for himself and other persons who had paid fees to sheriffs in the state for serving process in motor vehicle prosecutions, seeking damages representing compensation for the fees paid, plus attorney's fees. The citizen claimed that the sheriffs were prohibited from charging those fees by Md. Code Ann., Transportation § 26-410 (1977). The trial court granted the sheriffs' motion for summary judgment on the ground that Md. Code Ann., Courts and Judicial Proceedings § 7-402 (1973) authorized collection of the fees. The court vacated the judgment and remanded with directions to dismiss the complaint, costs to be paid by the citizen. The trial court should not have decided the merits of the claim. There was no statute authorizing a suit of this nature, no common law action lay for recovery of taxes or governmental fees paid under mistake of law, and the statute providing administrative refund remedies covering every type of improperly-charged tax or fee collected by a state entity was the exclusive remedy for the wrong alleged by the citizen.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was vacated and the case was remanded to that court with directions to dismiss the complaint, costs to be paid by the citizen.

State v. White


No. 13, September Term, 1997


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


348 Md. 179; 702 A.2d 1263; 1997 Md. LEXIS 621



December 5, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. (Circuit Court for Baltimore County). John Grason Turnbull, II, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED; BALTIMORE COUNTY TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted and sentenced by the circuit court on two charges of misdemeanor theft and one count of trespassing. The state sought certiorari review of the subsequent order by the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which applied the single larceny rule to defendant's theft convictions and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with robbing the office of two teachers in a local high school, and was convicted on two counts of misdemeanor theft and one count of trespassing. The trial court imposed consecutive sentences of 18 months on each of the misdemeanor theft convictions and a concurrent 60-day sentence for the trespassing. The appellate court applied the single larceny doctrine (doctrine) and merged the two theft convictions, but otherwise affirmed the judgments. The court granted the state's petition for certiorari to consider whether the doctrine was properly applied by the court of special appeals. The doctrine essentially provided that the stealing of several articles of property at the same time, belonging to several owners or the same owner, ordinarily constituted one offense. The court affirmed the judgment and held that, although application of the doctrine depended on the factual circumstances presented, the single larceny doctrine was a part of Maryland common law and, therefore, the appellate court did not err in applying the doctrine to the facts before it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court.

McDonald v. State


No. 99, September Term, 1995


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


347 Md. 452; 701 A.2d 675; 1997 Md. LEXIS 514



October 20, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied March 2, 1998, Reported at: 1998 U.S. LEXIS 1552.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Paul A. McGuckian.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR MONTGOMERY COUNTY AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland), which convicted him of possession of a controlled dangerous substance with intent to distribute in violation of Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 286(a)(1) (Supp. 1997), and of possession of a controlled dangerous substance in violation of Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 287(a).


OVERVIEW: During a random parcel check, a parcel service employee found a large quantity of marijuana. A trooper inspected it and applied for a search warrant for the address on the parcel. A warrant was issued, but it did not condition the execution of the warrant on a controlled delivery of the parcel. Minutes after delivery, police entered the house and found defendant opening the package. Defendant was arrested, and filed a motion to suppress the evidence, arguing the search warrant was an anticipatory warrant. The trial court denied the motion and defendant was convicted of possession of a controlled dangerous substance with intent to distribute in violation of Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 286(a)(1) (Supp. 1997), and of possession of a controlled dangerous substance in violation of Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 287(a). Defendant appealed. The court affirmed, holding that the warrant was not anticipatory and was not issued in reliance on the occurrence of a future delivery of the package, or any other future event. The warrant application contained objective facts from which officers could have reasonably concluded that there was probable cause to search the address.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction because the search warrant was not an anticipatory warrant and was not issued in reliance of a future event or future delivery of the parcel at issue. The court held that the warrant application contained several objective facts from which the officers could reasonably conclude there was probable cause to search.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a challenge to executive authority, appellant taxpayers sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland), which rendered judgment in favor of appellee governor and others and denied the taxpayers' request for injunction to prevent the implementation of an executive order.


OVERVIEW: The governor issued Maryland Executive Order 01.01.1996.13, which set procedures for certification of public employee organizations for collective bargaining purposes. It found that the order did not collide with the state personnel reform act, that the order did not exceed the governor's limited power to issue executive orders and otherwise establish state personnel policy, and that the order did not violate Maryland's constitutional separation of powers doctrine.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employers appealed a decision of the Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland), which required the employers to immediately comply with an employment discrimination decision and order of respondent, the Maryland Commission on Human Relations (commission). A prospective employee had filed a complaint with the commission because the employers denied him a job based on his refusal to shave a beard that he wore for religious reasons.

Further, there was no proceeding that was governed by the Administrative Procedure Act, Md. Code Ann., State Gov't § 10-222 (1995).

Ball v. State


No. 59, September Term, 1996


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


347 Md. 156; 699 A.2d 1170; 1997 Md. LEXIS 140



September 10, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of Death Penalty (Circuit Court for Charles County). Joseph Casula, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Charles County (Maryland), which sentenced him to death after he was found guilty of first degree murder and sentenced to a total of 50 years imprisonment for lesser included offenses.


OVERVIEW: Defendant confessed to killing an individual while robbing a home. On appeal, the court held that the detective's suggestion to reduce his confession to writing in order to tell the story in his own words could be interpreted as a neutral attempt to avoid later disagreement as to the particulars of defendant's oral confession and that it did not overbear defendant's free will, nor did it render the subsequent written confession involuntary. The court found that the mere fact that some asportation occurred before the use of force did not mean that the perpetrator was thereafter not guilty of the offense of robbery but rather that the totality of the circumstances that surrounded the taking had to be considered. The court determined that the trial court did not err in refusing to propound a requested jury instruction on an uncharged lesser offense of theft because there was no rational basis upon which the jury could have concluded that defendant was guilty of theft, but not guilty of robbery. The court concluded that defendant's failure to avail himself of the opportunity to confront the victim impact witnesses did not translate into a denial of his right to confrontation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court sentencing defendant to death for first degree murder.

Renko v. McLean


No. 77, September Term, 1996


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


346 Md. 464; 697 A.2d 468; 1997 Md. LEXIS 111



July 30, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Eugene M. Lerner, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED, WITH COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff daughter appealed a decision of the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland), which affirmed the judgment entering judgment in favor of defendant parents on the daughter's claim for injuries suffered when her mother negligently drove the car both women were occupying into the rear of another vehicle. At the time the daughter was seventeen years old.


OVERVIEW: The daughter was injured when a car driven by her mother was involved in a collision. She was seventeen at the time of the accident, and brought suit against her parents when she turned 18. The lower court granted judgment in favor of the parents. On appeal, the court issued a writ of certiorari before consideration by the intermediate appellate court of the issues presented, and affirmed the trial court. The court reaffirmed the parent-child tort immunity, holding that it was still in the best interests of both children and parents to retain that rule. Abrogating immunity would result only in further discord within the family and would interfere with the exercise of parental discretion in raising and disciplining children. The parent-child immunity was not unconstitutional, and survived the rational basis standard of review.


OUTCOME: The judgment granting judgment in favor of the parents on the daughter's action for the negligence of the mother was affirmed. The court reaffirmed the vitality of the parent-child immunity doctrine in the State of Maryland.

Burch v. State


No. 38, September Term, 1996


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


346 Md. 253; 696 A.2d 443; 1997 Md. LEXIS 91



July 3, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of Death Penalty. (Circuit Court for Prince George's County). Case No.: 96CR0460. Steven I. Platt, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS OF CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE OF DEATH ON COUNT ONE AFFIRMED; SENTENCE OF DEATH ON COUNT FOUR VACATED; CASE REMANDED FOR ENTRY OF SENTENCE ON COUNT FOUR OF LIFE IMPRISONMENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), in which two death sentences were imposed upon his conviction on a jury verdict of guilty on multiple offenses, including two counts of premeditated first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant killed two occupants of a home which he had burglarized. Using a verdict sheet designed for a single victim, and modified by the court and the parties to accommodate multiple victims, the jury found defendant a principal in the first degree to the murder of each victim, and imposed a single sentence of death in accordance with the form. The trial court, finding the verdict and death sentence applicable to each victim, imposed two death sentences. On review, the court conceded that the form used was improper, but rejected defendant's contention that the jury might have assessed two life sentences in separate sentencing determinations. All factors considered by the jury applied to both victims; thus, the court concluded that the appropriate remedy was to vacate one of the death sentences. It was not error to fail to instruct the jury on depraved heart murder, effectively depriving the jury of the option of convicting on a lesser included offense, where there was no rational basis for the jury to convict only on that offense, given the sufficient evidence of first-degree murder and the judge's having instructed the jury on two other varieties of second-degree murder.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of conviction. The court, however, affirmed one of the two death sentences, vacated the other death sentence, and remanded the case for entry of the sentence of life imprisonment in place of the vacated death sentence.

State v. Board of Educ.


No. 41, September Term, 1997


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


346 Md. 633; 697 A.2d 1334; 1997 Md. LEXIS 90



June 26, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Montgomery County). James McAuliffe, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED, AND CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO AFFIRM THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR MONTGOMERY COUNTY. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY THE RESPONDENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, State of Maryland, sought review by petition for a writ of certiorari, of a decision from the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which reversed the lower court's decision granting the state's motion to dismiss. The action arose out of a determination by a hearing examiner that over $ 1.2 million in overpayments to the respondent, a county board of education, was owed to the state.


OVERVIEW: Following the endorsement by the secretary of the state department of personnel (personnel) of the hearing examiner's decision, the county board of education sought judicial review. The lower court granted the state's motion to dismiss, holding that judicial review of the department of personnel's decision was precluded by prior caselaw. The board appealed and the court of special appeals reversed, holding that the department's decision was subject to judicial review. On appeal, the court reversed and held that language in a prior opinion by the court on the issue was not dicta, as it had been characterized by the court of special appeals. The court held that the general assembly could preclude judicial review in certain instances. The court held that the allocation and control of public funds, and the resolution of disputes among state government agencies and instrumentalities concerning such funds, were matters which the general assembly could fully control by legislation. The court held that the department's decision in this case was not subject to judicial review under either statutory provisions or the principles set forth in prior caselaw.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the decision of the court of special appeals, which had reversed a circuit court's decision to grant the state's motion to dismiss in an action seeking judicial review of a hearing officer's determination that overpayments were owed by a county board of education to the state.

 

46 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Professional Staff Nurses Ass'n v. Dimensions Health Corp.


No. 83, September Term, 1996.


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


346 Md. 132; 695 A.2d 158; 1997 Md. LEXIS 76; 155 L.R.R.M. 2732



June 18, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected June 23, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Prince George's County). Prince George's County Case # CAL95-6647. Steven I. Platt, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY THE PETITIONER, PROFESSIONAL STAFF NURSES ASSOCIATION.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner union appealed a judgment of the Special Court of Appeals (Maryland) which held, in favor of defendants, a health care corporation and nurse placement service, that the National Labor Relations Act (NLRA), 29 U.S.C.S. §§ 150-161, preempted the Maryland anti-strikebreakers statute, Md. Code Ann., Lab. & Empl. § 4-403 (1991).


OVERVIEW: The union filed suit arguing that the placement service was tortiously interfering with the collective bargaining negotiations between the union and the corporation in violation of § 4-403. The corporation intervened to ally with the placement service. On the motion of the corporation and placement service, the trial court dismissed the union's complaint for failure to state a claim and federal preemption. On the union's appeal, the appellate court affirmed solely on the basis of federal preemption. When the union again appealed, the court held that: (1) the appellate court improperly reached the constitutional questions which the union's complaint raised when the controversy could have been decided without addressing such constitutional issues; (2) the allegations that the union pled in its complaint did not present a justiciable controversy because there was no strike and no "strikebreaking" nurses for the placement service to supply in derogation of such a job action; and (3) the arguments in the union's appellate brief could not be read to state a claim under § 4-403 because to do so required an impermissibly broad reading of a criminal statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment entered in favor of the placement service and corporation.

 

47 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Maryland Classified Emples. Ass'n v. State


No. 79, September Term, 1996


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


346 Md. 1; 694 A.2d 937; 1997 Md. LEXIS 70



June 9, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore City pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Joseph H. H. Kaplan, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, association, chapter, and individual members, filed a declaratory judgment action against appellees, state and state agencies, alleging that 1995 Md. Laws ch. 491, which provided for privatization of certain child support enforcement services, was unconstitutional. The Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland) held that ch. 491 was not unconstitutional. The association, chapter, and individual members filed an appeal.


OVERVIEW: The association, chapter, and individual members contended that 1995 Md. Laws ch. 491 violated the single subject requirement of Md. Const. art. III, § 29. They also argued that the statute violated their rights to due process of law because they had obtained a property interest in their employment and would lose their jobs under a pilot program for privatization of certain child support enforcement services. The court found that 1995 Md. Laws ch. 491 did not violate the single subject requirement because the objective of improved child support enforcement had a sufficient nexus with the balance of the legislation to constitute part of the single subject of welfare reform. The court further found no federal or state due process violation. It reasoned that there was no right to continued state employment protected by a theory of substantive due process; moreover, an employee who lost his job was not entitled to a hearing when the position was abolished pursuant to a bona fide government reorganization or kindred cost-cutting measure. The court observed that the association, chapter, and individual members had notice of the threat to their jobs and opportunities for a hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's declaratory judgment that a state law establishing a pilot program for privatization of certain child support enforcement services was not unconstitutional.

Conyers v. State

COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND

DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS AFFIRMED, EXCEPT THE CONVICTION FOR BURGLARY IS REVERSED AND THE IMPOSITION OF THE DEATH SENTENCE FOR THE MURDER OF WANDA JOHNSON IS VACATED. CASE REMANDED TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR WICOMICO COUNTY FOR A NEW SENTENCING PROCEEDING UNDER § 413 OF ART. 27. COSTS TO BE EQUALLY DIVIDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of premeditated murder, felony murder, first-degree burglary, and various robbery offenses by the Circuit Court for Wicomico County (Maryland). Defendant was sentenced to death and appealed.


OVERVIEW: During the course of a burglary defendant allegedly shot and killed the owner of the home. In addition, defendant allegedly killed another man in the street. The court found that the trial court's refusal to admit a statement by defendant that someone other than defendant was in possession of his guns on the night in question was proper because the doctrine of verbal completeness did not allow evidence otherwise inadmissible as hearsay to be admitted. It was not error for the trial court to join defendant's two murder offenses for trial because under the mutual admissibility test evidence concerning both offenses would have been admissible in a separate trial for each offense. Next, the court found that the evidence was insufficient to sustain defendant's conviction for burglary because the evidence of breaking was insufficient. However, the evidence was sufficient to convict for robbery and robbery with a deadly weapon. Evidence of defendant's juvenile record should have been excluded, and was highly inflammatory requiring the reversal of defendant's death sentence and the grant of a new sentencing hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions except for the burglary conviction. The court granted reversed the death sentence imposed and granted a new sentencing hearing.

Gisriel v. Ocean City Bd. of Election


No. 5, September Term, 1995


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


345 Md. 477; 693 A.2d 757; 1997 Md. LEXIS 50



May 1, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Worcester County). Theodore R. Eschenburg, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED, WITH COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff local citizen brought an action suit against defendants, the board of supervisors of elections, the city, and the city council, alleging that a referendum petition on a recently enacted ordinance should have been authorized. The Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) reversed a judgment in favor of the local citizen. The local citizen challenged the appellate court's judgment.


OVERVIEW: The board of supervisors of elections (board) determined that the citizen had not obtained a sufficient number of signatures to place the ordinance at issue before the electorate. The board's method of determining whether referendum petitions met the requisite number of qualified signatures was to compare the names on a submitted petition with the city's list of registered voters as of the date the petition was filed. The citizen argued that the names of unqualified voters should have first been removed from the master list. On appeal, the court first found that the lower court had proper jurisdiction of the appeal because Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 12-301 (1995), which limited the right to appeal an adjudicatory decision by an administrative agency or local legislative body pursuant to a statute, ordinance, or charter provision, was not applicable in the instant case, which was a traditional common law mandamus action. The court found that the voter registration lists were presumed to be the lists of all qualified voters at any given point in time as long as reasonable procedures were available to periodically delete from the lists the names of unqualified voters.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment from the lower court against the local citizen.

52 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Jakanna Woodworks v. Montgomery County


No. 18, September Term, 1996


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


344 Md. 584; 689 A.2d 65; 1997 Md. LEXIS 11



February 13, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County. S. Michael Pincus, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR MONTGOMERY COUNTY REVERSED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY MONTGOMERY COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner store sought review of the order of the lower court and the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland), which had upheld a fine imposed under respondent county's code because petitioner had failed to obtain a license prior to placing an advertisement. Petitioner argued that the regulation of commercial speech was an invalid prior restraint that violated the Md. Const. Decl. Rts. art. 40 and U.S. Const. amend. I.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner store relocated and sold off its inventory prior to relocation. Petitioner advertised its sale in a newspaper as a "liquidation". Respondent county's code required merchants to obtain a license prior to advertising a "closing out sale"; respondent's code stated that respondent "may" grant a license if respondent was satisfied that the proposed sale was consistent with the proposed advertising. Petitioner did not obtain such a license and was fined. Petitioner sought review unsuccessfully in the district court and the intermediate appellate court. Respondent claimed that the advertisement was a misrepresentation calculated to deceive the public, and it did so because petitioner did not use every means possible to rid itself of all inventory. The court reversed and held that respondent's code did not directly advance respondent's interest in protecting consumers from deceptive advertising. The restriction of words such as "liquidation" did little to prevent false advertising. The court noted that respondent conceded that petitioner was fined for using the word liquidation in its unlicensed advertisement and not because the advertisement was misleading.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court and held that respondent county's code required petitioner business to apply for a license prior to advertising a "closing out sale". The court held that under the U.S. Constitution and the Maryland Declaration of Rights the code was not narrowly drafted to achieve its ends, and the code did nothing to directly advance respondent's interest in protecting consumers from deceptive advertising.

COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND

Sugarloaf Citizens' Ass'n v. Department of Env't


No. 60, September Term, 1995


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


344 Md. 271; 686 A.2d 605; 1996 Md. LEXIS 130



December 20, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected December 26, 1996. Motion for Reconsideration Denied February 11, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Md. LEXIS 29.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Montgomery County). DeLawrence Beard, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED, AND CASE REMANDED TO THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS WITH DIRECTIONS TO REVERSE THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR MONTGOMERY COUNTY AND REMAND THE CASE TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO ENTER A JUDGMENT AFFIRMING THE DECISION OF THE DEPARTMENT OF THE ENVIRONMENT. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY THE RESPONDENTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, landowners and non-profit organizations, challenged the decision of defendant Maryland Department of the Environment to issue two permits authorizing the construction of a solid waste incinerator. The Circuit Court for Montgomery County dismissed the action for lacking of standing. The Court of Special Appeals (Maryland). Plaintiffs filed a petition for a writ of certiorari, which the court granted.


OVERVIEW: The court ruled that the circuit court should have affirmed the administrative decision rather than dismiss the action for lack of standing. The court concluded that if the administrative law judge (ALJ) was rendering findings and conclusions on the plaintiffs' entitlement to maintain an action in court, rather than their standing to be parties at the administrative hearing, then the ALJ exceeded her proper role. The determination of whether plaintiffs had standing to maintain an action in court was exclusively a judicial function. Thus, the appellate court erred in holding that any deference could be given to the administrative decision concerning plaintiffs' lack of standing. The court ruled that the fact that the level of pollutants from the incinerator falling on nearby property may be "acceptable" under governmental air quality standards, thereby justifying the issuance of the permits, was not the test for plaintiff's standing to seek judicial review. Instead, the test was whether the plaintiffs were affected in a way different from the public generally. The administrative record showed that nearby property owners would be affected in a way different from the general public.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court and remanded the case to the appellate court with directions to reverse the judgment of the circuit court and remand the case to that court with directions to enter a judgment affirming defendant's decision.

Perry v. State


No. 119, September Term, 1995


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


344 Md. 204; 686 A.2d 274; 1996 Md. LEXIS 127



December 16, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of Death Penalty (Circuit Court for Montgomery County). County Case # 72050. D. Warren Donohue, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR MONTGOMERY COUNTY AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction and life imprisonment and death sentences from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland), which convicted defendant of conspiracy to commit murder.


OVERVIEW: The State convicted and sentenced defendant for his involvement in a conspiracy to commit murder. The court affirmed the lower court's conviction and sentence of defendant without prejudice to his ability to raise certain issues on post conviction review. There was no discretional abuse in the lower court's restriction of the scope of voir dire based on the absence of a reasonable likelihood of uncovering a disqualification in connection with another class of crime. Defendant's objections as to the inadmissibility of recorded conversations and ineffective assistance were not properly before the court. The record was inadequate to address such issues, which were risible on post conviction review. Nor did the lower court err in refusing to conduct a belated suppression hearing, in admitting a co-conspirator's deposition statements as hearsay exceptions, or in admitting fingerprint comparison evidence, given defendant's waiver of a right to a limiting instruction. Defendant's remaining contentions as to the jury instructions, the sufficiency of the evidence, and the constitutionality of the death penalty were meritless.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and the imposition of life imprisonment and the death penalty.

Lussier v. Maryland Racing Comm'n


No. 96, September Term, 1994


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


343 Md. 681; 684 A.2d 804; 1996 Md. LEXIS 115



November 8, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Baltimore County). James T. Smith, Jr., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED. PETITIONER TO PAY COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff racehorse owner challenged a decision from the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which affirmed a trial court's decision that upheld an order of defendant Maryland Racing Commission (commission) that imposed a $ 5,000 fine upon the racehorse owner for misconduct.


OVERVIEW: The racehorse owner contended that the commission's order was invalid because the legislature had not explicitly authorized the commission to impose a fine upon a racehorse owner. However, the court rejected the racehorse owner's contention. The court held that Md. Code Ann., Bus. Reg. § 11-210 broadly authorized the commission to adopt regulations to govern racing and betting on racing in the Maryland and then specified four types of regulations that the commission could not adopt. The court held that regulations promulgated under such a broad grant of authority were valid if they did not contradict the statutory language or purpose. On that basis, the court concluded that the commission's regulation authorizing the imposition of a $ 5,000 fine upon a racehorse owner who engaged in the type of deceptive misconduct at issue in this case was valid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment from the appellate court that the commission's regulation authorizing the imposition of a reasonable fine was valid.

DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED, WITH COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed, by writ of certiorari from the judgement of the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), which affirmed his conviction on charges of incest.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of engaging in sexual relations with the daughter of his half-sister. Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 335 provided that any person who had carnal knowledge of another person who was with the degrees of consanguinity within which marriages were prohibited by state law was guilty of a felony. Md. Code Ann., Fam. Law § 2-202(c)(1)(xii) prohibited a man from marrying his sister's daughter. Defendant appealed his conviction, which was affirmed by the appellate court. He was granted a petition for a writ of certiorari. He claimed that the statute did not address half-blood relationships and the rule of lenity prohibited the expansion of a criminal statute to cover activities not specifically contained in the statute. The court affirmed the convictions. The court held that the rule that a man could not marry his niece applied to half-blood relationships and that such a marriage was prohibited by the statute. As the marriage was prohibited, carnal relations between uncles and half-nieces were also prohibited. Defendant was guilty of incest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's judgment, which affirmed defendant's conviction on charges of incest.

OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision denying a grant of declaratory relief to the state board.

DeBusk v. Johns Hopkins Hosp.


No. 110, September Term, 1995


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


342 Md. 432; 677 A.2d 73; 1996 Md. LEXIS 57



June 3, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected June 6, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Baltimore City). Clifton J. Gordy, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee challenged an order from the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which affirmed the summary judgment ruling of the trial court that held that the employee's workers' compensation claim was barred by the two-year statute of limitations found in Md. Code Ann. Lab. & Empl. § 9-709 and that the statute was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The employee suffered a lifting injury while working as a nurse at a hospital. She felt a pull and suffered minor discomforts in her neck and shoulder at the time of the incident and sought medical care several months later. An exam showed nothing remarkable and she continued her work. Almost two years after the accident, tests revealed that she had disc herniation and a spur on her spine. More than two years after the accident, the employee filed a workers' compensation claim. On appeal of the lower court's finding that her claim was properly rejected under the two-year statute of limitations found in Md. Code Ann. Lab. & Empl. § 9-709, the court examined legislative history and the purpose of the law to hold that the two-year period did begin to run from the date of the accident. The employee argued that it ran from the date she discovered that she had a compensable injury. The court ruled that predictability was the cornerstone of the Workers' Compensation Act and that the interpretation was consistent with the plain words of the statute. The court also ruled that the statute was not unconstitutional because it was rationally related to a legitimate government objective.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order from the court of special appeals, which ruled that the employee's workers' compensation claim was barred by the two-year statute of limitations.

Armstead v. State


No. 133, September Term, 1993


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


342 Md. 38; 673 A.2d 221; 1996 Md. LEXIS 32; 64 U.S.L.W. 2691



March 20, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Howard County). Cornelius F. Sybert, Jr., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY THE PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was granted certiorari from the decision of the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Howard County, Maryland) affirming defendant's conviction and holding that the trial court did not err in refusing to exclude the DNA profile based on the statistical methods used because the evidence was admissible by Md. Code Ann. § 10-915.


OVERVIEW: Defendant filed a motion in limine to exclude the DNA evidence of identity alleging that he was entitled to an inverse Frye-Reed hearing, that the state was required to prove current general acceptance of DNA evidence as a prerequisite to the admission, that Md. Code Ann. § 10-915 was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad, that the use of DNA evidence violated his right to due process, and that the statute denied him his constitutional right to confrontation. The trial court held that the vagueness doctrine did not apply to an evidentiary statute and that DNA results were not so unreliable as to violate due process. The court held that the evidence was admissible pursuant to statute and that defendant's due process rights were not violated. The statute precluded all challenges to the admissibility of DNA evidence except constitutional challenges and eliminated "inverse Frye-Reed" hearings and individualized balancing of probative value against prejudicial effect. The jury was fully informed of the possibility for laboratory error. The state provided the required background information, and defendant had ample opportunity for cross-examination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and the decision of the court of special appeals that the trial court did not err in refusing to exclude DNA evidence because the evidence was admissible by statute.

 

63 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Gary v. State


No. 64, September Term, 1995


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


341 Md. 513; 671 A.2d 495; 1996 Md. LEXIS 15



February 8, 1996, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which affirmed defendant's conviction for conspiracy to commit murder and the trial court's imposition of a sentence of life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for his participation in a drive by shooting and on appeal contested his sentence of life imprisonment. The court found that under Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 38 (1957), conspiracy was punishable to the maximum penalty for the substantive underlying crime. Under Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 412(b) (1957), life imprisonment was the minimum penalty for murder. Defendant, however, argued that under the old version of Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 38 (1957) punishment for conspiracy was limited to 10 years and that this limit was merely repealed to avoid sentences that were greater than that imposed for the substantive crime. Defendant pointed to the unavailability of the death penalty for a conviction for conspiracy to commit murder to bolster his argument. The court found that it was just as logical to conclude that the legislature repealed the 10 year limit on sentences for conspiracy out of a desired to punish those who conspire to commit criminal acts as severely as those who commit them. Furthermore, the court found it more probable that the legislature did not authorize the death penalty for conspiracy because of the unique nature of that punishment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for conspiracy and his sentence of life imprisonment.

Grandison v. State


No. 64, September Term, 1994


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


341 Md. 175; 670 A.2d 398; 1995 Md. LEXIS 175



December 27, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected January 22, 1996.
Reconsideration denied by, 02/05/1996
Writ of certiorari denied Grandison v. Maryland, 519 U.S. 1027, 117 S. Ct. 581, 136 L. Ed. 2d 512, 1996 U.S. LEXIS 7483 (1996)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Application denied by Grandison v. State, 351 Md. 732, 720 A.2d 322, 1998 Md. LEXIS 1065 (1998)

DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was granted review of his conviction of first degree murder and death penalty from the Circuit Court for Somerset County (Maryland).


OVERVIEW: In an appeal of the death penalty, the court held that the murder for hire aggravating circumstance narrowed the class of defendants eligible for the death penalty and could also serve as an aggravating circumstance to warrant the penalty. Appellant's unmeritorious refusal to proceed with current counsel constituted a waiver of his right to counsel. Victim impact statements were admissible. To preserve the alleged error in limiting his right to cross examine the victim for review, appellant was required to proffer testimony with sufficient clarity to establish that the cross examination would reveal relevant information. The jury instructions actually given properly presented the law. Appellant was properly notified that the state would seek the death penalty. Prosecutor's closing argument presented neither individual nor cumulative errors. The presentence report, which included a statement of prior crimes and infractions while appellant was incarcerated, was properly admitted. Testimony from a prior proceeding was admissible because the witness was unavailable to testify.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of first degree murder and the death sentence.

 

65 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Gadson v. State


No. 25, September Term, 1995


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


341 Md. 1; 668 A.2d 22; 1995 Md. LEXIS 167



December 7, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County). Raymond G. Thieme, Jr., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO REMAND THIS CASE TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS TO BE PAID BY ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) affirmed a ruling that denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence. Certiorari was granted to review the ruling.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped before he entered a prison facility and was informed that the state police would perform a "canine sniff" of his vehicle. Although defendant objected and asked to leave the facility, the sniff was performed. As a result, drugs were found that were introduced at defendant's trial. The court held that absent reasonable, articulable suspicion of criminal activity, it was unreasonable under U.S. Const. amend. IV and Md. Const. Decl. Rts. art. 26 to detain defendant whom, prior to entering the prison, indicated a preference to leave rather than submit to the detention. The detention was an illegal seizure. The court rejected the state's argument that the detention was permissible under the exception to the search and seizure rule for detaining motorists at checkpoints. The reasonableness of a checkpoint detention was determined by balancing the intrusion of the motorist's privacy interests against the societal need served by the seizure. Defendant's seizure was not designed to serve the state's articulated interest in keeping drugs out of its correctional facilities because that purpose was fully served once defendant agreed to turn away from the prison building.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and the evidence was suppressed.

 

66 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Prince George's County v. Vieira


No. 128, SEPTEMBER TERM, 1994


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


340 Md. 651; 667 A.2d 898; 1995 Md. LEXIS 161



November 29, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. (Circuit Court for Prince George's County). Darlene G. Perry, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED, WITH COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner county filed an action for forfeiture of currency against respondent possessor of drug paraphernalia. The trial court ordered the currency forfeited. The possessor appealed to the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which reversed the trial court's judgment and the county sought review.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that the legislature intended a forfeiture petition for money or currency, to include the filing of an executed show cause order, as opposed to a proposed one, along with the complaint and affidavit, within ninety days of the date of final disposition of a criminal proceeding. The county argued on appeal that, in light of the plain meaning of the forfeiture statute and the fact that the complaint and the affidavit provided a basis on which a judge would execute a show cause order, the legislature intended that a proposed, not an executed, show cause order, be filed with the complaint and the affidavit. The court held that the forfeiture statute, Md. Code, Art. 27, § 297(d)(2)(i), characterized, without limitation, the summons component of the application for a forfeiture petition as a show cause order. In so doing, the legislature indicated its intention that an actual show cause order, i.e., one that had been executed by the court, be filed, as part of the application, within 90 days of the final disposition of the criminal proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

67 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Baltimore Sun Co. v. State


No. 35, September Term, 1995


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


340 Md. 437; 667 A.2d 166; 1995 Md. LEXIS 151; 24 Media L. Rep. 1362



November 13, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore City - Division for Juvenile Causes, pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeal. David B. Mitchell, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] ORDER OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY DATED FEBRUARY 6, 1995 VACATED; CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT FOR SUCH FURTHER ACTION AS THE COURT MAY DEEM APPROPRIATE CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION; COSTS TO BE PAID BY RESPONDENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant newspaper sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland), which excluded its access to a juvenile proceeding based on appellant's alleged violation of an earlier court order by printing information about the juvenile at issue and by refusing to print the court's order.


OVERVIEW: The lower court granted the media, including appellant, access to a juvenile proceeding on the condition that the juvenile in question was not referred to by his full legal name. Appellant published an enhanced photo of the juvenile that it received from the police and referred to the juvenile by a first and last name (the last name was his mother's, not his legal name). The lower court issued an order denying only appellant access to the proceedings after appellant refused to publish the court's order. The court found that a judicial order conditioning access to a juvenile proceeding upon the required publication of specific material was unconstitutional to the same extent as an order conditioning access upon a restraint from publication. The court concluded that as appellant did not technically violate the court's first order as there was not ban on photos and the juvenile's legal name was not published, appellant should have been given access on the same basis as other members of the press. The court vacated the order denying appellant access to the proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the lower court's order excluding appellant newspaper from a juvenile proceeding and held that the lower court abused its discretion in excluding appellant while allowing other media representatives to attend the proceedings as appellant did not actually violate the court's earlier order.

Motor Vehicle Admin. v. Karwacki


No. 119, SEPTEMBER TERM, 1994


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


340 Md. 271; 666 A.2d 511; 1995 Md. LEXIS 145



October 25, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Circuit Court for Baltimore City. John C. Themelis, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY REVERSED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO REINSTATE THE DECISION OF THE MVA. COSTS TO BE PAID BY THE RESPONDENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner vehicle administration sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland), which reversed an administrative law judge's decision from a probable cause hearing held pursuant to Md. Code Ann. Transport. I § 16-205.1(f)(7) that gave greater credit to the sworn written statement of an absent police officer, who had not been subpoenaed by either party, than to the conflicting testimony of respondent driver.


OVERVIEW: Respondent driver was pulled over for a traffic violation by a police officer. The officer came to believe that respondent had been driving while intoxicated and noted those observations on the appropriate forms, which respondent signed, and requested that respondent take a blood alcohol concentration test (test), which respondent refused. The officer was not subpoenaed for the probable cause hearing held pursuant to Md. Code Ann. Transport. I § 16-205.1(f)(7), but the forms and respondent's record from his prior refusal were submitted. The administrative law judge (ALJ) suspended respondent's license for a year. The trial court reversed, finding the suspension unsupported by competent material evidence. The court reversed because the officer's sworn statement was prima facie evidence of a test refusal, which was sufficient to establish that respondent refused to take the test. The court held that the officer's sworn statement provided adequate support for the ALJ's conclusion that respondent was fully advised of the consequences of a test refusal, notwithstanding respondent's testimony to the contrary.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's reversal of the ALJ's decision because the officer's sworn statement was prima facie evidence that respondent driver refused to take the test. The court further held that the officer's sworn statement provided adequate support for the ALJ's conclusion that respondent was fully advised of the consequences of a test refusal, notwithstanding his testimony to the contrary.

ACandS, Inc. v. GODWIN


No. 23, September Term, 1994


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


340 Md. 334; 667 A.2d 116; 1995 Md. LEXIS 143



October 18, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected. Motion for Reconsideration Denied December 1, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Md. LEXIS 162.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, manufacturers, suppliers, and installers, appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland), which entered judgments for three of six illustrative plaintiffs, users and/or bystanders, and determined "state of the art" and punitive damages issues common to 8,549 others in a consolidated trial of asbestos products liability failure to warn actions sounding in strict liability and negligence.


OVERVIEW: The lower court issued a mass consolidation order applicable to 8,555 actions involving claims for personal injuries or wrongful death allegedly resulting from exposure to asbestos. In a trial to determine common issues of liability, the parties also agreed to dispose of the claims of six illustrative users and/or bystanders. Following trial, judgment was entered granting compensatory damages to three of the six and imposing liability for punitive damages against a manufacturer and a supplier/installer. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court affirmed the judgments with regard to compensatory damages with a single exception. A finding of liability of one manufacturer as to one user/bystander was reversed, because there was insufficient evidence that he had been exposed to that manufacturer's product. The court reversed the judgments for punitive damages, finding no evidence of bad faith or actual malice. The court held that the consolidation did not result in a denial of due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, with the exception of one, the judgments for compensatory damages for the users and/or bystanders and reversed, for insufficient evidence, the judgments for punitive damages.

Fraternal Order of Police v. Baltimore County


No. 158, September Term, 1993


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


340 Md. 157; 665 A.2d 1029; 1995 Md. LEXIS 135; 151 L.R.R.M. 2044



October 10, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. John F. Fader, II, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE COUNTY REVERSED, AND CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS NOT INCONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS TO BE PAID BY BALTIMORE COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff union appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland), which vacated an arbitrator's award of compensation for lost wages and benefits to police employees covered by a collective bargaining agreement with defendant county because a furlough breached this agreement. The union filed a notice of appeal with the intermediate appellate court. This court granted its petition for writ of certiorari.


OVERVIEW: The county enacted a furlough plan in violation of a collective bargaining agreement with the union, pursuant to Baltimore County Code § 25-51, prohibiting the furlough of police officers in exchange for a freeze on cost-of-living adjustments and providing for arbitration of disputes, pursuant to § 25-59. The union's grievance challenging the county action was submitted to an arbitrator, who awarded compensation to the union. On appeal, the court held that the county was bound by the contract prohibiting the furlough of police officers. Although the provision prohibiting furloughs did affect compensation, the grievance was subject to arbitration. Funds were appropriated in the county's budget for the police compensation without any furloughs, as required by the agreement. The county exercised its legislative discretion under the county charter by enacting a budget including funds to compensate the employees covered by the collective bargaining agreement. The subsequent arbitrator's decision was consistent with the enacted budget. Baltimore County Charter § 714 did not authorize the county to breach its contracts unilaterally or to reduce appropriations in an enacted budget.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case to that court for proceedings not inconsistent with its opinion. Costs were to be paid by the county.

Whittlesey v. State


No. 16, September Term, 1994


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


340 Md. 30; 665 A.2d 223; 1995 Md. LEXIS 133



September 28, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied February 26, 1996, Reported at: 1996 U.S. LEXIS 1444.


PRIOR HISTORY: Review of Death Penalty (Circuit Court for Caroline County). J. Owen Wise, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED EXCEPT AS TO THE IMPOSITION OF THE DEATH SENTENCE; DEATH SENTENCE VACATED AND CASE REMANDED TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR CAROLINE COUNTY FOR A NEW SENTENCING PROCEEDING. COSTS TO BE PAID BY BALTIMORE COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his sentence rendered by the Circuit Court for Caroline County (Maryland) following a jury conviction for first degree murder and a sentence of death imposed by the same jury. Appellant was previously convicted of robbing the victim, who was his former classmate. He was indicted for murder eight years after the victim's disappearance when the victim's body was discovered in a park.


OVERVIEW: Appellant robbed and killed his former classmate and was found guilty of robbery and theft after the victim's belongings were found in his possession. The victim's body was found eight years after the robbery. Appellant did not testify at his trial before a jury. He was found guilty of both premeditated murder and felony murder and sentenced to death. On appeal, the court found that conversations between appellant and a witness were not excluded from evidence by the Sixth Amendment and reasoned that appellant's right to counsel had not attached because the charges of false statements and murder were not closely related. Uncharged misconduct evidence was properly admitted at trial for the purpose of showing appellant's state of mind. The trial court erred when it strictly applied the rules of evidence and did not admit hearsay evidence at the capital sentencing hearing because the word "evidence" in Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 413(c) did not require that the strict rules of evidence were to be followed. The court found that the trial was not a double jeopardy violation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for premeditated murder and felony murder. The court vacated the death sentence because the trial court had erred by strictly applying the rules of evidence at the capital sentencing hearing and ruling that certain hearsay evidence was inadmissible even though it was probative. The court remanded the case for a new sentencing proceeding.

Embrey v. Motor Vehicle Admin.


No. 6, SEPTEMBER TERM, 1995


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND

September 15, 1995, FILED

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner driver sought review, by writ of certiorari to the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland), from a decision by respondent state agency, which suspended the driver's license to operate a vehicle and refused to issue a restricted license because the driver had a prior restriction within the past five years.


OVERVIEW: The driver was arrested for driving under the influence of alcohol after he failed a field sobriety test. He agreed to take a breath test, which indicated an alcohol concentration of 0.13. Pursuant to Md. Ann. Code art. 16, § 205.1(b)(3) (1977, 1992 Repl. Vol., 1994 Cum. Supp.) the arresting officer confiscated the driver's license and served him with an order of suspension. The driver requested an administrative hearing to show cause why his license should not be suspended. At the hearing, the driver acknowledged receipt of a prior restricted license within the past five years. He argued that the current charge was not a second offense because his license was not suspended in the first proceeding. The administrative hearing officer and the trial court held that § 205.1 rendered the driver ineligible for a restricted license. On petition for review by certiorari, the court affirmed because the issuance of the prior restricted license meant that there had been a suspension within the meaning of § 205.1.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision that the driver was not entitled to a restricted license after he was arrested for driving under the influence of alcohol.

Aravanis v. Somerset County


No. 22, SEPTEMBER TERM, 1994


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


339 Md. 644; 664 A.2d 888; 1995 Md. LEXIS 125



September 13, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Somerset County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Daniel M. Long, Judge.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR SOMERSET COUNTY VACATED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS TO BE PAID BY SOMERSET COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment from the Circuit Court for Somerset County (Maryland), which granted appellee county's petition for civil forfeiture of his property, under Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 297 (1957, 1992 Repl. Vol.), after he pleaded guilty to possession of a controlled dangerous substance in sufficient quantity to indicate an intent to manufacture, distribute, or dispense, under Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 286 (1957, 1992 Repl. Vol.).


OVERVIEW: The court granted certiorari to consider whether Maryland's drug forfeiture statute, Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 297 (1957, 1992 Repl. Vol.), was subject to an excessive fines analysis, pursuant to the Eighth Amendment and/or Md. Const. Decl. Rts. art. 25. The appellant argued that the county failed to establish, by clear and convincing evidence, that he acquired the property during the period he was violating the law and that there was no other source for the acquisition of the property. The court held that: (1) the statutory presumption as to the forfeitability of property had no relevance to establishing its ownership; (2) the civil in rem forfeiture statute was partially intended as punishment; and (3) that the statute purported to limit the size of property that could be taken did not shield the forfeiture from Eighth Amendment review. The court examined the instrumentality and proportionality tests, favored the multi-factor test using a variety of proportionality factors, but declined to devise its own new test for determining the constitutional excessiveness of particular forfeitures. Accordingly, the court reversed the judgment and remanded the case.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment rendered by the trial court, which granted the county's petition for civil forfeiture of the appellant's property, and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings consistent with the court's opinion.

Insurance Comm'r v. Equitable Life Assurance Soc'y of the United States


No. 26, September Term, 1993


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


339 Md. 596; 664 A.2d 862; 1995 Md. LEXIS 122



September 11, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore City pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Robert I.H. Hammerman, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY VACATED, AND CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO VACATE THE ORDER OF THE INSURANCE COMMISSIONER AND TO REMAND THE CASE TO THE INSURANCE COMMISSIONER FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS NOT INCONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS TO BE EVENLY DIVIDED BETWEEN THE STATE OF MARYLAND AND THE EQUITABLE LIFE ASSURANCE SOCIETY OF THE UNITED STATES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, insurance commissioner, human relations commission, and the National Organization for Women (NOW), and cross-appellant insurer sought a writ of certiorari from the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland), which reversed in part a decision of appellant insurance commissioner and held that Md. Ann. Code art. 48A §§ 223(b)(2), 226(c)(2), and 234A(b) did not violate the Maryland Equal Rights Amendment, Md. Const. Decl. Rts. art. 46.


OVERVIEW: The Human Relations Commission (HR Commission) found that an insurer was discriminatorily determining rates and accessibility to disability and life insurance. An administrative appeals board affirmed. On appeal the circuit court held that the HR Commission did not have jurisdiction and transferred the case to the Insurance Commission. (Ins. On writ of certiorari the court ruled in part in favor of the insurer and vacated the remainder of the decision. The court agreed that the disability issue was moot. The court found that the Ins. Commission had authority to determine constitutionality. And finally, the court found that challenged statutes were not applicable to the controversy and that the Ins. Commission and courts thus erred in rendering judgment as to the statutes' constitutionality.


OUTCOME: The judgment holding that issues related to disability insurance discrimination were moot was affirmed. The judgment as to constitutionality of statutes was vacated, and the cause was remanded with directions to vacate orders from the Ins. Commission and to remand the case to the Ins. Commission for further proceedings. The court ordered that costs be divided evenly between the state and the insurer.

Ward v. Department of Pub. Safety & Correctional Servs.


No. 10, September Term, 1995


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


339 Md. 343; 663 A.2d 66; 1995 Md. LEXIS 108



August 21, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Wicomico County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Alfred T. Truitt, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR WICOMICO COUNTY AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART; CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO REMAND THE CASE TO THE ADMINISTRATIVE AGENCY FOR APPROPRIATE ACTION CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS TO BE PAID ONE HALF BY THE APPELLANT AND ONE HALF BY THE APPELLEE. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court for Wicomico County (Maryland) that affirmed the decision of the state's secretary of personnel, which suspended and then discharged him from his position as a correctional officer for appellee employer, department of public safety and correctional services. While the appeal was pending, the court, on its own motion, granted certiorari.


OVERVIEW: The employee filed actions for judicial review of his reprimand, suspensions, and removal from his position as a correctional officer. His removal was based on multiple disciplinary infractions, including failure to report for duty and failure to report receipt of criminal summons. The employer's regulations provided for a system of progressive discipline. The trial court rejected the employee's double jeopardy argument and, ruling from the bench, upheld the disciplinary sanctions, including the removal. On its own motion, the court granted certiorari. The court reversed in part the trial court's judgment and remanded, directing the trial court to remand the action to the administrative agency. The court rejected the employee's administrative double jeopardy argument and held that principles of double jeopardy were not applicable because the disciplinary sanctions imposed upon the employee were remedial in nature, not punitive. However, the court found that the imposition of one of his suspension was not authorized by the regulation under which it was purportedly imposed. However, the other disciplinary action against him were undertaken in accordance with the regulations.


OUTCOME: The court reversed that part of the trial court's judgment that affirmed the decision of the state's secretary of personnel, was it pertained to one of the suspensions imposed on the employee. As to that part of the judgment the court remanded, directing a remand to the administrative agency. Otherwise the court affirmed the disciplinary action against the employee, which were undertaken in accordance with the regulations.

Gertz v. Anne Arundel County


No. 13, September Term, 1994


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


339 Md. 261; 661 A.2d 1157; 1995 Md. LEXIS 100



July 21, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County). Bruce C. Williams JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO REINSTATE THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT/CROSS-APPELLEE GERTZ.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner and defendant county challenged an order of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which affirmed the denial of plaintiff's 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim and held that res judicata applied to bar judgment against plaintiff in his declaratory judgment action against defendant.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff landowner, who had been using fill on his land pursuant to a consent agreement from a lawsuit with defendant county, brought an action for declaratory judgment against defendant when it passed an ordinance requiring a permit for that activity. Defendant counterclaimed for an injunction, and plaintiff added a claim under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and for breach of contract. The trial court, ignoring a judgment for plaintiff on the declaratory judgment in a prior summary judgment order, found for defendant on all issues. The appellate court held that res judicata applied and that 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 did not apply. On further appeal, the court held that res judicata did not apply because the two lawsuits were based upon different sources, and that the summary judgment order was not the law of the case because it did not address all issues. The court found no 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's finding of res judicata, affirmed its denial of the constitutional claim, and remanded with an order that the appellate court reinstate the trial court's judgment.

Ashton v. Brown


No. 102, September Term, 1992


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


339 Md. 70; 660 A.2d 447; 1995 Md. LEXIS 89



June 30, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Frederick County). G. Edward Dwyer, Jr., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS VACATED, AND CASE REMANDED TO THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS WITH DIRECTIONS TO AFFIRM THOSE PARTS OF THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR FREDERICK COUNTY RELATING TO THE COUNTS CHARGING INTENTIONAL INFLICTION OF EMOTIONAL DISTRESS AND NEGLIGENCE, AND OTHERWISE TO VACATE THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT AND REMAND THE CASE TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR FREDERICK COUNTY FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS NOT INCONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY THE CITY OF FREDERICK.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff juveniles sought review of a judgment of the Court of Special Appeals of Maryland, which reversed in part the trial court's grant of the defendant city and police officers' motion for summary judgment. The lower court held the curfew ordinance, under which the juveniles were detained or arrested, was unconstitutionally vague but it affirmed that part of the order granting summary judgment which denied the juveniles' claims for damages.


OVERVIEW: Two juveniles were detained or arrested pursuant to a city curfew ordinance under Frederick City Code §§ 15-9(a), 15-10. The juveniles contended the ordinance was unconstitutionally vague under both the Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment and the Maryland Declaration of Rights art. 24 , among other grounds, and requested damages as a result of intentional infliction of emotional distress and negligence. The city and police officers claimed that the curfew ordinance was constitutional and that, even if it were invalid, the defendants were entitled to qualified immunity. The court affirmed the lower court's judgment that the ordinance was unconstitutionally vague because it did not contain sufficient criteria for the juveniles to determine if they were in violation. However, the court held that the lower court erred when it affirmed the trial court's conclusion that the juveniles were not entitled to damages. The court held that Maryland law ordinarily provided no immunity to public officials sued for violating state constitutional rights, and that the lower court erred in upholding the trial court's determination that the juveniles were not entitled to damages.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment of the lower court that held that the juveniles were not entitled to damages from the city and police officers after they enforced an unconstitutionally vague city ordinance by detaining or arresting the juveniles. The court ordered that the lower court remand the case to the trial court for further proceedings.
