Warsame v. State


No. 75, SEPTEMBER TERM, 1994


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


338 Md. 513; 659 A.2d 1271; 1995 Md. LEXIS 77



June 19, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Raymond G. Thieme, Jr., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED, WITH COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland) pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals, seeking review of his conviction for possession of a controlled substance with intent to distribute.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged whether a substance controlled in Maryland by virtue of Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 278(c) remained controlled despite the fact that the substance has never been listed in § 279, the Maryland schedule of controlled dangerous substances. Section 278(c) incorporated, as additional controlled substances, any newly controlled substances designated by federal law. The statute also directed the state agency to republish the list of state-scheduled substances. Defendant was convicted of possession of Cathine, a substance listed on federal schedule and thereby incorporated in the state law. However, the state schedule had not been republished to reflect the addition of Cathine. The court affirmed the conviction, holding that the publication requirement was directive only, and noncompliance with that requirement did not erase the law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Park v. Board of Liquor License Comm'rs


No. 106, September Term, 1994


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


338 Md. 366; 658 A.2d 687; 1995 Md. LEXIS 60



May 26, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Baltimore City). Andre M. Davis, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED. CASE REMANDED TO THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS WITH DIRECTION TO REMAND THE CASE TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY FOR THE ENTRY OF A JUDGEMENT DECLARING CHAPTER 24 OF THE ACTS OF 1992 UNCONSTITUTIONAL AND VOID. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY RESPONDENTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner licensees sought review of a decision from the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) which affirmed a trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of respondent Board of Liquor License Commissioners for Baltimore City. The licensees challenged the constitutionality of Md. Code Ann. art. 2B, § 18A(h) (1957, 1990 Repl. Vol., 1993 Cum. Supp.), requiring that a business with a certain license be considered a tavern for zoning purposes.


OVERVIEW: The licensees all operated liquor sales businesses pursuant to Class B-D-7 licenses issued by the board. Under Md. Code Ann. art. 2B, § 18A (1957, 1990 Repl. Vol., 1993 Cum. Supp.), all Class B-D-7 licensees were required to add on-premises consumption facilities or to obtain a Class A-2 license restricting the hours during which liquor could be sold. The licensees challenged the constitutionality of Md. Code Ann. art. 2B, § 18A(h) (1957, 1990 Repl. Vol., 1993 Cum. Supp.) which required that a business conducted under an A-2 license be considered a tavern for zoning purposes. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the board and the appellate court affirmed that decision. This court reversed the appellate court's decision. Section 18A(h) violated Md. Const. art. XI-A, § 4 because it was a local law concerning zoning, a subject over which the City of Baltimore had been granted express and exclusive legislative authority. Md. Code Ann. art. 2B, § 18A(h) (1957, 1990 Repl. Vol., 1993 Cum. Supp.) was not severable because the legislature would not have enacted § 18A without it. Thus, § 18A was held invalid.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's decision affirming the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of the board. The zoning statute being challenged by the licensees was held to be unconstitutional.

Brown v. County Comm'rs


No. 61, September Term, 1994


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


338 Md. 286; 658 A.2d 255; 1995 Md. LEXIS 57



May 17, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Circuit Court for Carroll County. Raymond E. Beck, Sr. JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR CARROLL COUNTY REVERSED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY RESPONDENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant detainee sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Carroll County (Maryland), which held him personally liable for the costs of medical treatment received while incarcerated.


OVERVIEW: The detainee was required to sign a consent form acknowledging his responsibility for the costs of treatment. At the time his pretrial detention began, however, he was qualified to receive Medicaid benefits. The court held that, for purposes of 42 C.F.R. § 435.1009(b), the detainee was in a public institution for a temporary period pending other arrangements appropriate to his needs; hence, he was not ineligible for Medicaid benefits by reason of his detention. The court further held that Md. Ann. Code art. 87, § 46(c) did not hold prisoners unconditionally and personally liable for the costs of medical treatment but required reimbursement "as appropriate." The court construed the statute to require a county to look to applicable available insurance and Medicaid coverage before pursuing a pretrial detainee personally for the costs of medical care, regardless of whether the detainee had signed a consent form.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that had held the detainee personally liable for treatment costs.

Schaeffer v. Anne Arundel County


No. 76, September Term, 1994


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


338 Md. 75; 656 A.2d 751; 1995 Md. LEXIS 42



April 7, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Eugene M. Lerner, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought to have an ordinace declared void ab initio. Taxpayer appealed from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee county, ruling that laches barred the action.


OVERVIEW: The court issued a writ of certiorari on its own motion to consider the following questions: (1) whether taxpayer's claims were barred by laches; (2) whether the county complied with the notice requirements of the Maryland Constitution, Md. Const. Art. XI-A, § 3; and (3) whether voiding the ordinance would violate the contracts clause of the U.S. Constitution. Taxpayer asserted that laches does not apply when a plaintiff disputes the constitutionality of an ordinance. The court disagreed with taxpayer and noted that defects and irregularities in the mode of enactment of an ordinance do not pertain to the nature of the ordinance itself and such challenges may be precluded by laches. The court found the claim was clearly barred by laches. His claim was filed more than three years after the last possible date of accrual for the action and the claim was susceptible to the general three year statute of limitations. Moreover, the delay prejudiced the party asserting the defense. The court noted that appellee provided enough notice as was required by statute and did not address the federal constitutional issue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Maryland Aggregates Ass'n v. State


No. 40, September Term, 1994


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


337 Md. 658; 655 A.2d 886; 1995 Md. LEXIS 37



March 22, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Genstar Stone Prods. Co. v. Maryland, 514 U.S. 1111, 115 S. Ct. 1965, 131 L. Ed. 2d 856, 1995 U.S. LEXIS 3289 (1995)
Related proceeding at Laurel Sand & Gravel, Inc. v. Philbrick, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 1353 (D. Md., Jan. 3, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Anne Arundel County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. James C. Cawood, Jr. JUDGE.
Maryland Aggregates Ass'n v. State, 1994 Md. LEXIS 143 (Md., Nov. 7, 1994)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mining industry appealed pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), following a grant of summary judgment in favor of defendant State of Maryland and others, and filing of a declaratory judgment that rejected all of the mining industry's constitutional challenges to Md. Nat. Res. Code Ann. 7-6A-10.1 and 7-6A-10.2 (1973, 1989, 1994) (the Act).


OVERVIEW: The mining industry contended that the Act, which related to the appropriation of water in connection with certain surface mining operations violated the Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment to the Federal Constitution and Md. Const. Decl. Rts. art. 24, because there was no rational basis for its enactment. The court disagreed, and found as did the trial court that the question was not whether the General Assembly was correct; it was whether it was entitled to reach the conclusions embodied in the Act. The Act established a compensation scheme for affected landowners that bore a rational relationship to a problem that the General Assembly identified for redress. The Act was not beyond the authority of the General Assembly. Thus the trial court properly granted summary judgment in favor of the state with respect to the mining industry's substantive due process argument. The mining industry further argued that quarries had been unfairly singled out from other large consumers of groundwater in a manner that violated equal protection principles. The court found this argument without merit and concluded that the statute was not constitutionally deficient.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant below of summary judgment in favor of the State of Maryland, and others, and the filing of a declaratory judgment that rejected all of the mining industry's constitutional challenges.

Fogle v. H & G Restaurant


No. 69, September Term, 1994


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


337 Md. 441; 654 A.2d 449; 1995 Md. LEXIS 24; 17 OSHC (BNA) 1099



February 24, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Talbot County). William S. Horne, Judge.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] INTERLOCUTORY INJUNCTION VACATED; CASE REMANDED TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR TALBOT COUNTY FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLEES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commissioner of the Division of Labor and Industry (commissioner) promulgated a rule prohibiting smoking in an enclosed workplace. Plaintiffs, businesses, trade associations, and tobacco companies (challengers), sought declaratory and injunctive relief. The Circuit Court for Talbot County (Maryland) issued an interlocutory injunction temporarily enjoining the enforcement of Md. Regs. Code tit. 09, § 12.23. The state appealed.


OVERVIEW: The commissioner, acting in a quasi-legislative mode, adopted a regulation which was within the boundaries of its rule-making authority. It was not the function of the court to pass upon the wisdom of the regulation, or to approve or disapprove it, because it did not exceed constitutional limits. The court held that (1) the challengers had little likelihood of prevailing on the merits, (2) the commissioner did not exceed his statutory authority in promulgating the regulation, (3) there was abundant scientific evidence in the record to justify the commissioner's conclusion that environmental tobacco smoke (ETS) was a "significant risk" to the health of Maryland employees, and this "significant risk" needed to be regulated by a complete prohibition against smoking in all enclosed workplaces, (4) the commissioner's findings that the economic impact of the regulation on the hospitality industry was minimal were legally sufficient, (5) implied preemption did not occur, (5) the Products Clause did not apply because the federal government had not adopted a specific standard with respect to the health effects of ETS in enclosed workplaces.


OUTCOME: The granting of an interlocutory injunction was an improper exercise of judicial discretion. Accordingly, the interlocutory injunction was vacated and the matter was remanded for trial on the merits.

Tidewater/Havre De Grace v. Mayor & City Council of Havre De Grace

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner marinas sought review of a judgment of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) by writ of certiorari which affirmed the trial court's decision that granted summary judgment in favor of respondents, mayor and city council (city), in the marinas' declaratory judgment action to test the validity of City of Havre de Grace, Md. Ordinance 765 in light of the authority granted to municipalities in Md. Ann. Code art. 24, § 9-605 (Repl. 1994).


OVERVIEW: City of Havre de Grace, Md. Ordinance 765 was passed by the city pursuant to Md. Ann. Code art. 24, § 9-605 (Repl. 1994) that granted the municipality the power to collect a user fee by ordinance on charges for the docking and storage of boats. The appellate court, in reversing a portion of the judgment by the trial court, stated that § 9-605 implicitly placed a clear and affirmative obligation on the marinas to charge and collect the appropriate user tax coincident with the time when the rental fees were collected. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court which upheld the decision of the trial court that granted summary judgment in favor of the city in the declaratory action by the marinas that challenged the validity of a city ordinance. The court assessed costs against the marinas.

Advance Fin. Co. v. Trustees of the Clients' Sec. Trust Fund of the Bar


Misc. No. 8, September Term, 1994


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


337 Md. 195; 652 A.2d 660; 1995 Md. LEXIS 8



January 25, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Exceptions to Clients' Security Trust Fund Decision.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] FINAL DETERMINATION OF THE TRUSTEES DENYING THE CLAIM VACATED; CASE REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS IN ACCORDANCE WITH THIS OPINION; COSTS TO BE PAID BY THE CLIENTS' SECURITY TRUST FUND OF THE BAR OF MARYLAND.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a licensed consumer loan company, filed exceptions under Md. Rule 1228(j)(2) to a determination by defendants, trustees of the Clients' Security Trust Fund of the Bar of Maryland (fund), denying the loan company's claim for loans to personal injury plaintiffs (borrowers) secured by assignments of proceeds of successful claims that were never paid by the borrowers' attorneys (attorneys) to the loan company on the recoveries received.


OVERVIEW: The loan company had obtained judgments against the attorneys and sought collection against the borrowers before it sought reimbursement from the fund for the loans where tort cases were settled and the amount to be paid to the loan company was not remitted by the attorneys. The fund was a court-administered trust under Md. R. 1228 financed by assessments on Maryland lawyers, operated under court rules authorized by Md. Code Ann., Bus. Occ. & Prof. §§ 10-310 - 10-312 (1989). The court found the loss payable by the fund because the attorneys had acted as fiduciaries for the loan company within the meaning of Md. Code Ann. § 10-312(b)(1) and Md. Rule 1228(b)(3) and in accordance with their ethical obligations under Md. Lawyers' R. Prof. Conduct 1.15(b). It was consistent with the purposes of the fund - to maintain the integrity of the legal profession by paying money to reimburse losses caused by defalcations of lawyers - to recognize that the attorneys' fiduciary ethical obligation to a non-client under Rule 1.15(b) was a fiduciary obligation under the Maryland statutes and rules, making the defalcations payable by the fund.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the final determination of the fund denying the claim of the loan company, and the case was remanded for further proceedings in accordance with the court's opinion. Costs were to the fund.

Goldsmith v. State


No. 146, September Term, 1993


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


337 Md. 112; 651 A.2d 866; 1995 Md. LEXIS 5



January 12, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected February 9, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. (Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County). James C. Cawood, Jr., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, charged with sexual offenses against his adopted stepdaughter, challenged the decision of the Court of Special Appeals of Maryland, which affirmed, following conviction, the denial of his pre-trial discovery request for the victim's psychotherapy records maintained by the victim's private psychotherapist.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged of committing sexual child abuse, second degree rape, second and third degree sexual offense, and unnatural and perverted sexual practices on his adopted stepdaughter. Defendant sought to obtain pre-trial discovery review of the victim's psychotherapy records maintained by the victim's private psychotherapist. The trial court denied his request and the court of special appeals affirmed that decision, following defendant's conviction. On appeal, defendant contended that he had a right to the records under Md. R. 4-264 and the Maryland and United States Constitution. The court affirmed the lower courts, holding that Rule 4-264 precluded pre-trial discovery of a victim's privileged psychotherapist-patient records. In addition, neither due process, compulsory process, nor the right to confront adverse witnesses established a pre-trial right of defendant to discovery review of his stepdaughter's privileged psychotherapy records. Finally, defendant failed to establish the requisite need to warrant a judge ordering disclosure of the privileged information at trial. Thus, both the denial of pre-trial discovery and the conviction were proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of defendant's request for pretrial discovery. The court also affirmed defendant's conviction for sexual offenses.

State v. Mazzone


No. 6, September Term, 1994


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


336 Md. 379; 648 A.2d 978; 1994 Md. LEXIS 137



October 24, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected November 25, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Baltimore County). John Grason Turnbull II, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS VACATED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT FOR FURTHER APPELLATE PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION TO DETERMINE THE MERITS OF OTHER ISSUES RAISED ON APPEAL BUT NOT DECIDED BY THAT COURT. COSTS TO BE PAID BY BALTIMORE COUNTY, MARYLAND.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), the state challenged a judgment that reversed defendant husband's conviction for drug conspiracy on the grounds that the minimization guidelines for an electronic wiretap allowed law enforcement agents to purposefully intercept privileged marital communications in violation of Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 9-105.


OVERVIEW: The State of Maryland challenged a judgment that reversed defendant husband's drug-conspiracy convictions because the minimization guidelines for an electronic wiretap improperly authorized the interception of privileged marital communications. The state argued that the trial court properly admitted into evidence the contents of the intercepted conversations, including two conversations between the husband and his wife. The appeals court held that a judge could not authorize police to purposefully intercept privileged marital communications. While agreeing with the appeals court's decision to reverse the convictions, the appellate court disagreed with its rationale. The appellate court held that the rationale ran afoul of a basic principle of statutory construction by giving the marital communications privilege, codified in Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 9-105, greater effect than the words of the statute supported. Because the maximum sanction to be imposed was suppression of the conversations that were unreasonably intercepted, the appellate court remanded for a new trial in the event that other issues raised but not decided by the appeals court were without merit.


OUTCOME: In affirming the judgment reversing the convictions, the court held that the improper admission of defendant husband's two marital communications into evidence required only that the case be remanded for a new trial in which the illegally intercepted communications could not be used. The court remanded for such new trial in the event that other issues raised by defendant and not decided by the appeals court were found to be without merit.

Luppino v. Gray


No. 115, SEPTEMBER TERM, 1993


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


336 Md. 194; 647 A.2d 429; 1994 Md. LEXIS 121



September 13, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Prince George's County). James P. Salmon, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED, WITH COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent buyers filed a lawsuit against petitioner seller for fraud, intentional concealment, and negligent misrepresentation because of earlier repairs and adverse conditions in the home. The jury in the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland) awarded respondents compensatory and punitive damages. Petitioner's motion for directed verdict, remittitur, or new trial was denied. The appeals court affirmed. Petitioner sought review.


OVERVIEW: The seller argued that he was erroneously deprived of his constitutional right to a nonjury trial and that the trial judge erroneously allowed the case to proceed to a jury. He contended that the waiver of a jury trial was the same as affirmatively agreeing to a court trial. The buyers contended that the seller waived his right to a nonjury trial because he failed to assert that right in the trial court. The court affirmed the decisions of the lower courts. The court held that Md. Const. art. IV, § 8(a), conferred a constitutional right on both parties in civil litigation to elect a nonjury trial, but that it did not confer a constitutional right to a nonjury trial on individual civil litigants. Section 8(a) required an agreement between the seller and the buyers. The seller's waiver of the constitutional right to a jury trial did not amount to an agreement among the parties to proceed without the aid of a jury. The waiver of a jury trial pursuant to Md. Ct. R. 4-325(b) did not trigger § 8(a).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the buyers for compensatory and punitive damages.

Ayers v. State


No. 84, SEPTEMBER TERM, 1993


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected July 25, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Montgomery County) L. Leonard Ruben, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AS TO THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR MONTGOMERY COUNTY UPON THE COUNT OF THE INDICTMENT CHARGING CONSPIRACY TO COMMIT A RACIALLY MOTIVATED CRIME UPON MYRTLE GUILLORY: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; AS TO THE JUDGMENT ON THE COUNT OF THE INDICTMENT CHARGING ASSAULT WITH INTENT TO MAIM JOHNNIE MAE McCRAE: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; AS TO THE JUDGMENT ON THE COUNT OF THE INDICTMENT CHARGING KIDNAPPING OF JOHNNIE MAE McCRAE: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; AS TO THE COUNT OF THE INDICTMENT CHARGING THE COMMISSION OF A RACIALLY MOTIVATED CRIME UPON JOHNNIE MAE McCRAE IN VIOLATION OF ARTICLE 27, § 470A: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY THE APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland), in which he was found guilty of and sentenced for assault, assault with intent to maim, kidnapping, conspiracy to commit a racially motivated crime, and committing a racially motivated crime in violation of a hate crimes statute.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and a friend attacked two minority women because of their race. Defendant battered one of the women and sprayed lighter fluid on her. The court held that the indictment contained no count based on harassment, but only conspiracy to commit and committing a racially motivated crime. The court held that there was no evidence that defendant engaged in any semblance of constitutionally protected speech or conduct directed at the victims which was considered by the jury in its determination of guilt. Defendant lacked standing to challenge the hate crimes statute facially on the basis that its harassment prong was vague and overbroad. The testimony of one of the women supported the evidence given by the other attacker and established that defendant's acts were racially motivated. A prior racial incident that was the catalyst for the attacks was properly admitted because its probative value outweighed its prejudicial impact. The sentences imposed for the crimes of assault with intent to maim, kidnapping, and committing a racially motivated crime were not grossly disproportionate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions and sentence and assessed costs on appeal against defendant.

Christ v. Md. Dep't of Natural Res.


No. 136, September Term, 1992


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


335 Md. 427; 644 A.2d 34; 1994 Md. LEXIS 94



July 14, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore County pursuant to certiorari to Court of Special Appeals. Edward A. DeWaters, Jr., JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE COUNTY VACATED, AND CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT FOR THE ENTRY OF A DECLARATORY JUDGMENT IN ACCORDANCE WITH THIS OPINION. APPELLANT TO PAY COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff father on behalf of minor appealed a decision from the Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland), which dismissed plaintiff's action against defendant Department of Natural Resources that sought declaratory judgment that Md. Regs. Code tit. 08, § 18.02.05A was invalid and a permanent injunction against its enforcement.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff father on behalf of minor sought a declaratory judgment that Md. Regs. Code tit. 08, § 18.02.05A was invalid and a permanent injunction against the enforcement of the regulation. Defendant department filed a motion for summary judgment, contending that the regulation was valid. The lower court rejected plaintiff's arguments, holding that defendant had not acted in an unconstitutional manner or exceeded its statutory authority and dismissed the case. Plaintiff appealed and the court issued a writ of certiorari prior to argument in the appellate court. The court agreed with the lower court's conclusions concerning the validity of the regulation but vacated the judgment dismissing the case. The court held that the lower court's rejection of plaintiff's position on the merits furnished no ground for dismissal. The court held that where a lower court erroneously dismissed a declaratory judgment action, the dismissal must be vacated and an appropriate declaratory judgment entered. The court held that § 18.02.05A was authorized by the general assembly.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment from the lower court that dismissed plaintiff father's complaint and remanded the case to the lower court for the entry of a declaratory judgment in accordance with the court's opinion. The court held that a regulation prohibiting children under 14 from operating a particularly dangerous type of motor vessel on public waters was a reasonable regulation to promote the statutory purpose of boating safety.

 

94 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Cardinell v. State


No. 32, September Term, 1992


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


335 Md. 381; 644 A.2d 11; 1994 Md. LEXIS 93



July 14, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Garrett County). Fred A. Thayer, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED, WITH COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought certiorari review of a judgment of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), reversing a trial court judgment that granted defendant's "supplemental" motion for revision of sentence, filed seven months after sentence was imposed. The trial court had ordered that execution of the unserved portion of the sentence be suspended and that defendant be placed on supervised probation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to drug charges and was sentenced to imprisonment for three years. Her timely motion for revision of sentence was denied, but the court granted defendant's "supplemental" motion for revision. Two days later, the State filed an answer to defendant's motion, arguing that the court had no jurisdiction to entertain the motion. The State appealed to the intermediate appellate court, which held that the trial court acted in excess of its jurisdiction, that the State was entitled to appeal, and that the trial court's order modifying the sentence must be vacated. The court held that the lower court was clearly without authority to modify defendant's sentence when it did so. The applicable rule provided that, although an illegal sentence could be corrected at any time, the court could otherwise alter a sentence only within 90 days after its imposition. The court further noted that although the State did not have a statutory right to appeal, the appeal would lie pursuant to the common law principle that the State had a right to appeal an action that was outside the lower court's jurisdiction, a principle that had not been abolished by the legislature.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was affirmed.

 

95 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Outmezguine v. State


No. 112, SEPTEMBER TERM, 1993


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


335 Md. 20; 641 A.2d 870; 1994 Md. LEXIS 72; 42 A.L.R.5th 835



June 3, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Montgomery County). James L. Ryan, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED, WITH COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which affirmed his conviction for unlawfully photographing a minor engaging in sexual conduct, in violation of Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 419A(c) (1957, 1992 Repl. Vol.).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for taking photographs of a 15-year-old engaged in sexual conduct. At trial, defendant claimed that he did not take the photographs or, in the alternative, did not know that the subject was a minor. It was not unconstitutional for Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 419A(c) (1957, 1992 Repl. Vol.) to operate as a strict liability crime. Knowledge of the minor's age was not an element of the offense and a reasonable mistake of age was not available as a defense. The strict liability child pornography statute did not have an impermissible chilling effect on the freedom of expression guaranteed by the First Amendment because the state's interest in protecting children outweighed the individual's right to produce nonobscene adult pornography. The statute's scienter requirement referred to knowledge of the nature and character of the material produced, not to the knowledge of the subject's age.


OUTCOME: The conviction for unlawfully photographing a minor engaged in sexual conduct was affirmed.

 

96 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Minor v. State


No. 87, September Term, 1993


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


334 Md. 707; 641 A.2d 214; 1994 Md. LEXIS 69



May 13, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Raymond G. Thieme, Jr., JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY THE APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction by the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland) on drug possession charges.


OVERVIEW: A police officer suspected that defendant was involved in the theft of motorcycles and obtained a search warrant to search for serial number plates and other items in defendant's home. During the search, the police found drugs and drug paraphernalia. Defendant was convicted on drug possession charges. Upon appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the officer who obtained the warrant would not have known that her affidavit failed to establish probable cause and that she should not have applied for the warrant. Thus, the officer had no duty to second guess the judge. The court found the officer presented the information received and the extent of her confirmatory investigation to a circuit court judge and was not obliged to withhold applying for the warrant. The court found that a reasonably well-trained officer would not have known that a judge should conclude that her investigation failed to satisfy the statutory requirements for a warrant, and thus her good-faith reliance on the warrant was therefore justified.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for drug possession based on a search warrant to search for evidence of theft, which was executed in good faith.

 

97 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Controller, Anne Arundel County v. Pleasure Cove Yacht Club


No. 17, September Term, 1993


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


334 Md. 450; 639 A.2d 685; 1994 Md. LEXIS 57



April 14, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Bruce C. Williams, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY AFFIRMED. ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY TO PAY COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Controller, Anne Arundel County, Md. (county), challenged the decision of the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland), which held that under the "boat slip tax," Anne Arundel County, Md., Code § 7-405(b), forklift and other marina services were not taxable. Before the court of special appeals heard the case, appellee taxpayer filed a petition for a writ of certiorari which was granted.


OVERVIEW: Md. Ann. Code art. 24, § 9-602 (1957) authorized the county to tax space rentals. The county enacted Anne Arundel County, Md., Code § 7-405(b), known as the "boat slip tax." The taxpayer, a yacht club, was assessed a tax deficiency for marina services charges under the boat slip tax and a penalty. The circuit court held that under the plain meaning of the ordinance, forklift and other marina services were not taxable. Pursuant to a writ of certiorari, the court affirmed the circuit court's judgment. Under strict construction of the statute, the court held that the county was authorized to levy a tax on space rentals, but not on other marina services, when the charge for the space rental was set forth separately from the charge for other marina services. The boat slip tax was not a general retail sales tax. The marina services were not inherently necessary to the wet slip, outside rack, or boatel rentals. The county's own regulations and guidelines, which seemed to exempt the use of the forklift and other marina services from the boat slip tax, were given deference as an administrative interpretation of the state enabling act and the county ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court, which held that consideration for marina services were not taxable under the county "boat slip tax." The county was ordered to pay costs.

Bundy v. State


No. 69, September Term, 1993


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


334 Md. 131; 638 A.2d 84; 1994 Md. LEXIS 38



March 14, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. (Circuit Court for Baltimore City). Richard T. Rombro, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO VACATE THE CONVICTION AND REMAND TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY FOR A NEW TRIAL. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY THE MAYOR AND CITY COUNCIL OF BALTIMORE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), on certiorari, which affirmed the judgment of the circuit court that convicted defendant of theft of goods.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's petition for a writ of certiorari was granted to consider whether defendant adequately preserved for appellate review his contention that the trial judge erroneously permitted the state to exercise more than four peremptory challenges. The intermediate appellate court held that the state was entitled to only four peremptory challenges in the consolidated trial of defendant and a codefendant but found that defendant's objection was not timely made; thus the peremptory challenge issue was not properly preserved for appellate review. Defendant disputed that conclusion, contending that his objection was timely and that, since the state exceeded the permitted number of peremptory challenges, his conviction should be reversed. The court held that the record sufficiently indicated that defense counsel's statement put the trial judge on notice of her complaint that the state just exceeded its allotted number of peremptory challenges. The court ruled that defendant was entitled to a retrial because the trial judge had opined that dismissal of the panel should be the remedy if the state had exercised two excess peremptory challenges, and the state had done so.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the court of special appeals and remanded to that court with instructions to vacate the conviction and remand to the circuit court for a new trial. The mayor and the city were ordered equally ordered to pay costs in the court and in the court of special appeals.

Curran v. Price


No. 76, September Term, 1993


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


334 Md. 149; 638 A.2d 93; 1994 Md. LEXIS 39



March 14, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County).



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY VACATED; CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO DISMISS THE ACTION AGAINST RONALD PRICE AS NOT AUTHORIZED BY § 764 OF ARTICLE 27. COSTS TO BE PAID BY THE STATE OF MARYLAND.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, Attorney General of Maryland, challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland) which denied an injunction against respondent and declared Maryland's "Son of Sam" law, Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 764 (1957, 1992 Repl. Vol. and 1993 Cum. Supp.) unconstitutional. The Attorney General contended that it was constitutional to require the respondent to submit any "notoriety of crimes" contract for review.


OVERVIEW: The respondent, indicted for sexual child abuse, appeared on television talk shows and announced that he had contracted to sell his life story. The Attorney General requested an injunction requiring the respondent to submit any contract to him for review under Maryland's "Son of Sam" law, Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 764 (1957, 1992 Repl. Vol. and 1993 Cum. Supp.). The trial court denied the request for injunctive relief and declared § 764 unconstitutional on First Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. I, grounds, and the state appealed. On appeal, the court vacated the judgment and remanded with directions to dismiss the action as not authorized by § 764. The court declined to reach the merits of the question of § 764's constitutionality because it was unnecessary to do so. The court held that the suit was not authorized by § 764 because the law only required persons entering into suspected "notoriety of crimes" contracts with a defendant to submit those contracts to the Attorney General for review, not the defendants themselves.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment holding Maryland's "Son of Sam" law unconstitutional and remanded with directions to dismiss the action against respondent because it was not authorized by the "Son of Sam" law as the statute did not require a defendant to submit a suspected "notoriety of crimes" contract to the Attorney General.

Shepter v. Johns Hopkins Univ.


No. 63, September Term, 1993


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


334 Md. 82; 637 A.2d 1223; 1994 Md. LEXIS 37



March 11, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore City pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. Joseph H. H. Kaplan, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: THE APPEAL FROM THE ORDER OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY DISMISSING COUNT III OF THE APPELLANTS' AMENDED COUNTERCLAIM AND THIRD-PARTY COMPLAINT IS DISMISSED. IN ALL OTHER RESPECTS THE JUDGMENTS OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY ARE AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY THE APPELLANTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, relatives of the settlors of an inter vivos trust, challenged the order of the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland) that dismissed their counterclaim against appellee, trustee and owner of a remainder interest in an inter vivos trust, which alleged that appellee subjected the trust to significant taxes and granted appellee's motion for summary judgment in claim against appellants for apportionment of estate taxes and interest.


OVERVIEW: Appellee, trustee and owner of a remainder interest in an inter vivos trust, filed claim in circuit court against appellants, relatives of the settlors of an inter vivos trust, who had a lifetime interest in the trust annuity, for apportionment under Md. Code Ann., Tax-Gen. § 7-308 (1988, 1993 Cum. Supp.) of federal estate taxes and interest that were collected from appellee at the death of the trust's surviving settlor following probate of the settlor's estate in orphans' court. Appellants filed a counterclaim, alleging that appellee breached a duty to them by subjecting the trust to significant taxes. The circuit court dismissed the counterclaim and granted appellee's motion for summary judgment against the settlor's son and personal representative for part of the tax and interest. The court affirmed, rejecting appellants' contention that § 7-308 vested exclusive jurisdiction over apportionment in the orphans' courts. It was held that concurrent jurisdiction existed between the circuit courts and the orphans' courts over tax apportionment claims. The court concluded that appellants failed to allege how appellee's actions resulted in a substantial increase in estate taxes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's order which dismissed the counterclaim filed by appellants, relatives of the settlors of an inter vivos trust, and granted summary judgment to appellee, trustee and owner of a remainder interest in an inter vivos trust, in appellee's action for apportionment of estate taxes and interest because appellants failed to prove that appellee's actions resulted in an increase in estate taxes.

Verzi v. Baltimore County


No. 47, September Term, 1993


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


333 Md. 411; 635 A.2d 967; 1994 Md. LEXIS 14



January 17, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore County pursuant to certiorari to Court of Special Appeals. J. Norris Byrnes, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE COUNTY REVERSED; CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT FOR THE ENTRY OF A JUDGMENT DECLARING THE LOCATION REQUIREMENT OF SECTION 24-230 OF THE BALTIMORE COUNTY CODE INVALID AND FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS NOT INCONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION; COSTS TO BE PAID BY BALTIMORE COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the owner of a towing service, sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland) awarding summary judgment to defendant county in an action challenging the constitutionality of a location requirement.


OVERVIEW: The owner of a towing service filed an action against the county, seeking a declaratory judgment that a location requirement in the county code was unconstitutional. The owner sought a writ of mandamus ordering the county to assign him a tow area and to call him in the event that a tow operator was needed in his area. The location requirement mandated that a licensed tow operator have a place of business within the county before that operator could be called by police to tow vehicles that were disabled by accidents. The trial court awarded summary judgment to the county. On appeal, the court reversed, finding that the location requirement was wholly unrelated to any legitimate government objective and that it violated the equal protection guarantees of the Maryland Constitution. Because the court could find no rational basis for the distinction between in-county and out-of-county towers, it was led to the probable view that the classification was intended to confer the monopoly of a profitable business upon residents of the town. The court held that the county was not free to make arbitrary distinctions based upon whether a licensee's premises were located within the county.


OUTCOME: The order awarding summary judgment to the county was reversed and the case was remanded for the entry of a judgment declaring the location requirement invalid.

Bailey v. Maryland State Dep't of Pub. Safety & Correctional Servs.


No. 41, September Term, 1993


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


333 Md. 397; 635 A.2d 432; 1994 Md. LEXIS 8; 145 L.R.R.M. 2606



January 13, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to Court of Special Appeals. (Circuit Court for Baltimore County) J. William Hinkel, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO REMAND THE CASE TO THE ADMINISTRATIVE AGENCY FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY RESPONDENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff correctional officer appealed a decision of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which denied him the right, as a supervisory employee of defendant Maryland State Department of Public Safety and Correctional Services (department), to represent other state employees in grievance proceedings against the state.


OVERVIEW: After being promoted to a supervisory position, the correctional officer was prohibited from continuing to represent fellow employees in various grievance proceedings. The officer challenged the direct order under Md. Ann. Code of 1957 art. 64A, § 53(b). An administrative law judge (ALJ) concluded that § 53(b), which provided that an employee with a grievance could be represented by any person or persons of his choice, held that the officer did not have standing to use that section. The trial court reversed, finding that § 53(b) placed no limitations on "management representation." The appellate court reversed, holding that the officer lacked standing because he was not an aggrieved party. The court granted certiorari and reversed, holding that the officer was an aggrieved party within the meaning of § 52 and § 53(b), and therefore possessed standing to challenge the ALJ's decision. Because the per se restriction was an unreasonable interpretation of the statute's objectives, the ALJ's decision concerning this issue was arbitrary and capricious. As no evidence of an actual conflict of interest was presented, the court would not deem one to exist as a matter of law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court that had been entered in favor of the department and remanded for further proceedings.

Coalition for Open Doors v. Annapolis Lodge No. 622

York Roofing v. Adcock


No. 27, September Term, 1993


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


333 Md. 158; 634 A.2d 39; 1993 Md. LEXIS 176



December 10, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals. (Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County). Warren B. Duckett, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONERS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner lienors sought to overturn the judgment of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which held that respondent owners were not subject to mechanics' liens that were filed by the lienors. The appellate court had affirmed the judgment of a circuit court.


OVERVIEW: The owners entered into a contract to purchase a building before the lienors filed notices of intent to file mechanics' liens. Previously, the lienors had made improvements on the property that the owners purchased. The circuit court found that the owners were not aware of the unpaid obligations when they entered into the contract to purchase the property. The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court and held that following the contractual agreement, the owners had equitable title to the property and that it was not subject to a lien pursuant to Md. Code Ann., Real Prop. § 9-105(a) (1974, 1988 Repl.). The court also ruled that, under Md. Code Ann., Real Prop. § 9-101 (1974, 1988 Repl.), the owners were not subject to a mechanics' lien because the owners had not entered into a contract with the lienors. The court further ruled that because the lienors had never established a lien prior to the creation of the owners' equitable title, the owners' equitable title was insulated from any lien of judgment even if the owners had been aware of the lienors' claims when they agreed to purchase the property.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court, which held that the lienors did not possess valid mechanics' liens against the owners of a building.

OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged a decision affirming a finding that he was guilty of distribution of cocaine and heroin. OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for distribution of cocaine and heroin because a judge did not abuse his discretion in refusing to ask a question not addressing a potential ground for disqualification. The judge did not err in permitting the state to make a missing witness argument.

Epps v. State


No. 35, September Term, 1993


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


333 Md. 121; 634 A.2d 20; 1993 Md. LEXIS 170



December 6, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Somerset Co.). Richard D. Warren, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED IN PART; CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO VACATE THE SENTENCE AND REMAND THE CASE FOR RESENTENCING. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY SOMERSET COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought a writ of certiorari from the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which affirmed defendant's conviction entered by the circuit court for battery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was an inmate in the segregation unit. Defendant had previously been convicted for assaulting a guard with a wire instrument. When a guard was walking past his cell, a liquid, presumed to be water, was squirted on the guard. The guard claimed that defendant admitted that he had squirted the water. Defendant denied the incident. Defendant was convicted of assault, and was sentenced to 20 years, consecutive to his existing sentence. Defendant appealed, and argued that the sentence was disproportionate, in violation of the Eighth Amendment. The appellate court affirmed the conviction. Defendant sought certiorari. The court granted certiorari, affirmed the conviction, reversed the sentence, and remanded. The court held that perfect proportionality among sentences was not required, but that gross disproportionality was prohibited. The court held that in reviewing proportionality, it looked at the specific facts of the crime charged, not the elements of the offense. The court held that throwing a small amount of water on someone was at the low end of the spectrum of assaultive behavior. The court held that the sentence was grossly disproportionate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part the appellate court's judgment affirming the trial court's conviction of defendant for battery, but reversed the appellate court's judgment affirming the trial court's sentence. The case was remanded to the trial court for resentencing.

Thomas v. State


No. 20, September Term, 1992


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


333 Md. 84; 634 A.2d 1; 1993 Md. LEXIS 172



December 6, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied January 11, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Caroline County pursuant to certiorari to Court of Special Appeals. J. Owen Wise, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE OF 20 YEARS FOR BATTERY OF APRIL 2 VACATED, AND CASE REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING ON THAT COUNT; REMAINDER OF JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR CAROLINE COUNTY AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY CAROLINE COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his convictions and sentences for two counts of common law battery, reckless endangerment, unlawful use of a telephone, and violation of an order to vacate the family home by the Circuit Court for Caroline County (Maryland).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of two counts of common law battery, reckless endangerment, unlawful use of a telephone, and violation of an order to vacate the family home, and sentenced to a total of 50 years and 8 months. On appeal, the court vacated a 20 year sentence for one of the battery convictions, but affirmed the remainder of the judgment. The court held that the sentence was disproportionate to the crime. The court held that the battery consisted of a slap to his wife's face which did not result in any lasting physical injury, and thus could not be considered legally serious. The court held that the sentence was not the result of a recidivist history, and was not based on any legislative or judicial decision to impose severe penalties to deter domestic violence. The court held that the sentence was based on speculation by the trial judge concerning the life span of the victim.


OUTCOME: The court vacated a 20 year sentence imposed on defendant for a one conviction for common law battery, but affirmed the remaining sentences and convictions for a second common law battery, reckless endangerment, unlawful use of a telephone, and violation of an order to vacate the family home. The court held that the 20 year sentence was disproportionate to the crime because the slap did not result in any lasting physical injury.

 

108 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Garnett v. State


No. 3 September Term, 1993


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


332 Md. 571; 632 A.2d 797; 1993 Md. LEXIS 162



November 12, 1993, Decided  
November 12, 1993, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] JUDGMENT AFFIRMED, WITH COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland) convicted defendant for second-degree rape of a victim in violation of Md. Code Ann. art. 27, § 463(1957, 1992 repl. vol.) and excluded as immaterial evidence that defendant was told the victim was at the age of consent. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a 20-year old young retarded male who previously met the victim, who was 13 years old, and talked with her occasionally by telephone. He approached the victim's house, and she opened her bedroom window and directed him to use a ladder to climb up the window. The two talked, engaged in sexual intercourse, and remained in the bedroom for more than seven hours before defendant departed therefrom. Defendant alleged that the victim previously represented that she was 16 years old and that he had acted with such belief, and there was no mens rea and reasonable mistake of fact; the state alleged that Md. Code Ann. art. 27, § 463(a)(3) was a strict liability offense. The court held (1) the second degree rape statute, § 463(a)(3), was a strict liability offense that did not require the state to prove mens rea; (2) as such, defendant was guilty of the second degree rape by engaging in sexual intercourse with the victim, who was under fourteen years of age and four years his junior; and (3) the mistake-of-age defense was not allowable under § 463(a)(3), which made no reference to defendant's knowledge, belief, or other state of mind.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment of conviction because defendant could not make a mistake of fact defense to a strict liability offense.

Johnson v. State


No. 141, September Term, 1992


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


332 Md. 456; 632 A.2d 152; 1993 Md. LEXIS 155



October 29, 1993, Decided  
October 29, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County). Martin A. Wolff, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH INSTRUCTIONS TO REMAND TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY FOR A NEW TRIAL. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY THE ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with rape and presented the defense that the victim was exchanging sex for money. Defendant challenged his conviction, claiming that the trial court had improperly excluded evidence. The Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) affirmed the order that denied defendant's motion to admit evidence that the victim had previously engaged in sexual conduct for money. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal of his rape conviction, defendant sought to prove that the victim's allegations of rape were a vindictive response to not receiving drugs in return for sexual relations. The prosecution argued that evidence of the victim's past sexual activities was prejudicial and barred under the rape shield statute, Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 461(a) (1957). The court rejected the prosecution's argument, holding that the probative value of the evidence substantially outweighed its potential for unfair prejudice. The court found that the evidence related to a direct matter that would not obscure the issues and confuse the jury. The court reasoned that there was a close connection between the sexual conduct evidence and defendant's defense. Defendant sought to show the victim's motive for accusing him of rape. Further, the court found that there was little danger that the evidence would be misused by the jury. Finally, the court found that the evidence was necessary to defendant's defense. The court reasoned that the central focus of the case was the very issue to which the contested evidence related.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that upheld the denial of defendant's motion to admit evidence that the victim had previously engaged in sexual conduct for money. The case was remanded for a new trial.

Thanos v. State


No. 91, September Term, 1993


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


332 Md. 511; 632 A.2d 768; 1993 Md. LEXIS 161



October 27, 1993, Per Curiam Order; November 10, 1993, Opinion, Decided  
November 10, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Frederick A. Thayer, III, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: APPEAL DISMISSED, COSTS TO BE PAID BY BALTIMORE COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder and sentenced to death. The Circuit Court for Garrett County (Maryland) found that defendant waived his rights to an automatic stay under Md. Code Ann. art. 27, § 645A(a) (1957) and review of his sentence. An appeal was filed in defendant's name.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was convicted, he told his attorney that he did not want to pursue further litigation. The attorney was discharged. The trial court granted the state's motion for a hearing regarding defendant's waiver of further review proceedings. The court determined that defendant was competent to waive further proceedings. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. It held that the trial court's finding that defendant was competent to make decisions concerning the discharge of his attorneys and the pursuit of additional legal proceedings was amply supported by the evidence. Defendant could not waive the 240-day stay of execution under § 645A(a) because the legislature intended the stay to be mandatory. If defendant did not desire to file a petition for post-conviction relief, the trial judge could issue a death warrant for a time beyond the period of the stay.


OUTCOME: The appeal had to be dismissed because defendant discharged his attorney and determined that no further appeal was to be taken.

Forman v. Motor Vehicle Admin.

September 16, 1993, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Circuit Court for Howard County. Cornelius F. Sybert, Jr., JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR HOWARD COUNTY REVERSED, AND CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO REVERSE THE DECISION OF THE MOTOR VEHICLE ADMINISTRATION AND REMAND THE CASE TO THE ADMINISTRATIVE LAW JUDGE FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS TO BE PAID BY THE RESPONDENT, THE MOTOR VEHICLE ADMINISTRATION.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner driver challenged the judgment, by writ of certiorari, of the Circuit Court for Howard County (Maryland), which affirmed the decision of respondent Motor Vehicle Administration that gave the driver a 120-day suspension of her driver's license for her refusal to take the breathalyzer test pursuant to Md. Code Transp. § 16-205.1 (1992 Repl.Vol.).


OVERVIEW: The driver's operator's license was suspended by the Motor Vehicle Administration (MVA) for 120 days after the driver refused to take a breathalyzer test when she was stopped for allegedly driving while intoxicated. The driver filed for review and the decision was affirmed. The driver appealed that decision, alleging that the officer induced her to refuse the test and that the administrative law judge improperly refused her request to subpoena the detaining officer. The court reversed the decision of the MVA and determined that an officer's negation of previously and properly given advice of right could have violated the licensee's due process rights. The court also stated that without findings of fact on all material issues and without a clear statement of the rationale behind the administrative law judge's action, a reviewing court was unable to properly perform its function. The court held that a remand was necessary because the administrative law judge failed to make adequate factual findings and he failed to explain his ultimate decision.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the MVA and remanded the cause for further findings of fact regarding the driver's suspension of her license.

Richardson v. State


No. 153, September Term, 1991


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


332 Md. 94; 630 A.2d 238; 1993 Md. LEXIS 140



September 10, 1993, Decided  
September 10, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to Court of Special Appeals. (Circuit Court for Baltimore County). William M. Nickerson, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED, WITH COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which affirmed his conviction for robbery and murder, and sentenced him to life with possibility of parole on the murder count and an additional sentence of 20 years imprisonment consecutive to the life sentence, as a result of the conviction of robbery with a deadly weapon.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended, among other things, that the trial judge erred in refusing to strike the state's motion of intent to seek the death penalty and in refusing to grant his motion for judgment of acquittal made during the sentencing proceeding. The court affirmed. The court found that what defendant sought by his motions to strike the state's notice of intention to seek a sentence of death was the entry of summary judgment on the issue of mental retardation and, because summary judgment did not exist in criminal procedure, the motions were properly denied. The court also found that a defendant who was given a life sentence because he was not eligible for the imposition of the death penalty faced a limitation of 15 years before consideration for parole. The court concluded, however, that although its interpretation of the applicable statute benefited defendant by determining the computation that had to be made with respect to his life sentence when his eligibility for parole consideration was calculated, it did not affect the judgments entered below.


OUTCOME: Convictions and sentences for robbery and murder were affirmed.

 

113 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sheldon


No. 9, September Term, 1993


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


332 Md. 45; 629 A.2d 753; 1993 Md. LEXIS 139



August 27, 1993, Decided  
August 27, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to Court of Special Appeals. (Circuit Court for Prince George's County), James P. Salmon, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED, WITH COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed orders from the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which granted defendants' motion to dismiss the indictments against them for burning crosses without obtaining permission from the property owners and the local fire department, in violation of Md. Code Ann. art. 27, § 10A (1957, 1992 Repl.), as violative of the First Amendment.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that the burning of a cross denoted conduct as opposed to speech, but that the act was sufficiently expressive to qualify for First Amendment protection. On appeal of the dismissal of defendants' indictments, the court affirmed that case law established that the act was speech within the contemplation of the First Amendment. The court affirmed that Md. Code Ann. art. 27, § 10A was a content-based regulation of speech and subject to strict scrutiny. The court rejected the state's assertion that the statutory purpose was to protect property owners from unwanted fires and to safeguard the community because other criminal statutes adequately provided for those legitimate state interests. The court noted that the legislative history of the cross-burning law revealed that the purpose of the statute was to express disagreement with the act's inherent expression. The court affirmed that the law fell within no doctrinal exceptions that exempted it from the First Amendment. The court held that Md. Code Ann. art. 27, § 10A was not necessary for the state's effort to foster racial and religious accord, and therefore did not survive strict scrutiny.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's determination that the cross-burning law was constitutionally invalid, and affirmed the dismissal of the indictments against defendants.

Legislative Redistricting Cases


Misc. No. 37, September Term, 1991; Misc. Nos. 1, 5, 6, 16, 17, and 19, September Term, 1992


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


331 Md. 574; 629 A.2d 646; 1993 Md. LEXIS 128



August 24, 1993  
August 24, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected September 21, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petitions to review the 1992 Legislative Districting Plan for the State of Maryland. Marvin Smith, Special Master, JUDGE


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner citizens filed for review of a legislative redistricting plan enacted by respondent State of Maryland under the Md. Const. art. III, § 5, claiming that the plan violated among other things, the Voting Rights Act, 42 U.S.C.S. § 1971 et seq., (1993), notice requirements, and partisan gerrymandering requirements. A special master appointed by the court found no merit in any of the citizens' contentions.


OVERVIEW: In accordance with his constitutional duty under the Md. Const. art. III, §§ 2-5, the governor of Maryland, upon receiving the results of the 1990 census, undertook to develop a redistricting plan for the Maryland General Assembly. He appointed a five-member advisory committee to assist him. The committee submitted a plan and acknowledged that the following criteria constrained its decisions: equality of population between districts, minority representation, compactness, contiguity, and respect for natural boundaries and the boundaries of political subdivisions. The court held that public notices for hearings as to the redistricting plan were sufficient and that the governor did not have a statutory or constitutional obligation to be present at the final hearing of the redistricting process. The court further held that the redistricting plan adequately described the districts created and that one district in particular satisfied the constitutional compactness requirement. Additionally, the court held that the plan fell within the 10 percent flexibility rule of the "one person, one vote" requirement and that the plan did not violate the Voting Rights Act.


OUTCOME: The court denied the citizens' petitions.

 

115 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Fairbanks v. State


No. 150, September Term, 1991


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


331 Md. 482; 629 A.2d 63; 1993 Md. LEXIS 125



August 20, 1993  
August 20, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Certiorari to Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Baltimore County). Alfred L. Brennan, Sr., JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED, WITH COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision of the Court of Special Appeals, Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland), which held that defendant was not entitled to collaterally attack the constitutionality of a facially valid prior conviction during his sentencing hearing under a recidivist statute. Certiorari review was granted.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged that his prior conviction relied on by the State in order to enhance his sentence was constitutionally infirm because the State failed to show that he intelligently waived his right to trial by jury. The record disclosed that defendant was represented by counsel at the time of the prior conviction. The State contended that defendant was not entitled to collaterally attack the validity of the prior conviction during the sentencing proceeding because he was previously represented by counsel, and if defendant was allowed to raise the issue during the sentencing proceeding, the burden of proof was upon defendant to demonstrate the constitutional deficiency claimed. The court held that collateral challenges to the constitutional validity of a facially valid predicate conviction could not be raised at a sentencing hearing. The fact that defendant was properly represented by counsel during the prior conviction raised a strong presumption of regularity and satisfied the facial validity of the prior conviction. The State met its burden of proof beyond a reasonable doubt by providing a properly authenticated record of the prior conviction.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court that denied defendant the right to collaterally attack a prior conviction during a sentencing hearing was affirmed.

Chapman v. State


No. 133, September Term, 1992


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


331 Md. 448; 628 A.2d 676; 1993 Md. LEXIS 119



July 30, 1993  
July 30, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected August 17, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Harford County pursuant to certiorari to Court of Special Appeals. William O. Carr, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR HARFORD COUNTY AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY THE PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury found defendant guilty of obtaining property or services by bad check in the Circuit Court for Harford County (Maryland). Defendant sought certiorari, asserting that Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 142(c) (1957 & Repl. Vol. 1992) violated the Confrontation Clause of the Sixth Amendment. The court granted certiorari before the intermediate appellate court heard the case.


OVERVIEW: Defendant paid for a television at a department store with a check. When the department store presented the check to the bank for payment, the bank dishonored it because defendant's account was closed. Defendant was charged with obtaining property or services by bad check. At trial, the State introduced a bank affidavit, showing that defendant did not have an account with the bank when he wrote the check. Defendant was convicted and appealed. The court granted certiorari before the intermediate appellate court heard the case. The court affirmed, holding that out-of-court statements admitted under Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 142(c) (1957 & Repl. Vol. 1992) had sufficient guarantees of trustworthiness to satisfy the requirements of the Confrontation Clause of the Sixth Amendment. The court reasoned that the hearsay exception under § 142(c) was derived from the business records hearsay exception and found that the Confrontation Clause did not require the State to prove that the declarant of the affidavit was unavailable. The court also concluded that the typographical error in the affidavit did not undermine its reliability.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

Judy v. Schaefer


No. 138, September Term, 1992


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


331 Md. 239; 627 A.2d 1039; 1993 Md. LEXIS 107



July 22, 1993  
July 22, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Counsel Segment Corrected August 12, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Baltimore City). Robert I. H. Hammerman, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED, WITH COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Writ of certiorari was granted with respect to plaintiff indigent citizens' appeal of a judgment from the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which was to address the granting of defendant state's motion for summary judgment regarding the indigent citizens' challenge to the validity of the governor's reducing appropriations pursuant to Md. Code Ann., State Fin. & Proc. § 7-213 (1988).


OVERVIEW: On review, the indigent citizens argued that § 7-213 was inconsistent with Md. Const. art. III, § 52, and thus was unauthorized. The court, however, found that § 52 allowed the governor to revise departmental estimates and, in the event that departmental exceeded estimated revenues, Md. Const. art. III, § 52(5a) mandated that the governor reduce those departmental estimates. In addition, Md. Const. art. III, § 52 expressly provided that the governor was permitted to amend or supplement the budget bill. Furthermore, delegation of legislative power to the executive branch was constitutionally permissible, and did not constitute a violation of Md. Const. Decl. Rts. art. 8, because sufficient safeguards were legislatively provided for the guidance in administration of the statute. The court accordingly affirmed, concluding that the 25 percent limitation in Md. Code Ann., State Fin. & Proc. § 7-213 on the reduction of any appropriation was not violated when the governor eliminated the Medical Assistance State Only grant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision to grant summary judgment in favor of the state as to the indigent citizens' challenge to the governor's reduction of certain public assistance appropriations.

Kelly v. Vote Know Coalition, Inc.


No. 54, September Term, 1992


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


331 Md. 164; 626 A.2d 959; 1993 Md. LEXIS 98



June 28, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Original Opinion of August 19, 1992, Reported at: 1992 Md. LEXIS 134.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County pursuant to certiorari to Court of Special Appeals. Bruce C. Williams, JUDGE


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, political coalition and affiliated individuals, challenged the ballot language certified by defendant secretary of state for use in a referendum election. The Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland) declared that the ballot language was misleading and directed the secretary to certify new ballot language. Defendants, the secretary and the administrator of the state board of election laws, appealed.


OVERVIEW: An enactment of the Maryland General Assembly, signed by the governor, addressed the subject of abortion and revised statutory provisions relating to abortion. Plaintiffs petitioned the act to referendum and it was scheduled to be submitted to the voters at the next general election. Plaintiffs challenged the ballot language prepared by the secretary of state, alleging that the language miscast and misrepresented the true nature and purpose of the referred law and used vague, ambiguous, and obtuse generalizations. The circuit court declared that the ballot language was misleading. The court reversed the declaratory judgment and injunctive orders of the circuit court and directed that a new declaratory judgment upholding the validity of the ballot title be entered. The court ruled that the standards to be applied were clearly set forth in the constitution and statutes. The secretary presented the purpose of the measure concisely and intelligently in accordance with those standards. The court emphasized that judicial review of the ballot title was not concerned with the question of whether better ballot language could be drafted, but whether language met the required standards.


OUTCOME: The court held that the ballot language certified by the secretary of state complied with the requirements of the Maryland constitution and statutes. The case was remanded to the circuit court with directions to enter a declaratory judgment consistent with the opinion.
