Surratt v. Prince George's County


No. 140, September Term, 1989


Court of Appeals of Maryland


320 Md. 439; 578 A.2d 745; 1990 Md. LEXIS 132



September 4, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to Court of Special Appeals, (Circuit Court for Prince George's County), Jacob S. Levin, JUDGE. 



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTION TO VACATE THE 3 OCTOBER 1988 JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR PRINCE GEORGE'S COUNTY AND ITS ORDER OF 23 DECEMBER 1988 WITH RESPECT TO COSTS, AND TO REMAND THIS CASE TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY RESPONDENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, estate of deceased infant and infant's parents, on writ of certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), sought review of the judgment in favor of respondent county finding the medical malpractice claims barred by governmental immunity.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, estate of deceased infant and infant's parents, sought review of the appeals court reversal of a medical malpractice award against respondent county. The court first held that the county's governmental immunity waiver was not abolished by a 1986 amendment to Prince George's County, Md., County Charter § 1013. Because the ballot for the provision failed to meet the "understandable language" requirement of Md. Ann. Code art. 33, § 16-6(a), the amendment was rendered invalid. The court then applied the earlier version of § 1013 which served to waive governmental immunity but limited it to $ 250,000 per occurrence. The matter was remanded to determine whether the county had liability insurance that would cover the damage award, as well as the method of apportionment. The court also ruled that petitioners, who accepted a remittitur but had not received payment of the reduced judgment or filed order of satisfaction, were not barred from cross-appealing the judgment. Finally, the court directed that another judge decide the motion for recusal, because the claim was based on the trial court judge's personal misconduct, the alleged sexual harassment of counsel.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of respondent county and remanded to the circuit court with directions to vacate the decision and remand to the trial court for a determination of the availability of insurance coverage for respondent's liability and the apportionment of any insurance proceeds. The court also directed the assignment of another judge to evaluate the recusal motion.

 

155 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Board of Educ. v. Riverdale


No. 121, September Term, 1988


Court of Appeals of Maryland


320 Md. 384; 578 A.2d 207; 1990 Md. LEXIS 126



August 30, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected August 30, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court for Prince George's County pursuant to certiorari to Court of Special Appeals; Audrey E. Melbourne Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR PRINCE GEORGE'S COUNTY REVERSED, AND CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS NOT INCONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. APPELLEE TO PAY COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, county board of education, filed a complaint against defendants, mayor and town council, on alternate theories of negligence, strict liability, and nuisance. The board asserted that the municipality was liable for damages caused by a leak of gasoline from the underground tank of its maintenance facility. The Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland) granted the council's motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The board asserted that the town was liable for damages caused by a gasoline leak from the underground tank of its maintenance facility into the sump pump of a public elementary school owned by the board. It also alleged that the leaking gasoline caused flammable vapors in the school and that the school was closed by order of the fire department as a result. The trial court found that the town was immune from suit under the doctrine of governmental immunity. The board argued that general immunity principles were irrelevant because all governmental immunity in the area of water pollution had been abrogated by statute. The board argued, alternatively, that the town did not enjoy immunity because its operation of the maintenance facility was a proprietary rather than a governmental function. Finally the board contended that governmental immunity did not protect the town from nuisance actions. The court found that the town was not protected by immunity because the tort suit was brought by the board as a state agency. A municipality could not assert the defense of sovereign immunity in an action based on negligent performance of a governmental function brought by the state itself.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment granting the motion to dismiss the board's complaint and remanded for further proceedings.

 

156 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Board of License Comm'rs v. Haberlin


No. 27, September Term, 1989


Court of Appeals of Maryland


320 Md. 399; 578 A.2d 215; 1990 Md. LEXIS 130



August 30, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Circuit Court for Montgomery County pursuant to certiorari to Court of Special Appeals; John J. Mitchell, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE IN BANC COURT VACATED. CASE REMANDED TO THE IN BANC COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO DISMISS THE APPEAL. RESPONDENTS TO PAY COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, applicant and liquor board, sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland), which reversed the finding of the lower court and held that appellee competing licensees were entitled to judicial review of the liquor board's order pursuant to Md. Const. art. 2B, § 175(b)(1). The competing licensees also filed an appeal as to the dismissal of their declaratory judgment action.


OVERVIEW: The applicant filed a petition for a license to sell alcoholic beverages and an administrative hearing was held. The competing licensees opposed the application on the ground that the issuance of the license would violate the proscription against granting such licenses to chain stores. The liquor board granted the license and the competing licensees appealed and requested a judgment declaring that the decision was unlawful, arbitrary, capricious, null and void. After the circuit court dismissed the action on the basis that the competing licensees lacked standing under Md. Const. art. 2B, § 175(b)(1), the circuit administrative judge convened a court in banc, which reversed the judgment with regard to the original count. The applicant and the liquor board appealed and the principal issue concerned the scope of the right to take an in banc appeal pursuant to Md. Const. art. IV, § 22 and Md. R. Civ. P., Cir. Ct. 2-551. The court issued a writ of certiorari and vacated the judgment. The court held that the in banc court should not have exercised jurisdiction over the case and that the only avenue of appeal from the circuit court's order was an appeal to the Court of Special Appeals.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment of the in banc court and remanded with instructions to dismiss the competing licensees' appeal. The court ordered the competing licensees to pay costs.

 

157 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Caucus Distributors, Inc. v. Maryland Sec. Comm'r


No. 138, September Term, 1989


Court of Appeals of Maryland


320 Md. 313; 577 A.2d 783; 1990 Md. LEXIS 123



August 9, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore City pursuant to certiorari to Court of Special Appeals; Joseph H. H. Kaplan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED, WITH COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed a writ of certiorari prior to the judgment of the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland) dismissing petitioner's appeals as untimely and affirming the final order of respondent Securities Commissioner in proceedings brought against the petitioner for a violation of the Maryland Securities Act, Md. Code Ann., Corps. & Ass'ns §§ 11-101 through 11-805.


OVERVIEW: Respondent, the Securities Commissioner ("Commissioner"), found that petitioner, a political nonprofit organization, had violated the Maryland Securities Act (the "Act"), Md. Code Ann., Corps. & Ass'ns §§ 11-101 through 11-805 (1985), by misrepresenting and failing to disclose material facts to an investor in connection with the offer and sale of securities. Petitioner denied the alleged violation and claimed that respondent's cease and desist order deprived it of its right to political expression. The trial court affirmed respondent's order. On appeal, the court concluded that there was substantial evidence to support respondent's factual determinations and that that there was no error in finding petitioner's promissory notes to be securities within the contemplation of the Act. The court further concluded that petitioner's First Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. I, rights were not violated where the Act neither suppressed free speech nor deterred political association; instead, the Act extended to the public a precise measure for protecting against fraudulent sales of securities.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

158 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Jones v. Speed


No. 6, September Term 1989


Court of Appeals of Maryland


320 Md. 249; 577 A.2d 64; 1990 Md. LEXIS 119



August 2, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore City pursuant to certiorari to Court of Special Appeals; Thomas E. Noel, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY AFFIRMED AS TO COUNTS ONE THROUGH NINE OF THE COMPLAINT; JUDGMENT VACATED AS TO COUNTS 10 THROUGH 17 AND CASE REMANDED TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS NOT INCONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION; COSTS TO BE PAID ONE-HALF BY APPELLANTS AND ONE-HALF BY APPELLEE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, patient and husband, sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland), which granted defendant doctor's motion for summary judgment and dismissed plaintiffs' medical malpractice suit as time-barred under Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 5-109 (1974, 1989 Repl. Vol.).


OVERVIEW: After plaintiff patient was misdiagnosed, plaintiffs, patient and husband, filed a medical malpractice suit against defendant doctor. The lower court granted defendant's motion for summary judgment and dismissed the suit as barred under the five-year statute of limitations period of Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 5-109 (1974, 1989 Repl. Vol.). On appeal, the court affirmed in part but vacated and remanded in part the lower court's order holding that the lower court had correctly determined that counts one through nine of plaintiffs' complaint were barred under § 5-109. However, the court held that the remaining counts of the complaint were not barred under § 5-109 because the complaint alleged that those acts of negligence occurred within five years of the date of plaintiffs' filing of the suit. The court further held that although the viable claims could have been litigated in an earlier proceeding between the parties, the claims were not barred by res judicata because no final adjudication of the barred claims had occurred in the prior proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part but vacated and remanded in part an order of the lower court, which granted defendant doctor's motion for summary judgment and dismissed the medical malpractice suit of plaintiffs, patient and husband, as time-barred. Defendant's alleged subsequent acts of negligence were not barred by the doctrine of res judicata.

 

159 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


East Prince Frederick Corp. v. Board of County Comm'rs


No. 118, September Term, 1989


Court of Appeals of Maryland


320 Md. 178; 577 A.2d 27; 1990 Md. LEXIS 111



July 31, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to Court of Special Appeals; Circuit Court for Calvert County, John Hansen Briscoe, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner corporation sought certiorari review of the judgment of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) which reversed the trial court's judgment and held that respondent county's use -it-or-lose-it sewer and water allocation did not violate the United State Constitution's Contract Clause.


OVERVIEW: The corporation paid a capital connection fee to the county to reserve a daily allocation of 4,400 gallons of sewer and water usage to serve a planned shopping strip. The shopping strip was never constructed and the corporation never used its sewer and water usage allocation. Subsequently, due to a lack of additional water and sewer capacity, the county adopted a use-it-or-lose-it allocation policy, requiring those who had reserved usage to use or pay a minimum charge. The corporation filed suit alleging that the policy violated the Contracts Clause. The trial court held that the Contracts Clause was violated, but the appellate court reversed. On appeal, the court affirmed. The policy impaired the parties contract, but the corporation had the option between losing its allocation and retaining it by paying the minimum charge. The policy was reasonable to address the county's lack of sewer and water capacity to encourage those who were not using their reservations to make them available for use by others.


OUTCOME: The judgment holding that the county's use-it-or-lose it sewer and water allocation policy did not violate the Contract Clause was affirmed.

 

160 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Mandel v. O'Hara


No. 33, September Term, 1990


Court of Appeals of Maryland


320 Md. 103; 576 A.2d 766; 1990 Md. LEXIS 108



July 27, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Baltimore City pursuant to certiorari to court of Special Appeals; Elsbeth Bothe, Judge.



DISPOSITION: ORDER OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY DENYING THE MOTION FOR SUMMARY JUDGMENT OF THE DEFENDANT, MARVIN MANDEL, REVERSED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT FOR THE ENTRY OF JUDGMENT IN FAVOR OF THE DEFENDANT, MARVIN MANDEL, ONLY. COSTS TO BE PAID BY THE APPELLEES. THE STAY ISSUED ON JUNE 1, 1990, BY THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS IS LIFTED, EFFECTIVE WITH THE FILING OF THIS OPINION.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee stockholders filed a complaint against appellant governor and alleged common law deceit. The governor filed a motion for summary judgment based on absolute immunity. The Circuit Court for Baltimore City (Maryland) denied his motion and the governor appealed.


OVERVIEW: The stockholders owned stock in a corporation that owned a racetrack. The governor vetoed the bill that would have allowed the stockholders' corporation to race in the state. After the stockholders sold their stock, the General Assembly overrode the veto. The stockholders alleged in their complaint that common law deceit was practiced upon them in the sale of their stock. They argued that the governor conspired with others in the General Assembly to reduce the price of the stock so that they could acquire it at a depressed price. The governor filed a motion for summary judgment based on his absolute immunity. The court reversed the lower court's denial of the governor's motion for summary judgment. The court held that the discretion exercised by the governor in deciding whether to veto or approve legislation did not differ from that to be exercised by legislators in deciding whether to vote for or against a bill. The court held that there was no policy reason why legislators should enjoy absolute immunity for their legislative acts but that the governor should have only a qualified immunity for his legislative function of vetoing or approving legislation.


OUTCOME: The judgment that denied the governor's motion for summary judgment was reversed and the case was remanded.

Gardner v. Board of County Comm'rs


No. 103, September Term, 1989


Court of Appeals of Maryland


320 Md. 63; 576 A.2d 208; 1990 Md. LEXIS 100



July 5, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to Court of Special Appeals; Circuit Court for St. Mary's County; Audrey E. Melbourne, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS VACATED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT FOR THE ENTRY OF A MANDATE AFFIRMING THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ST. MARY'S COUNTY. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY ST. MARY'S COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent county appealed an order of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which held that the county could not assess a special tax because the majority of lot owners, who would benefit from the tax, did not sign the petition.


OVERVIEW: The lot owners asked the county to assess a special tax, which would pay for road improvement. Petitioner taxpayers, sought to have the tax ordinance declared void. The county appealed the voiding of the ordinance. On appeal, the court held that the circuit court had subject matter jurisdiction because it could rule that an initial claim for relief did not state a claim upon which relief could have been granted and Md. R. Civ. P., Cir. Ct. 2-341 permitted amendments to pleadings. The taxpayers violated Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 3-405(c) when they failed to give notice to the Attorney General regarding their allegation of the ordinance's unconstitutionality. However, the lack of notice did not deprive the circuit court of jurisdiction over the subject matter because the circuit court declared the ordinance to be invalid on nonconstitutional grounds. Md. R Civ. P., Cir. Ct. 2-211 and 21-231 did not require the joinder of similarly situated taxpayers. Under the ordinance it was sufficient to require the owners of unimproved, nonabutting lots to be counted in determining whether the petition was presented by the majority of the affected property owners.


OUTCOME: The court vacated an order of the special appeals court and remanded the matter for the entry of a mandate affirming the judgment of the trial court.

 

162 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Maryland State Dep't of Health & Mental Hygiene v. Phoebus


No. 126, September Term, 1988


Court of Appeals of Maryland


319 Md. 710; 575 A.2d 335; 1990 Md. LEXIS 95



June 26, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to Court of Special Appeals; Circuit Court for Worcester County; Theodore R. Eschenburg, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED, WITH COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Maryland Department of Health and Mental Hygiene (department) challenged a decision from the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which affirmed the trial court's decision that appellee employee be reinstated with back pay. The trial court reversed the decision of an administrative hearing officer after it determined that the employee had not been terminated by his appointing authority. The employee was an unclassified employee.


OVERVIEW: The employee was a director of one of the department's centers. After a heated telephone conversation with his immediate supervisor, the employee was suspended for the rest of the day. The employee appealed the suspension. The day after the appeal hearing an acting assistant secretary of the department terminated the employee's employment. The employee appealed his termination arguing, among other things, the termination was improper because the action was taken by the acting assistant secretary and not the appointing authority as contemplated by Md. Code Ann., Health-Gen. II § 2-103(b) (1982, 1990 Repl. Vol.). The hearing officer upheld the termination. The department, on appeal, questioned if it had the burden to prove an unclassified employee was properly terminated by his appointing authority. The court affirmed, holding that: (1) the burden was on the employee to show his termination was illegal; (2) the employee showed that under pertinent statutes, the secretary of the department was the official having the authority to remove the employee; and (3) the department failed to show that the authority to terminate the employee had been delegated to the assistant secretary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's decision affirming the trial court's decision that the employee be reinstated with back pay.

 

163 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Gluckstern v. Sutton


No. 107, September Term, 1988


Court of Appeals of Maryland


319 Md. 634; 574 A.2d 898; 1990 Md. LEXIS 91



June 7, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to Court of Special Appeals; Circuit Court for Baltimore County; Edward A. DeWaters, Jr. JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS VACATED, AND CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO AFFIRM THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE COUNTY. PETITIONER TO PAY COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) dismissed petitioner director of an institution and chairman of the institutional board of review's appeal of order that required board to afford respondent prisoner another parole hearing and to proceed on facts and evidence as they existed when respondent was originally considered for parole and that such was not to be subject to gubernatorial approval. Petitioner filed petition for a writ of certiorari.


OVERVIEW: The court granted petitioner director of an institution and chairman of the institutional board of review's petition for a writ of certiorari to the appellate court. The appellate court had dismissed respondent prisoner's appeal of an order that required the board to afford respondent another parole hearing and to proceed solely on facts and evidence as they existed when the board originally considered respondent for parole and that if the board elected to grant parole, such was not to be subject to gubernatorial approval. In addition, the court granted a stay of the circuit court's order until its decision. Petitioner's notice of appeal, filed within 30 days of the revised judgment, was timely. The appeal was authorized by the Post Conviction Procedure Act, Md. Code Ann. art. 27, § 645A(e). The appellate court erred in dismissing the appeal. The court also noted that the ordering of a new parole hearing was an available type of relief in a habeas corpus case. The judge below correctly held that, under the ex post facto clauses of the federal and state constitutions, the requirement of gubernatorial approval could not be applied to a decision by the board to parole respondent.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment of the appellate court and remanded the case to that court with directions to affirm the judgment of the circuit court. Petitioner director of an institution and chairman of the institutional board of review to pay costs in the court and in the appellate court.

 

164 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Sugarloaf Citizens Assoc., Inc. v. Gudis


No. 59, September Term, 1989


Court of Appeals of Maryland


319 Md. 558; 573 A.2d 1325; 1990 Md. LEXIS 85



May 30, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to Court of Special Appeals; (Circuit Court for Montgomery County); John J. Mitchell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID ONE-HALF BY PETITIONERS AND ONE-HALF BY RESPONDENTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayers brought an action against respondents, the county council and one of its members, which asked the trial court to void an action voted upon and passed by the council, due to an alleged conflict of interest of the county council member, pursuant to Montgomery County Code § 19A-22(b). The Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) affirmed the trial court's ruling refusing to void the action. The taxpayers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers contended that the council member was prohibited from voting on an incinerator pursuant to Montgomery County Code § 19A-7(a), which disqualified a council member from voting in a matter in which he had a financial interest. The taxpayers argued that because the council member owned stock in the stock in the company that owned the land where the incinerator was to be built, he should have been disqualified from voting and the vote overturned. The court upheld the lower court's ruling and allowed the vote to stand. In so holding, the court found that 1) Montgomery County Code § 19A-22(b), which allowed a court to void an action taken by an official or employee with a conflict of interest, impermissibly attempted to vest in the court a nonjudicial power; 2) § 19A-22(b) was severable from the remainder of the county ethics law; 3) § 19A-7(a) remained a valid part of the law, but could not be invoked as the basis for invalidating the incinerator vote, because improper legislative motive is not sufficient to set aside legislation; and 4) mere ownership of stock by a legislator who cast a critical vote was an insufficient basis for legislation invalidation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court.

 

165 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. Wilzack


No. 140, September Term, 1988


Court of Appeals of Maryland


319 Md. 485; 573 A.2d 809; 1990 Md. LEXIS 83



May 29, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Denied June 25, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County pursuant to certiorari to Court of Special Appeals; DeLawrence Beard, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED; CASE REMANDED TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR MONTGOMERY COUNTY FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS TO BE PAID BY THE APPELLEES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, mentally competent adult, sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Maryland), which granted the state's motions for summary judgment on the ground that it acted in compliance with Md. Code Ann., Health-Gen. § 10-708 and did not violate any of appellant's constitutional rights.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, mentally competent adult, sought review of the trial court's judgment, which granted the state's motions for summary judgment on the ground that it acted in compliance with Md. Code Ann., Health-Gen. § 10-708 and did not violate any of appellant's constitutional rights. The trial court's judgment was reversed and remanded. The court recognized that appellant possessed a significant liberty interest in avoiding the unwanted administration of antipsychotic drugs under the Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The court concluded that § 10-708, on its face and as applied to appellant, did not afford the requisite procedural due process protections to which appellant was entitled. Thus, it was error for the trial court to grant the state summary judgment against appellant's claims. It should have granted appellant's motion for partial summary judgment on the ground that § 10-708 violated procedural due process protections because under § 10-708, the state was prohibited from non-consensual administration of drugs to a mentally competent adult under non-emergency circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment because the administration of drugs to the mentally competent adult, under non-emergency circumstances without his consent violated the protections afforded by the Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment.

 

166 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Harrison v. Schwartz


No. 89, September Term, 1989


Court of Appeals of Maryland


319 Md. 360; 572 A.2d 528; 1990 Md. LEXIS 65



April 19, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected April 27, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Carroll County), Donald J. Gilmore, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED IN PART AND AFFIRMED IN PART. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTION TO AFFIRM THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR CARROLL COUNTY. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY APPELLEES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner airport appealed a decision of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which reversed in part a trial court ruling in favor of the airport on a suit by respondent neighbors to enforce zoning conditions placed on the airport to control noise. The lower appellate court found that the Supremacy Clause, U.S. Const. art. VI, cl. 2, and the Noise Control Act of 1972, 49 U.S.C.S. App. §§ 1301 et seq., invalidated only one condition.


OVERVIEW: A small commercial airport was found to have exceeded its conditional use permit and applied for another. Conditions attached to the new permit included restricting flights to daytime hours, restricting flights to one every 15 minutes, and requiring that pilots use particular landing patterns. The trial court found all three to be preempted by federal law. The court agreed completely with the trial court, finding that congress had indicated an intent to preempt the entire field of aircraft operations in navigable airspace in the Noise Control Act of 1972, among other statutes. The court, therefore, held that the neighbors could not enforce any local zoning restriction that impinged on aircraft operation. While the lower appellate court had found only that the landing pattern restriction was preempted, the court found that the timing and noise restrictions were similarly preempted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the lower appellate court's holding. The court remanded the case for affirmance of the trial court's judgment in favor of the airport that found that the zoning restrictions were preempted.

ATTORNEY GRIEVANCE COMMN. OF MARYLAND v. FICKER


Misc. Docket (Subtitle BV) No. 11, September Term, 1988


Court of Appeals of Maryland


319 Md. 305; 572 A.2d 501; 1990 Md. LEXIS 67



April 18, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Attorney Griev. Comm'n v. Ficker, 349 Md. 13, 706 A.2d 1045, 1998 Md. LEXIS 147 (Mar. 10, 1998)
Related proceeding at Atty. Griev. Comm'n v. Ficker, 399 Md. 445, 924 A.2d 1105, 2007 Md. LEXIS 341 (June 7, 2007)
Related proceeding at In re Reinstatement of Ficker, 406 Md. 577, 961 A.2d 552, 2008 Md. LEXIS 617 (Dec. 8, 2008)
Related proceeding at Atty. Griev. Comm'n of Md. v. Ficker, 2017 Md. LEXIS 458 (Md., June 30, 2017)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] IT IS SO ORDERED. RESPONDENT SHALL PAY ALL COSTS AS TAXED BY THE CLERK OF THIS COURT, INCLUDING THE COSTS OF ALL TRANSCRIPTS, PURSUANT TO MARYLAND RULE BV15 c FOR WHICH SUM JUDGMENT IS ENTERED IN FAVOR OF THE ATTORNEY GRIEVANCE COMMISSION AGAINST ROBIN K.A. FICKER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Attorney Grievance Commission brought a disciplinary action against respondent attorney charging violations of the Code of Professional Responsibility and the Rules of Professional Conduct involving the neglect of legal matters entrusted to him, conduct prejudicial to the administration of justice, and misleading advertising.


OVERVIEW: Respondent attorney excepted to the findings of facts, conclusions of law, and recommendations brought before the court in a disciplinary action initiated by petitioner Attorney Grievance Commission. The court held that respondent's single failure to appear before the court on behalf of his client or to enter his written appearance could constitute neglect under the Code of Professional Responsibility DR 6-101(A)(3). The respondent's inadvertence, lack of persistent pattern or conduct, or lack of prejudice to the client properly went to the issue of mitigation rather than the fact of violation. The court held that Code of Professional Responsibility DR 6-101(A)(5) should not be read to apply only to particular egregious conduct but a single inadvertent failure to appear in court could constitute conduct prejudicial to the administration of justice. The court held that respondent's advertisement, in which he solicited "Palimony" suits did not violate Md. Lawyers' R. Prof. Conduct 7.1 because the term "Palimony" did not refer to a nonexistent action. The court determined that reprimand was an appropriate sanction for the respondent's derelictions.


OUTCOME: The court reprimanded respondent attorney for the dereliction of his professional responsibilities. A single failure to appear in court could constitute "neglect" of a legal matter under the Code of Professional Responsibility. However, respondent's advertised solicitation of "Palimony" suits did violate the Rule of Professional Responsibility barring false advertising.

 

168 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Lofland v. Montgomery County


No. 105, September Term, 1989


Court of Appeals of Maryland


319 Md. 265; 572 A.2d 163; 1990 Md. LEXIS 60



April 16, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to Court of Special Appeals, Circuit Court for Montgomery County, James S. McAuliffe, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED; CASE REMANDED TO THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS WITH DIRECTIONS TO AFFIRM THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR MONTGOMERY COUNTY AND REMAND THE CASE TO THAT COURT FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS IN ACCORDANCE WITH THIS OPINION; COSTS IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AND IN THIS COURT TO BE PAID BY MONTGOMERY COUNTY, MARYLAND.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee sought review, by writ of certiorari, of a decision of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which reversed the circuit court's decision holding that respondent Montgomery County Merit System Protection Board (board) was required to conduct a hearing to determine whether the employee's grievance concerning differential pay was timely filed.


OVERVIEW: The employee worked as a fire fighter/paramedic from December 1985 through May 1987. The county had a policy that, upon completion of one year of probationary service, certain fire fighter/paramedics would be eligible for a 10 percent pay differential. The employee satisfied the requirement throughout his employment period, but did not receive the pay differential. On August 25, 1987, in another case, the board voided the policy that eligibility for the pay differential depended upon completion of the probationary period. The employee filed a grievance on October 7, 1987, complaining that he had not received the pay differential during his employment. The personnel director held that the grievance was not timely filed, and the board denied a request for a hearing. The employee appealed to the circuit court, which ordered the board to conduct a hearing. The court of special appeals reversed, and the employee sought review. The court granted certiorari and reversed. The record did not disclose whether or when the employee should reasonably have known of an automatic entitlement under the revised policy. A hearing was necessary to determine whether the grievance was timely filed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the court of special appeals and remanded the case to that court with directions to affirm the judgment of the circuit court and remand the case to that court for further proceedings in connection with the employee's grievance with the board over salary benefits.

 

169 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Franklin v. State


No. 180, September Term, 1987


Court of Appeals of Maryland


319 Md. 116; 571 A.2d 1208; 1990 Md. LEXIS 49



April 6, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Prince George's County) Audrey E. Melbourne, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED AND CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO REVERSE THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR PRINCE GEORGE'S COUNTY AND REMAND THE CASE TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR A NEW TRIAL. PRINCE GEORGE'S COUNTY TO PAY THE COSTS IN THIS COURT AND THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was granted a writ of certiorari to Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) to challenge his conviction for assault with the intent to murder.


OVERVIEW: At trial, the jury was instructed that in order to find defendant guilty of assault with intent to murder, a specific intent to murder was not required. The intermediate appellate court held that a challenge to this instruction had not been preserved for appeal because it had been given without objection. On review, the court found there had been a new decision while defendant's case was pending that held that the instruction was an incorrect statement of the law. The court, upon its own motion, could correct any plain error in the jury instruction, without an objection from defense counsel, where the error was material and affected defendant's right to a fair trial. To prove assault with the intent to murder, the state had to prove a specific intent to kill. Assault with the intent to kill, a statutory crime was held to be distinct from assault with the intent to do bodily harm. Because the instruction was misleading and influenced the jury's deliberations, it was plain error and deprived him of a fair trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision which convicted defendant of assault with the intent to murder and remanded the matter for a new trial.

 

170 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Attorney Grievance Com. v. Korotki


Misc. (Subtitle BV) No. 24, September Term, 1988


Court of Appeals of Maryland


318 Md. 646; 569 A.2d 1224; 1990 Md. LEXIS 32



February 21, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Circuit Court for Baltimore County, Dana M. Levitz, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: IT IS SO ORDERED; RESPONDENT SHALL PAY ALL COSTS AS TAXED BY THE CLERK OF THIS COURT, INCLUDING THE COSTS OF ALL TRANSCRIPTS, PURSUANT TO MARYLAND RULE BV15C FOR WHICH SUM JUDGMENT IS ENTERED IN FAVOR OF THE ATTORNEY GRIEVANCE COMMISSION AGAINST ABRAHAM PAUL KOROTKI.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After respondent attorney as counsel in a single personal injury action charged his clients a contingent fee of 75 percent of the gross amount recovered after trial and appellate review, the Attorney Grievance Commission of Maryland charged the attorney with misconduct. The Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland) found the contingency fee in violation of Md. Code of Prof. Responsibility DR 2-106(A) (1986).


OVERVIEW: The attorney charged two of the clients fees totaling $ 471,424 on their combined gross recoveries of $ 628,565. Under the initial fee agreement, the attorney undertook to pursue the claims of his clients through all appeals. The court held that inadequacy of compensation furnished no justification for the attorney to seek a new agreement with his clients to increase his fee for work he had already agreed to do. In seeking the increase, the attorney also crossed the 50 percent line and acquired a greater interest in the outcome of the litigation than his clients. Without passing upon whether there could ever be circumstances justifying a contingent fee in excess of 50 percent, the court held that it was generally a violation of Md. Code of Prof. Responsibility DR 2-106(A) (1986) for the attorney's stake in the result to exceed the client's stake. The court sustained the findings and conclusion of the circuit court judge over the attorney's exceptions. Because this was a particularly aggravated case of greed overriding professionalism, the court suspended the attorney from the practice of law for 18 months.


OUTCOME: The court found the 75 percent contingency fee excessive. The attorney's suspension would begin 30 days from the filing of the court's opinion. The court also ordered that the attorney should pay all costs as taxed, including the costs of all transcripts for which sum judgment was entered in favor of the Attorney Grievance Commission against the attorney.

 

171 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Eanes v. State


No. 1, September Term, 1989


Court of Appeals of Maryland


318 Md. 436; 569 A.2d 604; 1990 Md. LEXIS 17



February 8, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected February 12, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to Circuit Court for Washington County, Fred C. Wright, III, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR WASHINGTON COUNTY AFFIRMED. COSTS TO BE PAID BY PETITIONER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner protestor sought review of a judgement of the Circuit Court for Washington County (Maryland), which affirmed his conviction for disturbing the police in violation of Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 121 (1987). The protestor raised several First Amendment challenges to his conviction.


OVERVIEW: The protestor was part of a group that gathered outside of an abortion clinic to protest abortion. The protestor became so loud that several residents complained about the level of the noise. A police officer responded to the complaints and arrested the protestor when he again began to shout his message. On appeal, the court stated that enactments should construed to be valid where feasible. In construing the language of § 121 the court held that "unseemly" modified "loud" and meant unreasonably loud in the circumstances. Construed in that manner § 121was content neutral, narrowly tailored to serve a significant State interest, and did not inhibit the use of various alternative channels of communication. The court held that this interpretation of § 121 gave sufficient notice of what conduct was penalized, and thus, § 121 was not void for vagueness. The court also imposed a requirement of prior warning by police, so that a speaker would be made aware that further communication at the offensive volume level could be cause for an arrest. Properly applied § 121 reached only that conduct which could be regulated consistent with the First Amendment, and thus, § 121 was not overbroad.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgement below.

 

172 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Porten Sullivan Corp. v. State


No. 93, September Term, 1989


Court of Appeals of Maryland


318 Md. 387; 568 A.2d 1111; 1990 Md. LEXIS 13



February 6, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Circuit Court for Prince George's County pursuant to certiorari to Court of Special Appeals, George W. Bowling, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR PRINCE GEORGE'S COUNTY REVERSED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT FOR ENTRY OF JUDGMENT CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLEES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation and its employee filed an action against appellees, state, county, and individuals, challenging Chapter 244, Acts of 1989. The Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland) upheld Chapter 244 in all respects. The court granted the corporation's petition for certiorari before any proceedings were had in the appellate court.


OVERVIEW: Chapter 244 was an emergency measure that was designed to extend the life of the county's energy tax. It contained both ethics and tax provisions. The corporation and its employees challenged the legislation, and the trial court upheld its validity. The court granted certiorari and reversed the trial court's judgment. The court held that Chapter 244 violated the "one-subject" constitutional mandate found in Md. Const. art. III, § 29. The court also held that the "ethics" provisions were severable from the "tax" provisions, and that the latter survived the constitutionally required demise of the former. The court noted that the "ethics" provisions were unrelated to raising revenue. The court found that Chapter 244 did not deal with "many related aspects" of "comprehensive legislation in a given field." Rather, Chapter 244 dealt with one aspect of zoning-related ethics and with limited taxing authority. The court concluded that Chapter 244 was unconstitutional because the "ethics" provisions were incongruous and discordant additions, "foreign or irrelevant matter," unconnected in subject-matter to the "tax" provisions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the lower court's judgment, which had upheld the validity of the challenged legislation.

Finally, the court found that defendant's death sentence was not aberrant, arbitrary, capricious, or freakish. It was not imposed under the influence of passion, prejudice, or any arbitrary factor. The evidence supported the jury's finding of a statutory aggravating circumstance.


OUTCOME: The order convicting defendant and sentencing him to death was affirmed.

Annapolis v. United Food & Commercial Workers, Local 400


No. 38, September Term, 1989


Court of Appeals of Maryland


317 Md. 544; 565 A.2d 672; 1989 Md. LEXIS 154; 4 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 1589



November 9, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County pursuant to certiorari to Court of Special Appeals, Bruce C. Williams, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY THE APPELLEES, UNITED FOOD AND COMMERCIAL WORKERS, LOCAL 400, et al.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant City filed an unfair labor practices complaint against appellee labor unions for refusal to negotiate as a result of the City's proposed drug testing program. A mediation service found that the City was entitled to unilaterally implement the program. The City sought review of the order of the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland), which issued a writ of mandamus enjoining the City from implementing its program.


OVERVIEW: City proposed the adoption of a drug testing program requiring its uniformed police and fire fighter personnel, as a part of their regularly scheduled periodic physical examinations, to submit a urine sample to determine the presence of illegal drugs. The labor unions representing the employees failed to reach a collective bargaining agreement with the City. The court held: 1) that the program did not involve random post-employment drug testing; 2) that the results were not used for criminal prosecutions without the employees' consent; 3) that the employees had three types of notice, there was no observation of urination, and test results were confidential; 4) that the City's interest in the safety of its uniformed police and fire personnel, their co-workers, and the public outweighed the negligible private interest; 5) that the potential for abuse or harassment by the City was negligible; 6) that a reasonable suspicion requirement was unwarranted; 7) that the testing was not facially at odds with the Fourth Amendment; and 8) that the trial court erred in enjoining the City from enforcing its program.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.

Bd. of Trs. v. Mayor & City Council of Balt. City


Nos. 95, 104, September Term, 1987


Court of Appeals of Maryland


317 Md. 72; 562 A.2d 720; 1989 Md. LEXIS 126; 11 Employee Benefits Cas. (BNA) 1521



September 1, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals, Circuit Court of Anne Arundel County, Judge Eugene M. Lerner.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE CITY MODIFIED SO AS TO GRANT THE MOTION FOR INTERVENTION AND TO REFLECT THE VIEWS SET FORTH IN THIS OPINION, AND AS MODIFIED, AFFIRMED. IN NO. 95, COSTS TO BE PAID BY THE BOARDS OF TRUSTEES. IN NO. 104, ONE-HALF OF THE COSTS TO BE PAID BY THE APPELLANTS AND ONE-HALF OF THE COSTS TO BE PAID BY THE MAYOR AND CITY COUNCIL OF BALTIMORE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff trustees appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Anne Arundel County (Maryland), which upheld ordinances challenged by the trustees in an action against defendants, mayor and city council. The circuit court also denied a motion to intervene brought by beneficiaries of the city's employee pension systems represented by the trustees.


OVERVIEW: The ordinances required that the pension systems divest their holdings in companies doing business in South Africa. The trustees argued that the ordinances delegated legislative power to a private entity by instructing that entities doing business in South Africa be identified by reference to an annual report. The trustees argued that the ordinances violated the Contract Clause of the United States Constitution by modifying the manner in which the pension funds were invested. The court granted the beneficiaries' motion to intervene, holding that a ruling upholding the ordinances would be res judicata in a separate action by the beneficiaries and that the trustees, municipal officials, could not adequately represent their interests in the pensions. The court upheld the ordinances finding no impermissible delegation of legislative power or violation of the Contract Clause. The list was merely an advisory reference. The ordinances may have affected pension systems' profitability and required consideration of social consequences, but the consequences were minimal. In addition, divestiture could not occur unless the it was consistent with the trustees' duty of prudence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court, upholding the city's ordinances as constitutional. The court modified the circuit court's judgment by granting the beneficiaries' motion to intervene.

Board of Education v. Secretary of Personnel


No. 136, September Term, 1987


Court of Appeals of Maryland


317 Md. 34; 562 A.2d 700; 1989 Md. LEXIS 122



August 31, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Circuit Court for Prince George's County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Appeals, Joseph S. Casula, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR PRINCE GEORGE'S COUNTY AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART, AND CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT FOR THE ISSUANCE OF A JUDGMENT DISMISSING THE COMPLAINT. COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE CIRCUIT COURT TO BE PAID BY THE BOARD OF EDUCATION OF PRINCE GEORGE'S COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the Board of Education of Prince George's County (Board), challenged the judgment from the Circuit Court for Prince George's County (Maryland), which issued a writ of mandamus compelling defendant, the Secretary of Personnel (Secretary), to render a declaratory ruling as to whether the Board was entitled to a "contested case" hearing.


OVERVIEW: The Board sought to challenge audit findings by the Maryland Department of Personnel, Division of Social Security and requested a "contested case" hearing, pursuant to the Administrative Procedures Act, Md. Code Ann., State Gov't § 10-215(a), which would have been subject to judicial review. Instead, the Board was granted an administrative proceeding, pursuant to Md. Ann. Code art. 73B, § 39(e), which was not subject to judicial review. Therefore, the Board instituted an action with the circuit court naming additional defendants. Following the issuance of the writ of mandamus by the circuit court, all parties appealed. However, prior to any proceedings in the Court of Special Appeals, the court issued a writ of certiorari and held that the circuit court erred in issuing the writ of mandamus because § 39(e) was the Board's exclusive remedy. Thus, in pertinent part, the court held that the Board was not entitled to a hearing which would be subject to judicial review because, as an agency of the state, the Board did not have standing to contest an act of the state.


OUTCOME: The court held that the circuit court erred in issuing a writ of mandamus to the Secretary after holding that the Board was not entitled to a "contested case" hearing which would have been subject to judicial review.

Chesapeake & Potomac Tel. Co. v. Comptroller of Treasury, Retail Sales Tax Div.


No. 143 September Term, 1987


Court of Appeals of Maryland


317 Md. 3; 561 A.2d 1034; 1989 Md. LEXIS 119



July 31, 1989

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant telephone company sought review of a decision from the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which affirmed the circuit court's order denying the telephone company any tax refund beyond that granted by appellee comptroller.


OVERVIEW: The telephone company sought a refund of use taxes it paid in connection with the distribution of telephone directories to its customers in different counties in the state of Maryland. The comptroller denied the telephone company's request for a refund from October 1977 to April 1982. The tax court affirmed the denial of the claim for October 1977 to April 1979, but ordered a refund from the period of May 1979 to April 1982. The court ruled that the telephone company had power and control over the directories at all times, therefore it was liable for payment of the use taxes. The tax imposed on the telephone company related to benefits provided by the state. Finally, the court held that the directories did not fall within the coverage of the claimed exemption.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the special appeals court, which denied the telephone company a tax refund on its 1977-79 claim and granted a refund on the 1979-82 claim. The telephone company was ordered to pay the costs.

Randall Book Corp. v. State


No. 135, September Term, 1987


Court of Appeals of Maryland


316 Md. 315; 558 A.2d 715; 1989 Md. LEXIS 93



June 7, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court for Baltimore County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals, James T. Smith, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR BALTIMORE COUNTY AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Baltimore County (Maryland), denied appellant book store's motion to correct an illegal sentence. The corporation appealed the order.


OVERVIEW: Police detectives executed a search warrant at the book store and located pornographic material. Subsequently, a jury found the book store guilty of violating Md. Ann. Code art. 27 § 416D(a). After the book store was sentenced, it filed a motion to correct an illegal sentence. The motion was denied. On appeal, the court held that the book store was entitled to appeal the sentence. The court concluded that the book store had a cognizable claim that the aggregate of multiple sentences constitutes cruel and unusual punishment prohibited by the Eighth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. VIII. The court determined that the legislature intended the knowing display of each separate obscene magazine to constitute a separate offense, separately punishable. The court held that the sentencing did not constitute cruel or unusual punishment or violate the double jeopardy clause of the Fifth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. V. Additionally, the court held that the total fine imposed was proportionate to the criminal activity.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order, which denied the book store's motion to correct an illegal sentence, was affirmed.

Woods v. State


No. 98, September Term, 1988


Court of Appeals of Maryland


315 Md. 591; 556 A.2d 236; 1989 Md. LEXIS 55



April 10, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended April 28, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County pursuant to certiorari to Court of Special Appeals, H. Chester Goudy, Jr.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY AFFIRMED; COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLANT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with murder and other offenses. The Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland) found the defendant guilty of murder in the first degree, attempted murder, conspiracy to dynamite an automobile, and using a handgun in the commission of the felony of murder. The defendant was sentenced to life without parole, concurrent life and one-year terms, and a consecutive five-year term. The defendant appealed. .


OVERVIEW: The defendant was hired by the victim's wife to kill him. The defendant urged that the sentence of life imprisonment without parole was illegal, evidence seized when he was arrested and his confession should have been suppressed, and the evidence was insufficient. The court held that the sentence of life imprisonment without parole did not deny the defendant due process of law nor subject him to cruel and unusual punishment. The trial judge followed all the required procedures, and life in prison was not worse than death. The defendant's warrantless arrest was proper because the totality of the circumstances showed probable cause. The fact that he was not taken before a judicial officer until almost nine hours after his arrest was only a factor to be considered in deciding the voluntariness and admissibility of his confession. Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 10-912 (1973, Repl. Vol. 1984). The defendant's confession was corroborated by physical evidence surrounding the victim. The gunshot wounds showed that he was murdered. The defendant's confession corroborated an accomplice's testimony that the defendant tried to blow up the victim and his car.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the defendant's convictions and sentences.

Rucker v. Comptroller of Treasury


No. 24, September Term, 1987


Court of Appeals of Maryland


315 Md. 559; 555 A.2d 1060; 1989 Md. LEXIS 52



April 6, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Circuit Court for Charles County pursuant to certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED. APPELLANT TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporate president challenged the assessment by appellee, Comptroller of the Treasury (comptroller), which under Md. Ann. Code art. 81, §§ 331, 383 (1957, 1980 Repl. Vol.), assessed the full amount of the corporation's sales and use tax against him as an officer. The president appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Charles County (Maryland), affirming the judgment of the Maryland Tax Court finding the president liable.


OVERVIEW: The president had formed a corporation with two others and assumed the position of president. The president had asserted that he had no involvement in the corporation's financial affairs and that §§ 331 and 383 should be interpreted in a manner which limited personal liability to only those corporate officers who either had the duty to collect and pay the taxes or who had a duty to supervise such payment. The court rejected such argument and affirmed the circuit court's determination that upheld the imposition of the tax assessment against the president. Sections 331 and 383 unambiguously placed the full amount of the sales and use tax on any corporate officer. The court found that when the president accepted one of the statutorily designated offices he became individually responsible for the payment of the corporation's sales and use taxes. Further, the court found that the statutes did not unconstitutionally deprive him of property without due process of law because the president failed to meet his burden of proving lack of a rational basis and that the rational basis for holding officers liable for tax payment, the collection of taxes which may have gone unpaid, was obvious.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court, which held the president liable for the full tax assessment based on the corporation's sales and use tax.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed the judgment of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which denied its motion for reconsideration regarding its reversal of defendant's conviction for robbery with a deadly weapon and related offenses and order for a new trial. Defendant filed a cross-petition for review.


OVERVIEW: The prosecutor used peremptory challenges to excuse the only two black members of the jury panel. An all white jury was empanelled. Defendant was white. The jury convicted defendant of robbery with a deadly weapon and related offenses. Defendant was a habitual offender, so he was sentenced to life in prison. On appeal, the appellate court affirmed. The court declined to review the case. The United States Supreme Court remanded the case for reconsideration in light of its recent decision regarding peremptory challenges. The appellate court reversed and ordered that a new trial be held. The appellate court also denied the State's motion for reconsideration. On appeal, the court reversed the appellate court's reversal of defendant' conviction and the order for a new trial. The court found that defendant had failed to establish a prima facie case of discrimination in his equal protection challenge to the jury venire. Since defendant and the excused jurors were not of the same race, defendant failed to meet the first prong of Batson. Neither could defendant, by was of peremptory challenges, assert a Sixth amendment claim of fair-cross-section deprivation in the composition of his jury.

State v. Burning Tree Club, Inc.


No. 106, September Term, 1987


Court of Appeals of Maryland


315 Md. 254; 554 A.2d 366; 1989 Md. LEXIS 40



March 8, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals, Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County - Judge Martin A. Wolff.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY VACATED, AND CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT FOR THE ISSUANCE OF A DECLARATORY JUDGMENT IN ACCORDANCE WITH THIS OPINION. PLAINTIFFS TO PAY COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee golf club sought declaratory and injunctive relief from appellant state's denial of an exemption from a tax assessment. The Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County (Maryland) entered summary judgment for the club on its claim that Chapter 334 violated the Maryland Equal Rights Amendment (E.R.A.) and that the unconstitutional language was not severable from the overall prohibition of sex discrimination in Chapter 334. The state appealed.


OVERVIEW: In exchange for a favorable tax assessment, the club entered into a 50-year agreement with the state to maintain its land as open spaces. However, due to the club's allegedly discriminatory membership policies, the state assessed the club's lands at their full cash value. The club sought declaratory and injunctive relief. The court denied relief, holding that (1) Chapter 334 was intended to have retroprospective effect; (2) Chapter 334 did not violate the Contract Clause; (3) Chapter 334 was not a special law prohibited by Md. Const. art. III, § 33; and (4) Chapter 334 did not violate the constitutional freedom of association rights of the club's members. Finally, although the periodic discrimination exception in Chapter 334 violated the E.R.A., the court held that the unconstitutional language was severable from the overall prohibition of sex discrimination in Chapter 334. Thus, in sum, the club had no right to a favorable tax assessment under the "open lands" exemption where it continued to discriminate on the basis of sex.


OUTCOME: The court vacated and remanded the lower court's judgment.

 

184 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Paolino v. McCormick & Co.


No. 40, September Term, 1988


Court of Appeals of Maryland


314 Md. 575; 552 A.2d 868; 1989 Md. LEXIS 7



February 3, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Baltimore City), Meyer M. Cardin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS VACATED AND CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO DISMISS THE APPEAL. ALL COSTS IN THIS COURT AND IN THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS TO BE PAID BY McCORMICK.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee appealed the decision of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which had found in favor of respondent employer, concluding that the employee's claim for temporary total disability was time barred.


OVERVIEW: The court issued a writ of certiorari to decide whether an employer that continued to pay wages to a disabled employee who had sustained an accidental injury arising out of and in the course of her employment was making payments of "compensation" for purposes of the statutory provision governing Workmen's Compensation, Md. Code art. 101, § 40(c). The court, however, was unable to reach that question because the employer lacked the ability to appeal the circuit court decision to the Court of Special Appeals. The original administrative decision denied the employee's claim for temporary total disability. On the employee's appeal to the circuit court, the decision was again in the employer's favor. Since the only part of the order that was appealable was wholly favorable to the employer, the employer lacked standing to appeal that judgment to the Court of Special Appeals. Consequently, the court vacated the judgment of the special appeals court and remanded for dismissal of the appeal.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment of the special appeals court and remanded the case with directions to dismiss the appeal.

 

185 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


State Admin. Bd. of Election Laws v. Billhimer


No. 172, September Term, 1987


Court of Appeals of Maryland


314 Md. 46; 548 A.2d 819; 1988 Md. LEXIS 137



October 21, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Denied December 2, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Anne Arundel County), James C. Cawood, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED; CASE REMANDED TO THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS WITH DIRECTIONS TO REMAND THE CASE TO THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY FOR THE ENTRY OF JUDGMENT AFFIRMING THE DECISION OF THE SECRETARY OF PERSONNEL; COSTS TO BE PAID BY THE APPELLEE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state administrative board of election laws (board) sought review of the decision of the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), which affirmed the judgment of the circuit court that reversed the determination by the secretary of personnel that appellee deputy state elections administrator's (administrator) position was an unclassified position.


OVERVIEW: The state administrative board of election laws, Md. Ann. Code art. 33, §1A-1, did not mention whether its employees were classified or unclassified state employees. The administrator was terminated and advised that, under the personnel rules for unclassified employees, his right of appeal was limited to an inquiry into whether he was discharged for illegal or unconstitutional reasons. The administrator challenged his position's classification as unclassified. The court reversed the decision, finding that the arbitrator had correctly stated that the controlling law in this case was contained in Maryland's Merit System, Md. Ann. Code art. 64A, §§ 1 and 3(13). Section 1 defined a classified employee and the administrator did not achieve his position through the competitive process. The court found that the secretary of personnel's decision was supported by substantial evidence that the administrator's position was unclassified based on the exemptions in § 3(13). The court noted that since its inception employees within the administrator's department, with the governor's approval, had always been classified as unclassified.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded to the Court of Special Appeals with directions to remand to the circuit court for entry of a judgment affirming the secretary of personnel's decision that the administrator's position was unclassified.

 

186 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


State v. Colvin


No. 88, September Term, 1986


Court of Appeals of Maryland


314 Md. 1; 548 A.2d 506; 1988 Md. LEXIS 135



October 14, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended October 19, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Circuit Court for Anne Arundel (Post Conviction Proceeding), Martin A. Wolff, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR ANNE ARUNDEL COUNTY AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Anne Arundel (Maryland), which vacated appellee's death sentence and ordered a new capital sentencing hearing, finding that at the original sentencing, the state introduced appellee's adult criminal convictions which were obtained under an unconstitutional procedure. Also, appellee sought review, claiming a new trial was required because of ineffective assistance of counsel.


OVERVIEW: Appellee was sentenced to death following a murder and felony conviction. On post conviction review, the lower court held that at sentencing, the state had introduced criminal convictions obtained under unconstitutional procedures. After a new sentencing hearing was ordered, the state sought review, and appellee sought review, claiming a new trial was required because of ineffective counsel. In affirming, the court rejected the ineffective assistance claim because appellee had not demonstrated a reasonable probability of innocence if counsel had utilized information concerning the possibility of other suspects. Assuming arguendo that the information would have raised reasonable doubt, the court held there had been no prejudice because appellee was nevertheless guilty of first-degree murder under Md. Ann. Code art. 27, §§ 30(b), 410 as appellee had committed murder in the first-degree at least as an accomplice or principal in the second degree. In upholding the decision to vacate the sentence, the court held equal protection had been violated by admission of the convictions because the convictions, obtained under invalid procedures, had been used to demonstrate predicate crimes.


OUTCOME: Court affirmed a judgment vacating appellee's death sentence and ordering a new sentencing hearing because equal protection was violated when the State demonstrated appellee's predicate crimes with convictions obtained under invalid procedures. The court also held a new trial was not required on account of ineffective assistance of counsel because a reasonable probability of innocence had not been demonstrated and prejudice had not been shown.

 

187 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Treece v. State


No. 174, September Term, 1987


Court of Appeals of Maryland


313 Md. 665; 547 A.2d 1054; 1988 Md. LEXIS 132



October 11, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended October 18, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to Court of Special Appeals Circuit Court for Prince George's County, Howard S. Chasanow, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS REVERSED. CASE REMANDED TO THAT COURT WITH DIRECTIONS TO REVERSE THE JUDGMENTS OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR PRINCE GEORGE'S COUNTY AND TO REMAND THE CASE TO THAT COURT FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS NOT INCONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS TO BE PAID BY PRINCE GEORGE'S COUNTY, MARYLAND.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed convictions for second degree rape and false imprisonment from the Court of Special Appeals (Maryland), contending his counsel should not have asserted lack of criminal responsibility under Md. R. Crim. Causes § 4-242.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his convictions for second degree rape and false imprisonment on the basis that defense counsel had interposed a defense of not criminally responsible under Md. R. Crim. Causes § 4-242 against his will. After being found competent to stand trial, defendant announced his disagreement with the plea. There was conflicting testimony at trial whether defendant was suffering from delusions, including being watched by government agencies. The state contended the decision to assert the plea was a tactical trial decision like any other affirmative defense. The court disagreed and held that defendant who was competent was entitled to decide whether the defense of criminal responsibility was to be interposed because its consequences were so grave and personal that competent defendant should have the right to make his own decision whether to impose that plea. A successful plea did not mean freedom. In this case, the plea interfered with defendant's defense of consent. As to whether the defense was entitled to make the concluding argument on criminal responsibility, that was referred to the Standing Committee on Rules of Practice and Procedure.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was reversed and the case remanded to reverse the conviction and for further proceedings in the trial court consistent with defendant's right to decide whether to assert a plea of not criminally responsible.

 

188 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Maryland State Administrative Bd. of Election Laws v. Talbot County


No. 74, September Term, 1988


Court of Appeals of Maryland


316 Md. 332; 558 A.2d 724; 1988 Md. LEXIS 129



October 7, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion June 8, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Circuit Court for Talbot County, J. Owen Wise, Judge



DISPOSITION: AS TO THAT PART OF THE JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR TALBOT COUNTY RELATING TO PAYMENT OF ATTORNEY FEES, EXPENSES AND COSTS IN THE TRIAL COURT: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED. COSTS ON APPEAL TO BE ALLOCATED UNDER MARYLAND RULE 8-607 AS FOLLOWS: MARYLAND STATE ADMINISTRATIVE BOARD OF ELECTION LAWS TO PAY OWN COSTS; COUNTY COUNCIL OF TALBOT COUNTY AND JAMES M. SLAY TO PAY ALL OTHER COSTS AS INCLUDED IN THIS COURT'S MANDATE. MANDATE TO ISSUE FORTHWITH.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, state board and private citizens, appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court for Talbot County (Maryland) that granted a declaratory judgment in favor of plaintiffs, county council and county attorney. The circuit court held that a voter-initiative provision in the county's charter was unconstitutional because it violated Md. Const. art. XI-A. The state board was enjoined from placing the private citizens' initiative on the ballot.


OVERVIEW: The private citizens pursuant to the voter-initiative provision sought to place an initiative on the ballot. The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment. Initially, the court held that there was a justiciable issue under the Maryland Uniform Declaratory Judgments Act, Md. Code Ann., Cts. & Jud. Proc. § 3-409(a), because the county attorney had standing to bring the declaratory judgment action in his personal capacity as a taxpayer, and he alleged sufficient harm by claiming that a vote on the initiative pursuant to an unconstitutional charter provision could waste taxes he paid. Therefore, whether the county council had standing was irrelevant. Furthermore, the local board and private citizens were proper defendants and so an actual controversy existed because even if they had no duty to defend the voter-initiative provision, their exercise of rights under that provision threatened the rights of the county attorney and county council. The court upheld the finding that the voter-initiative provision was unconstitutional because it violated Md. Const. art. XI-A, § 3, which vested the county council with the sole authority to initiate legislation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the declaratory judgment that held the voter-initiative provision in the county charter violated the Maryland Constitution. The court also affirmed the enjoinment of the state board from placing the private citizens' initiative on the ballot. The court also affirmed the denial of the private citizens' claim for attorney's fees, expenses, and costs incurred in the circuit court.

 

189 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Minor v. State


No. 98, September Term, 1986


COURT OF APPEALS OF MARYLAND


313 Md. 573; 546 A.2d 1028; 1988 Md. LEXIS 126



September 13, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended September 28, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Special Appeals (Circuit Court for Prince George's County - Judge Howard S. Chasanow).



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF SPECIAL APPEALS AFFIRMED; APPELLANT TO PAY THE COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was sentenced to 25 years in prison, without the possibility of parole, under Maryland's habitual offender statute, Md. Ann. Code art. 27, § 643B(c) (1957, 1982 Repl. Vol., 1987 Cum. Supp.). Defendant's conviction for daytime housebreaking was his fourth conviction for a crime of violence in 10 years. The Court of Special Appeals (Maryland) affirmed the circuit court's sentence, and the court subsequently granted certiorari.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his 25-year sentence, without the possibility of parole, was cruel and unusual punishment. Defendant reasoned that the Maryland Legislature erred in classifying housebreaking as a violent crime for purposes of § 643(B)(c) and that his sentence was, therefore, disproportionate. The court affirmed. The court, after noting that proportionality challenges typically failed, held that substantial deference was due the legislature and sentencing courts in challenges to the propriety of sentences. An extended proportionality analysis was not required given the seriousness of the daytime crime, the stringent dictates of § 643(B)(c), and the deference due to the legislative sentencing scheme. In particular, defendant's past and present criminal conduct made clear that his sentence was within constitutional limits. Even if a proportionality analysis had been required, the sentence would have been valid because daytime housebreaking was a serious offense with a potential for violence, and the sentence was proportionate to sentences imposed for other crimes in Maryland as well as other jurisdictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's sentence under Maryland's habitual offender statute.

 

190 of 1543 DOCUMENTS


Golden Sands Club Condominium, Inc. v. Waller


No. 167, September Term, 1987


Court of Appeals of Maryland


313 Md. 484; 545 A.2d 1332; 1988 Md. LEXIS 119



August 29, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended September 8, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Worcester County pursuant to certiorari to Court of Special Appeals, Dale R. Cathell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT FOR WORCESTER COUNTY REVERSED. CASE REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS NOT INCONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. COSTS TO BE PAID BY APPELLEE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Worcester County (Maryland) found notice provisions of the Maryland Contract Lien Act, Md. Code Ann., Real Prop. § 14-203, unconstitutional in an action brought by appellee owner against appellant condominium development.


OVERVIEW: When the owner failed to pay assessments as assessed by the development, the development provided written notice to the owner as required under § 14-203 of its intention to create a lien against the owner's condominium. The owner then brought the current and claimed, among other things, that the statutory lien provisions were unconstitutional. On appeal from the trial court's ruling striking § 14-203 as unconstitutional, the court recognized that the owner was entitled under § 14-203 to obtain a hearing by filing an action in circuit court against the lien claimant. Assuming that was done, no lien could have been imposed prior to holding a hearing. This opportunity for hearing was found sufficient, and § 14-203 was deemed constitutional despite the fact that the owner was required to file suit in order to obtain the hearing. Because the action required was not complex and because the burden of proof and burden of pressing forward with the lien proceedings were on the person attempting to assert the lien, § 14-203 was found to satisfy all constitutional procedural due process requirements.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court ruling and remanded the action for further proceedings.
